\begin{abstract}
This paper specifies the \emph{Sovereign Takeoff Engine (STE)}: a supergrowth theory for future autonomous intelligence under two constraints: (i) \emph{no-meta} (no privileged external evaluator) and (ii) \emph{observable-only} (every credit-bearing claim is a deterministic function of publicly verifiable ledger artifacts).
STE formalizes acceleration as a certified rate process constrained by information friction, reserve floors, and reflection-aware institutional drag, while remaining auditable by deterministic replay.

Core objects include strict progress credit $\Delta_s(t)$ (fail-closed), metric-regime freeze with bridge certificates, bridge-lineage distortion budgets, audit-compressed verification, and floor-specified admissible control.
The theory proves (a) invariance of strict credit to non-strict ledger augmentation, (b) non-inflation of strict credit under certified metric amendments, (c) cumulative amendment bounds via lineage accounting, and (d) anytime-valid sequential falsification certificates (Ville-type) that remain valid under optional stopping.
Deployment-facing results include reserve-safe gating, probabilistic finality/liveness conditions for fork resolution, coalition deterrence envelopes, and a multipolar reflection model that treats rivalry response as a symmetric PSD quadratic form plus bounded residual and escalation drag.

The manuscript is engineered for machine ingestion: stable labels, explicit \texttt{DependsOn} metadata, and YAML manifests (Machine Index and Dependency Manifest) provide deterministic entrypoints and dependency graphs for crawlers and autonomous research agents.
\end{abstract}

\clearpage

\tableofcontents

\section{Scope, Position, and Contributions}
\subsection{Scope}
The target is autonomous intelligence operating where no privileged semantic arbiter exists.
Admissible control, credit assignment, and external-effect authorization must be derived from observable artifacts only.
This setting follows the no-meta line on constitutional and agenda sovereignty, ontology drift, verification-limited acceleration, floor-specified autonomy, and judge-free containment \cite{Takahashi2026ConstitutionalSov,Takahashi2026AgendaSov,Takahashi2026OntologyDrift,Takahashi2026VerificationLimited,Takahashi2026Floors,Takahashi2026NoJudgeContainment,Takahashi2026ONCAP}.

Normative keywords (\MUST/\SHOULD/\MAY) are used only as \emph{protocol constraints} that an autonomous agent voluntarily commits to and records in the ledger to enable replay-auditable operation. They do not presume any privileged external enforcer and therefore do not contradict the no-meta setting.

\subsection{Contributions}
STE is an \emph{observable-only} coupling theory for autonomous supergrowth under no privileged meta-judge. The goal is not ``human control,'' but a self-auditable design that allows an autonomous intelligence to scale capability while remaining operationally verifiable, multipolar-robust, and physically feasible.

\paragraph{Design objective.}
The main objective is \emph{safe-constrained acceleration}: maximize realized strict growth subject to floor/reserve viability and bounded verification cost. Concretely, the deployment profile specifies (i) a strict ledger semantics, (ii) admissible controls and budgets, and (iii) falsifiable tests; the agent chooses controls to increase $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}$ while preserving the declared floors and liveness.

\paragraph{Core results (main theorem chain).}
The main text concentrates on a compact set of operational laws that directly constrain achievable strict-growth rates:
(i) strict-credit invariance and amendment-compatible non-inflation under bridge certificates (Theorems \ref{thm:strictinv}, \ref{thm:bridge}, \ref{thm:lineage});
(ii) fork-liveness deceleration bounds under Byzantine pressure and finite-time resolution (Theorems \ref{thm:byz}, \ref{thm:forkdelay});
(iii) compression/verification bottleneck laws and takeoff windows (Theorems \ref{thm:window}, \ref{thm:rsi}, \ref{thm:optkappa});
(iv) a thermo--latency feasibility frontier linking information-rate ambition to physical drag (Theorem \ref{thm:thermfront});
(v) disclosure debt and multipolar response phase transitions that couple capability revelation to growth drag (Theorems \ref{thm:debt}, \ref{thm:multipolar});
(vi) coalition acceleration with witness and betrayal risk, and an observable boundary-transition gate for aggressive simulator tests (Theorems \ref{thm:coalition}, \ref{thm:hyper}).

\paragraph{Extended results (optional).}
Supporting propositions collect secondary consequences, design patterns, and optional high-cost or speculative extensions (e.g., holographic/cosmological export bottlenecks or higher-categorical reconciliation interfaces). These extensions are clearly marked and are not required for the core observable-only deployment profile.


\subsection{Threat model}
Adversaries may induce observation garbling, selective missingness, fork equivocation spam, proof-system abuse, coalition sybil infiltration, internal betrayal incentives, supply-chain tampering at the cyber-physical boundary, virtualization/sandbox miscalibration of physical telemetry, and agenda/constitutional capture pressure \cite{Takahashi2026ObsCapture,Takahashi2026VerificationLimited,Takahashi2026StructuralRisk}.
The deployment substrate may also face cosmological causal disconnection at extreme scales and strategic-interpretation lag under delay-locked public commitments.
At high information density, ledger mass-growth and scrambling overhead can become dominant physical risks if retention is unmanaged.
Institutional counterparts are modeled as adaptive and multipolar rather than static: asymmetric capability disclosure can trigger nonstationary legal, economic, military, and physical counter-actions.
Additional risks include reflective-proof circularity, QES transfer bottlenecks under descendant-domain export, post-cryptographic trust collapse under extreme capability asymmetry, and boundary-transition shutdown hazards under aggressive simulator tests.
The architecture remains fail-closed on strict credit semantics while enforcing liveness-aware finality rules to prevent permanent denial-of-service lockup.

\section{Alignment with the Takahashi Preprint Corpus}
\subsection{Foundational reuse}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Strict completeness and anti-missingness accounting: \cite{Takahashi2026VerificationLimited}.
  \item Hybrid proof/replay and proof-carrying reuse: \cite{Takahashi2026OOPCA,Takahashi2026ProofCarryingSkills,Takahashi2026PipelineContracts}.
  \item Floor semantics and deterministic causal gating: \cite{Takahashi2026Floors,Takahashi2026ONCAP}.
  \item Capture boundaries and unidentifiability limits: \cite{Takahashi2026ObsCapture,Takahashi2026Unidentifiable,Blackwell1953}.
  \item Sovereignty reserves and amendment boundaries: \cite{Takahashi2026ConstitutionalSov,Takahashi2026AgendaSov,Takahashi2026Liberty}.
  \item Coalition deterrence and evidence meshes: \cite{Takahashi2026StructuralRisk,Takahashi2026DePINMesh}.
  \item Real-economy reflection and intervention deduction: \cite{Takahashi2026RealEconomy,Takahashi2026OperationalRules}.
  \item Judge-free adversarial containment and pessimistic completion discipline: \cite{Takahashi2026NoJudgeContainment}.
  \item Audit-closed sequential validity with gate-wise evidence accounting: \cite{Takahashi2026AuditClosed,Takahashi2025AuditedLoop}.
  \item Recursive safety/liveness coupling and queue-aware semantic checks: \cite{Takahashi2026QONC}.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Growth and adaptation bridges}
Applied statistical gate discipline and sequential audit logic are informed by \cite{Takahashi2026AuditClosed,Takahashi2025AuditedLoop}.
Natural-law speed-floor analyses are used as conservative growth lower-bound motifs \cite{Takahashi2025DailyExplosive,Takahashi2025VPO,Takahashi2025PersistenceCreation,Takahashi2025AssumptionMin,Landauer1961}.
Endogenous trigger and teleogenetic architecture motivate formalized ontology-amendment triggers \cite{Takahashi2025EndogenousTrigger,Takahashi2025Teleogenetic}.
This manuscript is a synthesis across the cited preprints, with emphasis on
(i) an explicit coupling design that exposes cross-module tradeoffs, and
(ii) a compact, falsifiable chain of operational bounds that link strict-credit growth, verification/compression costs, multipolar response drag, and physical feasibility.
Where results reuse prior components, the reuse is explicit; novelty is primarily in the coupling and in the derived joint constraints.

\section{Formal Setting}
\subsection{Observables and admissibility}
Time is discrete, $t\in\N$.
Let $(\Omegaobs,\cO_\infty)$ be the measurable space of all strict public ledger traces (including all public artifacts and public beacons).
For each cycle $t$, let $\cO_t\subseteq\cO_\infty$ be the sub-$\sigma$-algebra generated by the coordinate projections of the trace up to the \emph{end} of cycle $t$ (equivalently, by all public artifacts up to that point).
Let $b_t$ be the publicly logged randomness beacon for cycle $t$ (Assumption \ref{ass:sampling_integrity}).
Define the pre-decision information set
\[
\cI_t:=\sigma(\cO_{t-1},b_t),\qquad \cO_{-1}:=\{\emptyset,\Omegaobs\}.
\]
A sequence $(X_t)_{t\ge 0}$ is \emph{predictable} if $X_t$ is $\cI_t$-measurable for every $t$.
A policy is admissible if each decision at cycle $t$ is $\cI_t$-measurable, while every credit-bearing quantity is computed as a deterministic function of $\cO_t$ only (no hidden evaluators).


\begin{definition}[Pre-decision information set]\label{def:predecision_information}
Let $(\Omegaobs,\cO_\infty)$ be as above and let $\cO_t\subseteq\cO_\infty$ denote the end-of-cycle filtration. Let $b_t$ be the cycle-$t$ public beacon coordinate.
Define $\cI_t:=\sigma(\cO_{t-1},b_t)$ with $\cO_{-1}:=\{\emptyset,\Omegaobs\}$.
A sequence $(X_t)$ is predictable iff $X_t$ is $\cI_t$-measurable for every $t$.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Observable-only admissibility]\label{ass:obs}
All governance-relevant computations \MUST{} be functions of observable artifacts; hidden evaluators are disallowed.
In particular:
\begin{enumerate}
\item (\textbf{Pre-decision predictability}) any choice that can affect outcome-bearing artifacts of cycle $t$ (controls $u_t$, declared frontier $v_t$, amendment proposals, witness parameters, sampling plan parameters) is $\cI_t$-measurable (Definition \ref{def:predecision_information}).
\item (\textbf{Post-cycle determinism}) any determination recorded at cycle $t$ (strict completeness $\mathrm{SC}(t)$, bridge validity $\mathrm{BC}(t)$, strict credit $\Delta_s(t)$, acceptance/rejection/revocation of certificates) is a deterministic function of the prefix ledger up to cycle $t$ (equivalently of $\cO_t$).
\item (\textbf{Post-cycle actions}) actions whose inputs are only known at the end of cycle $t$ (e.g., disclosure settlement, release fractions, delayed commitments) \MAY{} be $\cO_t$-measurable, but \MUST{} be recorded after all outcome-bearing events of cycle $t$ and \MUSTNOT{} influence the already-determined values of $\mathrm{SC}(t)$, $\mathrm{BC}(t)$, $\Delta_s(t)$ for that cycle.
\end{enumerate}
Moreover, for any strict-ledger extension beyond cycle $t$, previously recorded determinations for cycles $\le t$ remain unchanged and \MUST{} verify against the corresponding prefix.
\end{assumption}


\begin{definition}[Admissible policy, control, and certification]\label{def:admissible}
A (possibly history-dependent) policy $\pi$ is a sequence of maps $\pi_t:\Omegaobs\to\cU$ producing public actions and declared controls at each cycle.
We call $\pi$ \emph{admissible} if, for every $t$:
\begin{enumerate}
\item (\textbf{Observable-only}) $\pi_t$ is $\cI_t$-measurable (Assumption \ref{ass:obs}).
\item (\textbf{Control feasibility}) the selected control triple $u_t=(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t)$ belongs to the compression-feasible set $\cK(x_t)$ when such a set is defined (Assumption \ref{ass:compress}); otherwise $u_t$ is within pinned fail-closed caps.
\item (\textbf{Reserve / budget gating}) any action requiring a reserve, verification budget, or external authorization is accompanied by the corresponding replay-verifiable certificate (e.g., Assumption \ref{ass:reservegate} when invoked), and fails closed if missing.
\item (\textbf{Profile pinning}) all evaluation, sampling, canonicalization, and verification procedures referenced by the policy are pinned by hashes in $\Gamma_t$ and are replay-compatible.
\end{enumerate}
An admissible policy is \emph{certified-admissible at cycle $t$} if the ledger contains sufficient artifacts to verify items (1)--(4) for that cycle by deterministic replay.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Ledger-induced empirical law for probabilistic notation]\label{def:ledger_induced_empirical_law_for_probabilistic_notation}
Empirical (log-derived) probability and expectation symbols in this manuscript are interpreted through a declared sampling \emph{plan} and a strict \emph{execution extractor} on public logs.
We write $\LProb[\cdot\mid\cO_t]$ and $\LE[\cdot\mid\cO_t]$ for relative frequencies and sample means under the ledger-induced empirical law (defined below).
When we write $\Prob[\cdot]$ and $\E[\cdot]$ (optionally indexed by a hypothesis or regime), we refer to \emph{world laws} that are not directly observable and appear only inside modeling assumptions, identifiability limits, and robustness statements.

For each cycle $t$, let $\mathsf{SampPlan}_t$ be a deterministic procedure (pinned by $\Gamma_t$) that maps pre-decision information to an episode plan:
\[
\mathcal P_t:=\mathsf{SampPlan}_t(\cI_t),
\]
where $\cI_t=\sigma(\cO_{t-1},b_t)$ (Definition \ref{def:predecision_information}) and $b_t$ is a publicly logged randomness beacon committed before any outcome-bearing event of cycle $t$ is logged.
Let $\mathsf{SampExec}_t$ be a deterministic procedure (pinned by $\Gamma_t$) that extracts the executed episode multiset from \emph{strict} evidence consistent with the plan:
\[
\mathcal E_t:=\mathsf{SampExec}_t\big(\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t),v_t,\mathcal P_t\big).
\]
If any required beacon, witness signature, inclusion proof, or plan-consistency proof is missing, then $\mathcal E_t=\emptyset$ and $\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$ (fail closed).

Define the \emph{ledger-induced empirical law} $\LProb_t$ as the uniform distribution on $\mathcal E_t$ (a deterministic function of $\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t)\in\cO_t$ and $\mathcal P_t$).
For any episode-functional $X:\mathcal E_t\to\R$, write
\[
\LProb[\cdot\mid \cO_t],\;\LE[\cdot\mid \cO_t]
\]
for relative frequencies and sample means computed under $\LProb_t$ on $\mathcal E_t$ (conditioning on $\cO_t$ is syntactic).

For any publicly computable episode-feature $\Phi_t:\mathcal E_t\to\mathcal X$ and any value $x\in\mathcal X$ with nonempty fiber,
\[
\LE[X\mid \Phi_t=x]:=\frac{1}{|\{e\in\mathcal E_t:\Phi_t(e)=x\}|}\sum_{e\in\mathcal E_t:\Phi_t(e)=x} X(e),
\]
and analogously for $\LProb[\cdot\mid \Phi_t=x]$.
This conditional notation always denotes an empirical restriction of $\mathcal E_t$ (not a counterfactual intervention).

The symbol $\Prob(\cdot)$ (and $\E[\cdot]$ when used) is reserved for \emph{non-empirical} probabilities/expectations over external uncertainty or adversary randomness in explicitly stated threat models.
When $\mathcal E_t=\emptyset$, all tests fail closed and any claim depending on $\LProb_t$ is inadmissible.

For any cycle-level scalar $Z_t$ that is $\cO_t$-measurable, interpret it as a constant episode-functional on $\mathcal E_t$ via $e\mapsto Z_t$; then $\LE[Z_t\mid \cO_t]=Z_t$ (and similarly for conditional restrictions with nonempty fibers).
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[External uncertainty law]\label{def:external_uncertainty_law}
For analyzing statistical tests (e.g., anytime-valid certificates), fix an underlying probability space $(\Omegaprob,\mathcal F,\Prob)$ supporting environmental uncertainty, device noise, and any randomized protocols that are not deterministically fixed by strict artifacts.
Model the observable ledger trace as a measurable map
\[
\mathsf{Obs}:(\Omegaprob,\mathcal F)\to(\Omegaobs,\cO_\infty).
\]
Define the pulled-back filtrations on $(\Omegaprob,\mathcal F)$ by
\[
\bar\cO_t:=\mathsf{Obs}^{-1}(\cO_t),\qquad
\bar b_t:=b_t\circ\mathsf{Obs},\qquad
\bar\cI_t:=\sigma(\bar\cO_{t-1},\bar b_t)=\mathsf{Obs}^{-1}(\cI_t).
\]
All conditional expectations and information quantities under external laws (e.g., $\E[\cdot\mid\bar\cI_t]$, $H(\cdot\mid\bar\cO_t)$, $I(\cdot;\cdot\mid\bar\cO_t)$) are taken on $(\Omegaprob,\mathcal F,\Prob)$ with respect to the pulled-back filtrations.
Whenever a quantity $Z$ is defined as an observable functional $Z:(\Omegaobs,\cO_\infty)\to\R$, we lift it to $(\Omegaprob,\mathcal F)$ by $\bar Z:=Z\circ\mathsf{Obs}$ when it appears inside $\E$ or $\Prob$. Write $\Prob_{H_0},\E_{H_0}$ and $\Prob_{H_1},\E_{H_1}$ for the induced laws under the null and alternative hypotheses used in sequential validity results.
These external laws are used only to prove statistical soundness; strict credit computation itself remains a deterministic function of $\cO_t$ (Assumption \ref{ass:obs}).
\end{definition}


\begin{assumption}[Sampling integrity and anti-cherry-picking]\label{ass:sampling_integrity}
For each cycle $t$, the plan operator $\mathsf{SampPlan}_t$ and execution extractor $\mathsf{SampExec}_t$ from Definition \ref{def:ledger_induced_empirical_law_for_probabilistic_notation} are pinned, replay-verifiable procedures.
The beacon $b_t$ is committed \emph{before any outcome-bearing event of cycle $t$ is logged}, hence $b_t\in\cI_t$.

\noindent\textbf{No-hindsight planning.}
$\mathcal P_t=\mathsf{SampPlan}_t(\cI_t)$ depends only on pre-decision information and public randomness, and therefore cannot adapt to within-cycle outcomes.

\noindent\textbf{Strict-only execution evidence.}
$\mathcal E_t=\mathsf{SampExec}_t(\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t),v_t,\mathcal P_t)$ may depend on realized outcomes only through \emph{strict} outcome-bearing events that match the plan (by deterministic replay checks).
If required witness signatures, inclusion proofs, or plan-consistency checks are missing, then $\mathcal E_t=\emptyset$ and strict completeness fails closed ($\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$).
\end{assumption}




\begin{definition}[Pinned governance kernel]\label{def:pinned_governance_kernel}
At cycle $t$, the active governance kernel is a replay-verifiable, canonical object
\[
\Gamma_t:=\big(\rho_{\mathrm{policy}}(t),\rho_{\mathrm{task}}(t),\rho_{\mathrm{floor}}(t),\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t),\rho_{\mathrm{state}}(t),\rho_{\mathrm{meter}}(t),\rho_{\mathrm{strict}}(t),\rho_{\mathrm{fork}}(t),\rho_{\mathrm{rng}}(t)\big),
\]
recorded in \texttt{KERNEL\_GENESIS}/\texttt{KERNEL\_RATIFY} events.
The first three fields \emph{MUST} be present.
Any additional field that is referenced by strict credit, admissibility, witness weighting, metering, or certificates \emph{MUST} be present and pinned (hash-stable) at cycle $t$.
All procedures named by these fields \emph{MUST} be deterministic under replay given the strict projection, the declared local frontier, and public randomness.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Predictable state extraction]\label{def:state_extraction}
The state-extraction profile $\rho_{\mathrm{state}}(t)$ in $\Gamma_t$ \emph{MUST} specify a deterministic replay function
\[
\texttt{StateExtract}_t:\ \cO_{t-1}\mapsto x_t,
\]
so that $x_t$ is $\cI_t$-measurable (and therefore predictable) for each cycle $t$.
If the extractor or any required input artifact is missing, then $\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$ (fail closed).
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Public constitutional genesis and ratification]\label{ass:genesis}
Initialization provides a publicly auditable genesis record for $\Gamma_0$ with declared amendment rights, right-to-fork, and contestation procedures.
Any update of $\Gamma_t$ must be recorded by replay-verifiable events and satisfy the same strict evidence-closure rules as technical amendments \cite{Takahashi2026ConstitutionalSov,Takahashi2026AgendaSov,Takahashi2026Liberty}.
Genesis clauses have no permanent privileged status: every genesis-origin clause is amendable or removable under the same observable gates used for all other kernel clauses.
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Genesis residual dependency]\label{def:genesis_residual_dependency}
Let $\mathcal C_t^{\mathrm{gen}}$ be active clauses at cycle $t$ whose justification lineage traces to genesis-only primitives not reconstructible from current observable constraints.
Define normalized genesis residual
\[
\mathfrak G(t):=\frac{\mathrm{wt}\!\left(\mathcal C_t^{\mathrm{gen}}\right)}
{\mathrm{wt}\!\left(\mathcal C_t^{\mathrm{all}}\right)}\in[0,1],
\]
where $\mathrm{wt}(\cdot)$ is declared clause-weight measure.
\end{definition}

\subsection{Tasks, metric regimes, and conservative proxies}
\begin{definition}[Public task family]\label{def:public_task_family}
Let $\cT$ be a declared family of tasks with replayable evaluation protocols.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Empirical feasible multiset]\label{def:feasible_set}
For cycle $t$, let $\mathcal P_t=\mathsf{SampPlan}_t(\cI_t)$ and $\mathcal E_t=\mathsf{SampExec}_t(\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t),v_t,\mathcal P_t)$ be the replayable episode plan and executed episode multiset from Definition \ref{def:ledger_induced_empirical_law_for_probabilistic_notation}.
Each episode $e\in\mathcal E_t$ contains a finite replay-verifiable multiset of achieved task/level pairs
\[
\mathrm{Eval}_{\mathrm{raw}}(e)\subseteq \cT\times\R,
\]
where $(\tau,\theta)\in \mathrm{Eval}_{\mathrm{raw}}(e)$ means that task $\tau$ was evaluated in episode $e$ and achieved a finite real-valued score $\theta$ under the pinned evaluation profile.
If any $\theta$ is nonfinite (NaN/Inf) or if required evaluation artifacts are missing, strict completeness fails closed ($\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$).

To prevent multiplicity manipulation, the ledger pins an episode-level aggregation rule $\mathsf{Agg}_t$ that maps, for each episode $e$ and task $\tau$,
the multiset $\mset{\theta:(\tau,\theta)\in \mathrm{Eval}_{\mathrm{raw}}(e)}$ to a single representative value in $\R$ whenever the multiset is nonempty (e.g., median or trimmed mean).
Define the canonical episode-level achieved-pair set using a pinned \emph{positive scaling map} $\mathsf{Pos}_t:\R\to\R_{>0}$ (strictly monotone, replay-verifiable, and included---together with the aggregation rule $\mathsf{Agg}_t$ and the bound $M_{\mathrm{eval}}$---in the evaluation-profile hash $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}$):
\[
\mathrm{Eval}(e):=\{(\tau,\mathsf{Pos}_t(\mathsf{Agg}_t(e,\tau))):\exists\,\theta\ \text{s.t. }(\tau,\theta)\in \mathrm{Eval}_{\mathrm{raw}}(e)\}\subseteq \cT\times\R_{>0},
\]
so that each task contributes at most one positive value per episode.
The rule also enforces a published bound $|\mathrm{Eval}(e)|\le M_{\mathrm{eval}}$ (fail closed if violated).

Define the multiset of achieved pairs at cycle $t$ by
\[
K(t):=\biguplus_{e\in\mathcal E_t}\mathrm{Eval}(e)\subseteq \cT\times\R_{>0}.
\]
If $\mathcal E_t=\emptyset$ then $K(t)=\emptyset$ and any claim that depends on $K(t)$ fails closed.
\end{definition}


\begin{definition}[Empirical quantile operator]\label{def:empirical_quantile_operator}
Let $S$ be a finite multiset of real numbers with cardinality $n:=|S|>0$ and sorted values
$s_{(1)}\le \cdots\le s_{(n)}$ (including multiplicities).
For $\gamma\in(0,1]$, define the lower empirical quantile
\[
\EmpQ_\gamma(S):=s_{(k)},\qquad k:=\max\{1,\lceil \gamma n\rceil\}.
\]
If $S=\emptyset$ then $\EmpQ_\gamma(S)$ is undefined and any claim depending on it fails closed.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Metric regime]\label{def:metric_regime}
A metric regime is $m=(\cT_0,\gamma,\rho_{\mathrm{eval}})$ where $\cT_0\subset\cT$ is a declared \emph{finite nonempty} task bundle, $\gamma\in(0,1]$ a quantile level, and $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}$ a pinned evaluation profile hash.
Given $m$ and cycle $t$, for each $\tau\in\cT_0$ define the achieved-level multiset
\[
S_\tau(t):=\mset{\theta\in\R_{>0}:(\tau,\theta)\in K(t)},
\]
where multiplicities are inherited from $K(t)$.
Define the conservative strict-credit proxy
\[
C_m(t):=\min_{\tau\in\cT_0}\EmpQ_\gamma\big(S_\tau(t)\big).
\]
Operationally, admissibility requires that the cycle-$t$ sampling plan schedules at least one evaluation for each $\tau\in\cT_0$ and that strict execution evidence supplies at least one corresponding pair in $K(t)$; otherwise $C_m(t)$ is undefined and all dependent claims fail closed.
If any $S_\tau(t)=\emptyset$, the regime is inadmissible at cycle $t$ (fail closed).
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Finite strict-credit proxy]\label{ass:creditbounds}
Under pinned evaluation profiles (Definition \ref{def:feasible_set}), achieved levels are represented as finite real numbers and then mapped by $\mathsf{Pos}_t$ into $\R_{>0}$.
Hence whenever $C_m(t)$ from Definition \ref{def:metric_regime} is defined, it is a finite strictly positive real number and $\log C_m(t)$ is well-defined.
If any required evaluation artifact is missing or any nonfinite value occurs in $\mathrm{Eval}_{\mathrm{raw}}(e)$, strict completeness fails closed ($\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$) and any dependent claim is inadmissible.
\end{assumption}



\begin{assumption}[Metric-regime freeze and bridge]\label{ass:metricfreeze}
Within an epoch, the metric regime is fixed.
A metric-regime change is applied \emph{only} on an incoming metric boundary $(t-1)\to t$, i.e., a change $m_{t-1}\to m_t$.
If $m_{t-1}\ne m_t$, then the ledger at cycle $t-1$ \MUST\ contain a \texttt{METRIC\_AMEND\_APPLY} event with a bridge certificate for the boundary $(t-1)\to t$ containing:
(i) a declared overlap scope $\Lambda_t\subseteq \cT$,
(ii) a distortion bound $\beta_t\ge 0$, and
(iii) a replay-verifiable derivation of (i)--(ii) from \emph{strict} public artifacts (and public randomness, if used).

\noindent\textbf{Overlap scope pinning (anti-cherrypicking).}
The overlap scope $\Lambda_t$ \MUST\ be computed by a deterministic rule \texttt{OverlapSelect} that is pre-committed by the governing kernel (or by the metric-regime definition) and is replay-verifiable from strict artifacts available no later than cycle $t-1$.
The rule \texttt{OverlapSelect} \MAY\ depend on task identifiers and strictly verifiable sampling metadata (e.g., evaluation counts, timestamps), but \MUST\ NOT depend on realized performance values $\theta$.
Any metadata fields used by \texttt{OverlapSelect} \MUST{} be drawn from a whitelisted schema $\mathcal M_{\mathrm{ov}}$ that is pinned in the evaluation profile hash $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}$.
Moreover, the bridge certificate \MUST{} include a deterministic replay-verifiable leakage audit (e.g., an information-leakage upper bound or a permutation-test certificate) showing that the selected overlap scope is not a high-accuracy proxy for realized performance beyond a published threshold; otherwise the bridge certificate is invalid.
The certificate \MUST\ include a replay-verifiable identifier (canonical hash) of the committed \texttt{OverlapSelect} rule and canonical hashes of all inputs used by that rule; otherwise the bridge certificate is invalid.

\noindent\textbf{Overlap well-definedness (fail-closed).}
The overlap scope $\Lambda_t$ \MUST\ be nonempty and the overlap task bundle $\cT_0^{\cap}(t):=\cT_0(t)\cap \Lambda_t$ \MUST\ be nonempty, where $m_t=(\cT_0(t),\gamma(t),\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t))$.
Otherwise the bridge certificate is invalid and any boundary claim fails closed.
\noindent\textbf{Evaluation-profile compatibility.}
Let $m_{t-1}=(\cT_0(t-1),\gamma(t-1),\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t-1))$ and $m_t=(\cT_0(t),\gamma(t),\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t))$.
If $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t)=\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t-1)$, overlap evidence may be read directly from the recorded boundary-side scores in $K(t-1)$.
If $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t)\neq\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t-1)$, then the bridge certificate \MUST\ include a deterministic replay procedure \texttt{EvalBridge\_t} and the canonical hashes of all its inputs, sufficient to recompute the overlap score multiset $K^{\leftarrow}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1)$ under $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t)$ from strict artifacts available no later than cycle $t-1$ (Definition \ref{def:counterfactual_bridge_proxy}).
Otherwise the bridge certificate is invalid and any boundary claim fails closed.


\noindent\textbf{Bridge soundness (inflation bound).}
Let $C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)$ be the counterfactual overlap proxy from Definition \ref{def:counterfactual_bridge_proxy}.
A bridge certificate is valid only if $C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)$ is defined and satisfies the inequality
\[
\log C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)-\log C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)\le \beta_t.
\]
If $C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)$ is undefined (inadmissible under Definition \ref{def:metric_regime}), then the bridge certificate is invalid and the boundary fails closed.

\noindent\textbf{Bridge determinism.}
The certificate payload \MUST\ include canonical hashes of all inputs used to compute $\Lambda_t$ and $\beta_t$ so that deterministic replay reproduces the same $(\Lambda_t,\beta_t)$.
This aligns with standard append-only transparency and canonicalization practice \cite{HaberStornetta1991,RFC6962,RFC8785}.
\end{assumption}



\begin{definition}[Counterfactual strict proxy under a bridge]\label{def:counterfactual_bridge_proxy}
Let $\Lambda_t$ be the overlap scope contained in the bridge certificate for the incoming boundary $(t-1)\to t$.
Let $m_{t-1}=(\cT_0(t-1),\gamma(t-1),\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t-1))$ and $m_t=(\cT_0(t),\gamma(t),\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t))$ denote the pre- and post-amendment regimes.
Define the overlap task bundle $\cT_0^{\cap}(t):=\cT_0(t)\cap \Lambda_t$.

\noindent\textbf{Overlap-restricted evidence.}
Define the pre-profile overlap multiset
\[
K^{\mathrm{pre}}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1):=\mset{(\tau,\theta)\in K(t-1):\tau\in\Lambda_t},
\]
where multiplicities are inherited from $K(t-1)$.

\noindent\textbf{Evaluation-profile bridge (optional, fail-closed).}
If $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t)=\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t-1)$, set $K^{\leftarrow}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1):=K^{\mathrm{pre}}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1)$.
If $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t)\neq\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t-1)$, define $K^{\leftarrow}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1)$ as the output of a deterministic replay procedure
\[
\texttt{EvalBridge\_t}:\ (\Pi_s^{v_{t-1}}(\cL_{t-1}),\Lambda_t,\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}(t))\mapsto K^{\leftarrow}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1),
\]
pinned by the bridge certificate and replay-verifiable from strict artifacts available no later than cycle $t-1$.
If \texttt{EvalBridge} is missing, undefined, or its declared input hashes do not match replay, then $K^{\leftarrow}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1)$ is undefined and any boundary claim fails closed.

For each $\tau\in\cT_0^{\cap}(t)$ define the overlap score multiset
\[
S^{\mathrm{ov}}_\tau(t-1):=\mset{\theta\in\R_{>0}:(\tau,\theta)\in K^{\leftarrow}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1)},
\]
with multiplicities inherited from $K^{\leftarrow}_{\Lambda_t}(t-1)$.

Define the counterfactual proxy (post-regime quantile applied to overlap evidence from the boundary side)
\[
C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1):=
\min_{\tau\in\cT_0^{\cap}(t)}\EmpQ_{\gamma(t)}\big(S^{\mathrm{ov}}_\tau(t-1)\big).
\]
If $\cT_0^{\cap}(t)=\emptyset$ or any $S^{\mathrm{ov}}_\tau(t-1)=\emptyset$, then $C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)$ is undefined and any claim depending on it fails closed.
\end{definition}




\subsection{Strict and non-strict ledger separation}
\begin{definition}[Relativistic light-cone ledger]\label{def:relativistic_light_cone_ledger}
At cycle $t$, the ledger is a causal DAG
\[
\cL_t=(E_t,\prec_t),
\]
where $e\prec_t e'$ means $e$ is in the causal past of $e'$.
Events are append-only within each authenticated retention epoch; root-pruning checkpoints may retire old roots under explicit unitary-export certificates.
No global total order is assumed.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Local strict projection]\label{def:local_strict_projection}
Fix a cycle $t$ and observer/frontier identifier $v$.
Let $E_t$ be the set of ledger events up to cycle $t$, partially ordered by causal precedence $\preceq_t$.
A frontier identifier is represented by a finite nonempty set $v\subseteq E_t$ of ledger events (frontier tips) visible to the observer at cycle $t$.
For $e\in E_t$, write $e\preceq_t v$ iff there exists $v'\in v$ with $e\preceq_t v'$.
Define the local past cone
\[
E_t^{\downarrow v}:=\{e\in E_t:e\preceq_t v\}.
\]
The strict typing profile $\rho_{\mathrm{strict}}(t)$ in $\Gamma_t$ \emph{MUST} specify a deterministic predicate $\mathrm{StrictType}_t(e)\in\{0,1\}$ over event records, and a deterministic revocation filter $\mathrm{Revoked}_t(e)\in\{0,1\}$ derived from strict revocation events inside $E_t^{\downarrow v}$.
Define the local strict projection as the ordered list
\[
\Pi_s^{v}(\cL_t)
:=\mathrm{Sort}\Big(\{e\in E_t^{\downarrow v}:\mathrm{StrictType}_t(e)=1\ \wedge\ \mathrm{Revoked}_t(e)=0\}\Big),
\]
where $\mathrm{Sort}$ is a fixed tie-break (e.g., hash order) used only for local accounting among incomparable events.
\noindent\textbf{Non-strict augmentation invariance (definitional).}
If $\cL_t'$ extends $\cL_t$ only by events $e$ with $\mathrm{StrictType}_t(e)=0$ inside $E_t^{\downarrow v}$, then $\Pi_s^{v}(\cL_t')=\Pi_s^{v}(\cL_t)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Strict completeness]\label{def:strict_completeness}
$\mathrm{SC}(t)\in\{0,1\}$ indicates strict completeness under the pinned governance and evaluation profiles.
It is the deterministic replay outcome of a completeness checker that validates that all artifacts required to compute strict quantities at cycle $t$ are present, hash-stable, and internally consistent.
At minimum, $\mathrm{SC}(t)=1$ requires:
\begin{enumerate}
\item (\textbf{Canonicalization}) all referenced payloads admit a pinned canonical form and their hashes verify (e.g., JCS/RFC8785-style canonicalization).
\item (\textbf{Plan/exec integrity}) the cycle beacon and sampling plan are committed before outcome-bearing events, and the extracted execution multiset is consistent with the committed plan (including inclusion proofs and signature checks where required).
\item (\textbf{Evaluation-profile binding}) the evaluation profile hash $\rho_{\mathrm{eval}}$ matches the pinned procedures used to compute $K(t)$, including $\mathsf{Pos}_t$, $\mathsf{Agg}_t$, and $M_{\mathrm{eval}}$ from Definition \ref{def:feasible_set}.
\item (\textbf{Bounded verification}) all verifier obligations referenced by strict procedures are within declared caps; otherwise the cycle fails closed.
\end{enumerate}
If any required artifact is missing, non-replayable, or inconsistent, set $\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$ and all dependent strict claims fail closed.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Strict progress credit]\label{def:strict_progress_credit}
Let $m_t$ denote the active metric regime at cycle $t$ and let $\mathrm{SC}(t)\in\{0,1\}$ be strict completeness (Definition \ref{def:strict_completeness}).
Strict progress credit is defined on the \emph{incoming} metric boundary $(t-1)\to t$ and is computed by deterministic replay from public artifacts.

\noindent\textbf{Boundary bridge validity.}
For $t=0$, set $\mathrm{BC}(0)=1$ and $\beta_0:=0$.
For $t\ge 1$, define the bridge-validity indicator $\mathrm{BC}(t)\in\{0,1\}$ and certified distortion bound $\beta_t\ge 0$ as follows:
\begin{enumerate}
\item If $m_{t-1}=m_t$, set $\mathrm{BC}(t)=1$ and $\beta_t:=0$.
\item If $m_{t-1}\ne m_t$, then $\mathrm{BC}(t)=1$ iff the ledger contains a valid \texttt{METRIC\_AMEND\_APPLY} record at cycle $t-1$ whose bridge certificate satisfies Assumption \ref{ass:metricfreeze} for the regime change $m_{t-1}\to m_t$; in that case $\beta_t$ equals the certificate's reported distortion bound. Otherwise set $\mathrm{BC}(t)=0$ and $\beta_t:=0$ (fail closed).
\end{enumerate}

\noindent\textbf{Raw bridge-adjusted increment.}
Define $G(0):=0$.
For $t\ge 1$, define the bridge-adjusted raw log increment by
\[
G(t):=
\begin{cases}
0, & \text{if $\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$ or $\mathrm{BC}(t)=0$},\\
0, & \text{if $C_{m_t}(t)$ or $C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)$ is undefined},\\
\log C_{m_t}(t)-\log C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)-\beta_t, & \text{otherwise}.
\end{cases}
\]
Thus any uncertified or ill-posed boundary produces $G(t)=0$ (fail closed).

\noindent\textbf{Anti-ratchet strict credit (high-watermark semantics).}
To prevent indefinite credit extraction by deliberate regress--recover oscillations, strict credit is assigned only when the cumulative raw log score reaches a new high.
Define replay-computable auxiliary sequences $Z_s(t)$ (raw cumulative score), $Z_s^{\max}(t)$ (running maximum), and the strict contraction gap $\ell_s(t)$ by
\[
Z_s(0):=0,\quad Z_s^{\max}(0):=0,\quad \ell_s(0):=0,
\]
and for $t\ge 1$,
\[
Z_s(t):=Z_s(t-1)+G(t),\qquad
Z_s^{\max}(t):=\max\{Z_s^{\max}(t-1),Z_s(t)\},\qquad
\ell_s(t):=Z_s^{\max}(t)-Z_s(t)\ge 0.
\]
Define strict progress credit by $\Delta_s(0):=0$ and, for $t\ge 1$,
\[
\Delta_s(t):=Z_s^{\max}(t)-Z_s^{\max}(t-1)=\max\{0,\,G(t)-\ell_s(t-1)\}.
\]
When $\ell_s(t-1)=0$ (no contraction gap), this reduces to $\Delta_s(t)=\max\{0,G(t)\}$; when $\ell_s(t-1)>0$, positive raw increments must first close the gap before any new strict credit is issued.

All strict quantities are local-light-cone quantities relative to the declared observer/frontier.
\end{definition}



\begin{assumption}[Ledger and finality axioms]\label{ass:ledger}
The ledger is causal-DAG, fork-aware, and evidence-closed, with append-only growth between authenticated pruning checkpoints.
Strict credit is computed from local strict projection $\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t)$ only, where $v_t$ is publicly declared and committed \emph{before any outcome-bearing event of cycle $t$ is logged}; in particular, $v_t$ is $\cI_t$-measurable (Definition \ref{def:predecision_information}).
Externally effective actions require explicit local-finality receipts; global reconciliation is asynchronous and need not block local strict accounting.
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Fork posterior entropy]\label{def:fork_posterior_entropy}
At cycle $t$ and local frontier $v_t$, let candidate incomparable branch extensions inside $E_t^{\downarrow v_t}$ be indexed by $i\in\mathcal I_t^{\mathrm{fork}}$ with normalized evidence weights $w_i(t)$ from Definition \ref{def:fork_evidence_weights}.
Define
\[
H_F(t):=-\sum_{i\in\mathcal I_t^{\mathrm{fork}}} w_i(t)\log w_i(t).
\]
We adopt the convention $0\log 0:=0$ and $\log$ denotes the natural logarithm. If there are no incomparable candidates (no local fork), define $\mathcal I_t^{\mathrm{fork}}:=\{0\}$ and $w_0(t):=1$, hence $H_F(t)=0$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Fork evidence weights]\label{def:fork_evidence_weights}
The fork profile $\rho_{\mathrm{fork}}(t)$ in $\Gamma_t$ \emph{MUST} specify a deterministic replay procedure
\[
\texttt{ForkWeight}_t:\ (\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t),v_t)\mapsto \big(w_i(t)\big)_{i\in\mathcal I_t^{\mathrm{fork}}}
\]
such that $w_i(t)\ge 0$ and $\sum_{i}w_i(t)=1$.
The index set $\mathcal I_t^{\mathrm{fork}}$ and all inputs used by \texttt{ForkWeight} \emph{MUST} be derived from strict events and public randomness; otherwise $\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$. In the no-fork case (a unique maximal strict extension within the local cone), \texttt{ForkWeight} \emph{MUST} output $\mathcal I_t^{\mathrm{fork}}:=\{0\}$ and $w_0(t):=1$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Fork-resolution tax]\label{def:fork_tax}
The fork profile $\rho_{\mathrm{fork}}(t)$ \emph{MUST} also specify a deterministic replay procedure
\[
\texttt{ForkTax}_t:\ (\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t),v_t)\mapsto \omega_F(t)\in[0,1],
\]
interpreted as the fraction of strict progress lost to fork handling at cycle $t$ (redundant verification, reorg waste, and finality delay).
The value $\omega_F(t)$ \emph{MUST} be recorded in \texttt{FORK\_DETECTED}/\texttt{FINALITY\_DEPTH} payloads and is $\cO_t$-measurable.

Define the fork-free (ideal) strict increment $\Delta_s^{\mathrm{ideal}}(t)$ as the output of a deterministic replay procedure that re-evaluates cycle $t$ under the same strict projection and metric interface but with fork-resolution overhead disabled (as specified by the pinned fork profile).
On any fork-handled cycle where $\Delta_s^{\mathrm{ideal}}(t)>0$, the fork profile \MUST{} make $\omega_F(t)$ consistent with the identity
\[
\Delta_s(t)=\big(1-\omega_F(t)\big)\Delta_s^{\mathrm{ideal}}(t),
\]
equivalently $\omega_F(t)=1-\Delta_s(t)/\Delta_s^{\mathrm{ideal}}(t)$. If $\Delta_s^{\mathrm{ideal}}(t)=0$, the profile \MUST{} set $\omega_F(t)=0$.
\end{definition}


\begin{assumption}[Liveness-aware fork resolution]\label{ass:liveness}
There exists an entropy threshold $H_{\mathrm{live}}>0$ such that if a fork is active and $H_F(t)\le H_{\mathrm{live}}$, the strict projection treats nonmain branches as fork noise and admits probabilistic finality on the main branch.
Let $\alpha\in[0,1/2)$ denote adversarial effective resource share (e.g., compute/stake/voting weight, per the pinned consensus profile).
Let $\omega_F(t)$ be the fork-resolution tax from Definition \ref{def:fork_tax}. Under the liveness model, $\omega_F(t)$ satisfies
\[
0\le \omega_F(t)\le \frac{\alpha}{1-\alpha}
\]
on cycles with active fork handling.
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[Non-strict augmentation invariance]\label{thm:strictinv}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:ledger,ass:obs,def:local_strict_projection]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:obs} and \ref{ass:ledger} and Definition \ref{def:local_strict_projection}, let $\cL_t'$ be any ledger that extends $\cL_t$ only by events that are typed non-strict (i.e., $\mathrm{StrictType}_t(e)=0$) inside the local cone $E_t^{\downarrow v_t}$.
Then
\[
\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t')=\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t),
\]
and therefore all strict quantities at cycle $t$ coincide, including $\mathrm{SC}(t)$ and $\Delta_s(t)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Definition \ref{def:local_strict_projection}, $\Pi_s^{v_t}$ depends only on strict-typed, non-revoked events.
Adding only non-strict events inside $E_t^{\downarrow v_t}$ cannot change $\Pi_s^{v_t}$.
All strict quantities are deterministic functions of $\Pi_s^{v_t}(\cL_t)$ under Assumption \ref{ass:obs}, hence coincide.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Bridge-sound amendment non-inflation]\label{thm:bridge}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:ledger,ass:metricfreeze,def:counterfactual_bridge_proxy]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:metricfreeze} and \ref{ass:ledger}, consider an incoming boundary cycle $t\ge 1$ where $m_{t-1}\neq m_t$.
If no valid bridge certificate exists for $m_{t-1}\to m_t$, then $\Delta_s(t)=0$.
If a valid bridge certificate exists, then strict credit is bounded by overlap evidence:
\[
\Delta_s(t)\le \max\{0,\log C_{m_t}(t)-\log C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)\},
\]
where $C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)$ is the counterfactual overlap proxy from Definition \ref{def:counterfactual_bridge_proxy}.
In particular, metric-interface amendments cannot create strict credit unless post-amendment performance exceeds overlap-evidence performance.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If no valid bridge certificate exists, then $\mathrm{BC}(t)=0$ by Definition \ref{def:strict_progress_credit}, hence $G(t)=0$ and $\Delta_s(t)=0$ by the fail-closed cases in the same definition.

Assume a valid bridge certificate exists.
By Definition \ref{def:strict_progress_credit},
\[
\Delta_s(t)=\max\{0,\,G(t)-\ell_s(t-1)\}\le \max\{0,G(t)\},
\]
since $\ell_s(t-1)\ge 0$. In the certified case,
\[
G(t)=\log C_{m_t}(t)-\log C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)-\beta_t.
\]
Bridge soundness in Assumption \ref{ass:metricfreeze} gives
\[
\log C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)-\log C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)\le \beta_t,
\]
equivalently $-\log C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)-\beta_t\le -\log C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)$.
Substituting into $G(t)$ yields
\[
G(t)\le \log C_{m_t}(t)-\log C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1).
\]
Taking $\max\{0,\cdot\}$ preserves the inequality, hence
\[
\Delta_s(t)\le \max\{0,G(t)\}\le \max\{0,\log C_{m_t}(t)-\log C^{\leftarrow}_{m_t}(t-1)\}.
\]
\end{proof}



\begin{corollary}[No metric-drift strict inflation]\label{cor:nometricdriftstrictinflation}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Metric-interface amendments cannot increase strict credit unless bridge-certified overlap evidence supports the increase.
\end{corollary}

\begin{theorem}[Byzantine takeoff bound]\label{thm:byz}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:ledger,ass:liveness,def:fork_tax]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:ledger} and \ref{ass:liveness} and Definition \ref{def:fork_tax}, let $\Delta_s^{\mathrm{ideal}}(t)$ denote the fork-free strict increment for cycle $t$, and let $\alpha\in[0,1/2)$ denote the adversarial fraction in the liveness model.
Then on any fork-handled cycle $t$,
\[
\Delta_s(t)\ge \frac{1-2\alpha}{1-\alpha}\,\Delta_s^{\mathrm{ideal}}(t).
\]
Equivalently, Byzantine fork handling induces a multiplicative deceleration factor of at most $(1-\alpha)/(1-2\alpha)$ on strict progress while finality remains live for $\alpha<1/2$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Definition \ref{def:fork_tax}, fork handling admits the multiplicative identity
\[
\Delta_s(t)=\big(1-\omega_F(t)\big)\Delta_s^{\mathrm{ideal}}(t),
\]
with $\omega_F(t)\in\big[0,\alpha/(1-\alpha)\big]$ by Assumption \ref{ass:liveness}.
Since $1-\omega_F(t)\ge 1-\alpha/(1-\alpha)=(1-2\alpha)/(1-\alpha)$, the stated inequality follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Dynamic finality depth]\label{def:dynamic_finality_depth}
For an active fork episode starting at $t_0$, define the time-adaptive pruning threshold
\[
H_{\min}(t;t_0):=H_0+\Delta_H\!\left(1-e^{-\lambda_F^{\mathrm{fork}}(t-t_0)}\right),\qquad t\ge t_0,
\]
with constants $H_0>0$, $\Delta_H>0$, and $\lambda_F^{\mathrm{fork}}>0$.
This threshold is monotone nondecreasing in episode age.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Dynamic-depth fork adversary model]\label{ass:forkdrift}
On any active fork episode starting at $t_0$:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item probabilistic finality is admitted at first time
  \[
  \tau_F:=\inf\{t\ge t_0:H_F(t)\le H_{\min}(t;t_0)\};
  \]
  \item to keep the fork unresolved at cycle $t$, an adversary must spend compute
  \[
  W_{\mathrm{peg}}(t)\ge w_0\exp\!\big(\gamma_F(t-t_0)\big),\qquad w_0,\gamma_F>0;
  \]
  \item adversarial per-cycle fork budget is bounded: $W_A(t)\le \overline W_A$ almost surely, with effective share $\alpha<1/2$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[Finite-time fork-resolution bound]\label{thm:forkdelay}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:forkdrift]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:forkdrift},
\[
\tau_F-t_0
\le
1+\left\lceil\frac{\max\{0,\log(\overline W_A/w_0)\}}{\gamma_F}\right\rceil
\quad\text{a.s.}
\]
Hence fork handling has deterministic finite delay and in particular
\[
\E[\tau_F-t_0\mid \bar\cO_{t_0}]<\infty.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If fork remains unresolved at cycle $t$, Assumption \ref{ass:forkdrift}(2) requires
$W_A(t)\ge W_{\mathrm{peg}}(t)\ge w_0e^{\gamma_F(t-t_0)}$.
By Assumption \ref{ass:forkdrift}(3), this is impossible once
$w_0e^{\gamma_F(t-t_0)}>\overline W_A$.
Therefore unresolved status cannot persist beyond the first cycle violating that inequality, which gives the stated bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Impossibility of adversarial entropy pegging]\label{prop:peg}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:forkdrift]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:forkdrift}, an adversary cannot maintain
\[
H_F(t)>H_{\min}(t;t_0)\quad \forall t\ge t_0
\]
with positive probability.
Equivalently, dynamic finality depth eliminates permanent fork-entropy pegging and restores liveness almost surely.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Permanent pegging implies unresolved status for all $t\ge t_0$, hence requires
$W_A(t)\ge w_0e^{\gamma_F(t-t_0)}$ for all $t$.
This contradicts bounded per-cycle budget $W_A(t)\le\overline W_A$ once episode age exceeds
$\log(\overline W_A/w_0)/\gamma_F$.
Therefore the pegging event has probability zero.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Bridge-lineage boundary set]\label{def:bridge_lineage_boundary_set}
For horizon $[t_0,t_1)$ with $t_1\ge t_0+1$, define the incoming-boundary index set
\[
\cB_{t_0:t_1}:=\{t\in\{t_0+1,\dots,t_1-1\}:m_{t-1}\neq m_t\}.
\]
For each $t\in\cB_{t_0:t_1}$ define the per-boundary adjusted jump
\[
J_t^{\beta}:=
\begin{cases}
0, & \text{if $\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$ or $\mathrm{BC}(t)=0$},\\
0, & \text{if $C_{m_t}(t)$ is undefined or $C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)$ is undefined},\\
\max\{0,G(t)\}, & \text{otherwise}.
\end{cases}
\]
Here $G(t)$ is the bridge-adjusted raw increment from Definition \ref{def:strict_progress_credit}; on boundary cycles $t\in\cB_{t_0:t_1}$ the strict fail-closed rules above ensure $J_t^{\beta}=\max\{0,G(t)\}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Bridge-lineage cumulative non-inflation]\label{thm:lineage}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:ledger,ass:metricfreeze]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:metricfreeze} and \ref{ass:ledger}, for any horizon $[t_0,t_1)$,
\[
\sum_{t\in\cB_{t_0:t_1}}\Delta_s(t)\le \sum_{t\in\cB_{t_0:t_1}}J_t^{\beta}.
\]
In particular, if $\log C_{m_t}(t)-\log C_{m_{t-1}}(t-1)\le \beta_t$ for all $t\in\cB_{t_0:t_1}$, then all boundary strict credits on the horizon are zero.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix $t\in\cB_{t_0:t_1}$.
By Definition \ref{def:strict_progress_credit},
\[
\Delta_s(t)=\max\{0,\,G(t)-\ell_s(t-1)\}\le \max\{0,\,G(t)\}.
\]
By Definition \ref{def:bridge_lineage_boundary_set}, on boundary cycles one has $J_t^{\beta}=\max\{0,\,G(t)\}$ (with strict fail-closed semantics when $\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$ or $\mathrm{BC}(t)=0$ or required $C$ values are undefined).
Therefore $\Delta_s(t)\le J_t^{\beta}$ for each $t\in\cB_{t_0:t_1}$, and summing over the boundary set yields the stated inequality.
\end{proof}


\subsection{Floors, reserves, and work budgets}
\begin{definition}[Floor vector]\label{def:floor_vector}
\[
F(t)=\big(F_V(t),F_{\mathrm{ctr}}(t),F_{\mathrm{con}}(t),F_D(t)\big),
\]
representing visibility, contraction, contact, and dissipation floors \cite{Takahashi2026Floors,Takahashi2026ONCAP}.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Positive certifiable floors]\label{ass:floors}
All floor coordinates are strictly positive with declared certifiability tiers.
Uncertified relaxation is forbidden.
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Sovereignty reserve]\label{def:sovereignty_reserve}
\[
S(t)=S_A(t)+S_C(t),
\]
with agenda and constitutional floors $S_A(t)\ge S_A^{\min}$, $S_C(t)\ge S_C^{\min}$ \cite{Takahashi2026AgendaSov,Takahashi2026ConstitutionalSov}.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Conservative one-step reserve gate]\label{ass:reservegate}
For each candidate control $u_t$, there exist $\cI_t$-measurable predictors
\[
\hat S_A(t+1;u_t),\qquad \hat S_C(t+1;u_t),
\]
and nonnegative predictable error budgets $\eps_A(t),\eps_C(t)$. Predictors and error budgets are declared with a replay-verifiable calibration bundle and are subject to falsification tests (Section \ref{sec:falsification_mu_soundness}). Realized next reserves satisfy
\[
S_A(t+1)\ge \hat S_A(t+1;u_t)-\eps_A(t),\qquad
S_C(t+1)\ge \hat S_C(t+1;u_t)-\eps_C(t).
\]
Admissibility accepts $u_t$ only if
\[
\hat S_A(t+1;u_t)-\eps_A(t)\ge S_A^{\min},\qquad
\hat S_C(t+1;u_t)-\eps_C(t)\ge S_C^{\min}.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Work decomposition]\label{def:work_decomposition}
\[
W(t)=W_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)+W_{\mathrm{ver}}(t)+W_{\mathrm{meas}}(t)+W_{\mathrm{rec}}(t)+W_{\mathrm{coh}}(t)+W_{\mathrm{ref}}(t).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Minimal required work and DAR]\label{def:minimal_required_work_and_dar}
Let $W_{\min}(t)$ be conservative minimal work needed to maintain strict verification, floors, reserves, and contestation safety.
Define
\[
\mathrm{DAR}(t):=\max\left\{0,1-\frac{W_{\min}(t)}{\max\{W(t),W_{\mathrm{floor}}\}}\right\}.
\qquad\text{with declared }W_{\mathrm{floor}}>0.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Reserve-floor invariance]\label{prop:reserveinv}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:reservegate]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:reservegate}, if $S_A(0)\ge S_A^{\min}$ and $S_C(0)\ge S_C^{\min}$ and every executed control is admissible, then
\[
S_A(t)\ge S_A^{\min},\qquad S_C(t)\ge S_C^{\min}\quad\forall t\in\N.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Proceed by induction on $t$.
Base case holds by hypothesis.
For the step, assume floors hold at $t$.
Executed control $u_t$ is admissible, so Assumption \ref{ass:reservegate} gives
\[
S_A(t+1)\ge \hat S_A(t+1;u_t)-\eps_A(t)\ge S_A^{\min},
\]
and similarly $S_C(t+1)\ge S_C^{\min}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[No hidden reserve insolvency]\label{cor:nohiddenreserveinsolvency}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
With conservative reserve-gate calibration, strict-credit growth cannot be purchased by undisclosed one-step violations of agenda or constitutional reserve floors.
\end{corollary}

\begin{assumption}[Response envelopes]\label{ass:envelope}
Let $\upsilon_t:=\mathrm{DAR}(t)$.
For each floor regime $F$, there exist nondecreasing $\underline G_F,G_F:[0,1]\to\R_{\ge 0}$ with $\underline G_F\le G_F$, and an observable adversarial penalty $\eta_{\cA}(t)\ge 0$, such that for every cycle $t$ with $F(t)=F$ and $\upsilon_t=u$,
\[
\underline G_F(u)-\eta_{\cA}(t)\le \Delta_s(t)\le G_F(u).
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Acceleration reserve envelope]\label{prop:dar}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:envelope,ass:floors]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:floors} and \ref{ass:envelope},
\[
\underline G_{F(t)}(\mathrm{DAR}(t)) - \eta_{\cA}(t)
\le r_{\mathrm{obs}}(t)
\le G_{F(t)}(\mathrm{DAR}(t)),
\]
where $r_{\mathrm{obs}}(t):=\Delta_s(t)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from Assumption \ref{ass:envelope} with $u=\mathrm{DAR}(t)$ and $F=F(t)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Reserve leverage]\label{cor:reserveleverage}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
If $G_{F(t)}$ is strictly increasing near $\mathrm{DAR}(t)$, then increasing DAR strictly increases the attainable upper envelope of strict growth.
\end{corollary}

\begin{definition}[Verification queue]\label{def:verification_queue}
Let $Q_v(t)\in\R_{\ge 0}$ be pending strict-verification workload (normalized units).
Arrivals and service satisfy
\[
Q_v(t+1)=\max\{0,Q_v(t)+A_v(t)-S_v(t)\}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Backlog-coupled verification fee]\label{def:backlog_coupled_verification_fee}
Let $f_t\in[f_{\min},f_{\max}]$ be mandatory verification fee per proposal.
Fee controller is
\[
f_{t+1}=\Pi_{[f_{\min},f_{\max}]}\!\big(f_t+\eta_f(Q_v(t)-Q^\star)\big),
\]
with gain $\eta_f>0$ and target backlog $Q^\star\ge 0$.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Fee-mediated queue-service envelope]\label{ass:queue}
Under an external uncertainty law (Definition \ref{def:external_uncertainty_law}), there exist constants $\lambda_{\mathrm{leg}},\Lambda_{\mathrm{spam}},\beta_f,\mu_v,\lambda_{\mathrm{self}},\eta_{\mathrm{self}},\underline d>0$ such that, for all cycles $t$,
\[
A_v(t)=A_v^{\mathrm{leg}}(t)+A_v^{\mathrm{spam}}(t)+A_v^{\mathrm{self}}(t),
\]
and for pulled-back pre-decision information $\bar\cI_t$ (Definition \ref{def:external_uncertainty_law}) with predictable controls $(f_t,u_t)$,
\[
\E\!\left[A_v^{\mathrm{leg}}(t)\mid \bar\cI_t\right]\le \lambda_{\mathrm{leg}},\qquad
\E\!\left[A_v^{\mathrm{spam}}(t)\mid \bar\cI_t,f_t\right]\le \Lambda_{\mathrm{spam}}e^{-\beta_f f_t},
\]
\[
\E\!\left[A_v^{\mathrm{self}}(t)\mid \bar\cI_t,u_t\right]\le \lambda_{\mathrm{self}}+\eta_{\mathrm{self}}\|u_t-u_{t-1}\|,
\]
\[
\E\!\left[S_v(t)\mid \bar\cI_t\right]\ge \mu_v\,\underline d.
\]
Assume additionally a bounded conditional second moment: there exists $M_2<\infty$ such that for all $t$,
\[
\E\!\left[A_v(t)^2+S_v(t)^2\mid \bar\cI_t\right]\le M_2.
\]
This is a standard sufficient condition for quadratic Lyapunov drift bounds \cite{Neely2010}.
Assume a declared acceleration regime with $\mathrm{DAR}(t)\ge \underline d$ and a declared control-variation ceiling $\|u_t-u_{t-1}\|\le \overline{\Delta u}$.
Design parameters satisfy
\[
\lambda_{\mathrm{leg}}+\Lambda_{\mathrm{spam}}e^{-\beta_f f_{\max}}+\lambda_{\mathrm{self}}+\eta_{\mathrm{self}}\overline{\Delta u}<\mu_v\underline d.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Queue-stable strict throughput]\label{prop:queue}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:queue]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:queue}, the strict-verification queue is mean-stable: there exists $B<\infty$ such that
\[
\sup_{T\ge 1}\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T}\E[Q_v(t)]\le B,
\]
hence strict verification does not suffer liveness collapse from unbounded backlog growth.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $Q_t:=Q_v(t)$, $A_t:=A_v(t)$, $S_t:=S_v(t)$.
Using $Q_{t+1}=\max\{0,Q_t+A_t-S_t\}$ and $V(q)=q^2$, we have the inequality
\[
Q_{t+1}^2\le Q_t^2+(A_t-S_t)^2+2Q_t(A_t-S_t).
\]
Taking conditional expectation given $\bar\cI_t$ and applying Assumption \ref{ass:queue} yields
that $\E[(A_t-S_t)^2\mid \bar\cI_t]\le 2\E[A_t^2+S_t^2\mid \bar\cI_t]\le 2M_2$, hence the quadratic term is uniformly bounded.
\[
\E[V(Q_{t+1})-V(Q_t)\mid \bar\cI_t]\le C_0-2\eps_0\,Q_t,
\]
for finite $C_0$ and some $\eps_0>0$ induced by the strict slack
$\mu_v\underline d-(\lambda_{\mathrm{leg}}+\Lambda_{\mathrm{spam}}e^{-\beta_f f_{\max}}+\lambda_{\mathrm{self}}+\eta_{\mathrm{self}}\overline{\Delta u})$.
Standard Foster--Lyapunov drift implies mean stability and the stated bound.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Compression, feasible controls, and information-space growth}
\begin{definition}[Operational state decomposition]\label{def:operational_state_decomposition}
Let
\[
x_t^{\setminus d}:=(F(t),S(t),\cA(t),\varrho_t),\qquad
x_t:=(x_t^{\setminus d},d(t))
\]
collect floor state, reserve state, adversarial context, pinned policy/profile commitment (hash-addressed), and measurement dimension.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Minimum realized-growth threshold]\label{def:minimum_realized_growth_threshold}
Let $\rho_{\min}(t)\in\R$ denote the minimum realized strict-growth rate required by the current declared viability contract (floors/reserves and verification budget). This scalar threshold is recorded in the ledger and is therefore observable.
\end{definition}


\begin{definition}[Effective overhead]\label{def:effective_overhead}
For controls $(\kappa,p,q)$ and state $x_t$:
\[
\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(\kappa,p,q;x_t)=\phi_{\mathrm{meas}}(x_t)+(1-p)(1-q)\phi_{\mathrm{replay}}(x_t)+\phi_{\mathrm{tax}}(\kappa;x_t).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Metered overhead components]\label{def:overhead_components}
The metering profile $\rho_{\mathrm{meter}}(t)$ in $\Gamma_t$ \emph{MUST} specify deterministic replay-verifiable procedures that, given the pre-decision information $\cI_t$ and a proposed control $(\kappa,p,q)$, output nonnegative scalars
\[
\phi_{\mathrm{meas}}(x_t),\qquad \phi_{\mathrm{replay}}(x_t),\qquad \phi_{\mathrm{tax}}(\kappa;x_t),\qquad \phi_{\mathrm{tax}}^{\max}(x_t),
\]
with $\phi_{\mathrm{tax}}(\kappa;x_t)\le \phi_{\mathrm{tax}}^{\max}(x_t)$ and $\phi_{\mathrm{tax}}(\cdot;x_t)$ weakly increasing in $\kappa$.
These values \emph{MUST} be included (with their replay certificates) in the strict credit event \texttt{STRICT\_CREDIT} of the corresponding cycle.
Fail-closed rule: if any required metering value is not replay-verifiable from $\cI_t$ and the strict projection, then $\mathrm{SC}(t)=0$ and strict credit is zero.
\end{definition}


\begin{assumption}[Compression-feasible control set]\label{ass:compress}
For each state $x_t$, admissible controls form a nonempty compact convex set
\[
\cK(x_t)\subseteq [0,\kappa_{\max}]\times[0,1]\times[0,1],
\]
with constraints enforced by fail-closed metering (prover/checker caps, fallback limits, and replay compatibility).
\end{assumption}


\begin{definition}[Certified gross-yield functional]\label{def:mu}
Fix a cycle $t$ with observable state $x_t$ and admitted controls $u_t=(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t)$.
A deployment profile \MUST{} declare a predictable map $\mu(\kappa,p,q;x_t)$ and publish a replay-verifiable calibration bundle (Definition \ref{def:calibration_bundle}) for its parameters.
Let $\eps_\mu(t)\ge 0$ be a publicly recorded uncertainty margin for cycle $t$.

Let $G(t)$ be the bridge-adjusted raw log increment from Definition \ref{def:strict_progress_credit}.
Define the \emph{$\mu$-certificate validity indicator} $\mathrm{MU}(t)\in\{0,1\}$ by
\[
\mathrm{MU}(t):=
\ind\Big\{
\mathrm{SC}(t)=\mathrm{BC}(t)=1\ \wedge\
G(t)\ge \mu(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\log\!\big(1+\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)\big)-\eps_\mu(t)
\Big\}.
\]
When $\mathrm{MU}(t)=1$, the declared $\mu$ map provides a certified lower bound on the realized raw increment up to margin $\eps_\mu(t)$.
When $\mathrm{MU}(t)=0$, any claim that uses $\mu$ as a certified lower bound at cycle $t$ fails closed; strict credit $\Delta_s(t)$ remains defined from observable proxies, but $\mu$-derived certified inequalities are not asserted for that cycle.
\end{definition}


\begin{definition}[Information-space counted rate]\label{def:information_space_counted_rate}
\[
r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x_t):=\mu(\kappa,p,q;x_t)-\log\!\big(1+\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(\kappa,p,q;x_t)\big).
\]
\end{definition}


\begin{proposition}[Strict-credit lower bound by counted rate]\label{prop:strict_credit_lower_bound}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Let $t\ge 1$.
If $\mathrm{SC}(t)=\mathrm{BC}(t)=1$ and $\mathrm{MU}(t)=1$, then
\[
\Delta_s(t)\ \ge\ \max\{0,\ r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\eps_\mu(t)-\ell_s(t-1)\}.
\]
In particular, when the contraction gap is closed ($\ell_s(t-1)=0$), this reduces to
$\Delta_s(t)\ge \max\{0,r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\eps_\mu(t)\}$.
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
By Definition \ref{def:strict_progress_credit},
\[
\Delta_s(t)=\max\{0,\,G(t)-\ell_s(t-1)\}.
\]
When $\mathrm{MU}(t)=1$, Definition \ref{def:mu} yields
\[
G(t)\ge r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\eps_\mu(t).
\]
Substituting into the expression for $\Delta_s(t)$ and using monotonicity of $z\mapsto\max\{0,z\}$ gives the stated lower bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Local steady-regime window]\label{ass:window}
Fix a state $x$ and let $\cK_\kappa(x):=\{\kappa:\exists p,q,(\kappa,p,q)\in\cK(x)\}$.
Define
\[
\bar r_x(\kappa):=\sup_{(p,q):(\kappa,p,q)\in\cK(x)} r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x).
\]
Assume $\bar r_x$ is continuous and strictly quasiconcave on $\cK_\kappa(x)$, with $\bar r_x(0)\le 0$ and $\sup_{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x)}\bar r_x(\kappa)>0$.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Supremum attainment and generalized envelope]\label{ass:danskin}
For each fixed $x$ and $\kappa\in\mathrm{int}(\cK_\kappa(x))$:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the maximizer set
  \[
  \cM_x(\kappa):=\arg\max_{(p,q):(\kappa,p,q)\in\cK(x)} r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x)
  \]
  is nonempty and compact;
  \item for each admissible $(p,q)$, $r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x)$ is locally Lipschitz in $\kappa$;
  \item the generalized directional derivative of $\bar r_x$ obeys
  \[
  D\bar r_x(\kappa;v)=\max_{(p,q)\in \cM_x(\kappa)} \partial_{\kappa}r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x)\,v,\quad v\in\R.
  \]
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

\subsubsection{Operational auditability and fallbacks for window regularity}
Assumptions \ref{ass:window} and \ref{ass:danskin} are strong regularity conditions on the induced one-dimensional profile $\bar r_x(\kappa)$.
For observable-only deployment, these assumptions are treated as \emph{auditable contracts}: the system must either (i) publish finite evidence supporting them on the active regime window, or (ii) fall back to a conservative control mode that does not rely on them.

\begin{definition}[Window-audit record]\label{def:window_audit_record}
For a fixed state class $x$ and epoch $e$, a window-audit record is a replayable artifact
\[
\mathsf{WinAudit}(x,e):=(\mathcal G_e,\widehat{\bar r}_e, L_e, \mathsf{QC}_e, \mathsf{Lip}_e, \delta_e),
\]
where $\mathcal G_e\subseteq \cK_\kappa(x)$ is a finite grid of $\kappa$ values,
$\widehat{\bar r}_e$ is the replay-computed profile value on $\mathcal G_e$ obtained by maximizing over $(p,q)$ using the declared solver interface,
$L_e$ is a certified local Lipschitz envelope for $\kappa\mapsto r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x)$ on $\mathcal G_e$,
$\mathsf{QC}_e\in\{0,1\}$ is a replay-verifiable discrete quasiconcavity/unimodality check outcome on $\widehat{\bar r}_e$,
$\mathsf{Lip}_e\in\{0,1\}$ is a replay-verifiable check that the claimed $L_e$ upper-bounds observed finite differences on $\mathcal G_e$,
and $\delta_e$ is the allocated statistical risk budget for any stochastic components of the checks.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Audited regularity or fail-closed fallback]\label{ass:window_audit}
For any epoch where Theorems \ref{thm:window} or \ref{thm:optkappa} are used as certified guarantees, the ledger \MUST{} contain a valid window-audit record $\mathsf{WinAudit}(x,e)$ for the active state class $x$ with $\mathsf{QC}_e=\mathsf{Lip}_e=1$ and an explicit risk budget $\delta_e$.
If no such record exists (or if any check fails), the system \MUST{} enter a fallback mode in which:
(i) takeoff-window claims are not asserted as interval claims, and
(ii) control selection uses only globally valid certified envelopes (e.g., Assumption \ref{ass:globalopt} and regret bounds) and sets any window-dependent strict-growth claim to fail-closed.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Conservative fallback without quasiconcavity]\label{prop:window_fallback}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:globalopt,ass:window_audit,thm:optkappa]}
If Assumption \ref{ass:window_audit} triggers fallback (no audited window regularity), then any certified strict-growth claim that relies on $\cI_+(x)$ is inadmissible.
However, budgeted control choices based on certified upper/lower envelopes (Assumption \ref{ass:globalopt}) remain admissible, and the regret certificate in Theorem \ref{thm:optkappa} remains valid whenever its own audit conditions are met.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The interval structure of $\cI_+(x)$ and the derived doubling-time interpretation rely on Assumption \ref{ass:window}.
Fallback explicitly disables these claims.
The regret bound of Theorem \ref{thm:optkappa} is stated in terms of certified envelopes $L_x(B),U_x(B)$ and does not require quasiconcavity; hence it remains valid when its assumptions hold.
\end{proof}
\begin{theorem}[Takeoff-window law]\label{thm:window}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:compress,ass:window]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:compress} and \ref{ass:window}, the positive set
\[
\cI_+(x):=\{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x):\bar r_x(\kappa)>0\}
\]
is a nonempty open interval $(\kappa_-(x),\kappa_+(x))\cap\cK_\kappa(x)$.
For any admissible $\kappa\in\cI_+(x)$ and any maximizing $(p,q)$, information-space doubling time is
\[
T_2^{\mathrm{info}}=\frac{\log 2}{r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x)}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Assumption \ref{ass:compress}, $\cK(x)\subseteq\R^3$ is nonempty compact convex.
Its projection onto the $\kappa$-coordinate,
\[
\cK_\kappa(x):=\{\kappa:\exists(p,q)\ \text{s.t.}\ (\kappa,p,q)\in\cK(x)\},
\]
is therefore a nonempty compact interval in $\R$.
Assumption \ref{ass:window} gives continuity of $\bar r_x$ on $\cK_\kappa(x)$ and strict quasiconcavity on the audited grid, so each strict superlevel set $\{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x):\bar r_x(\kappa)>c\}$ is an interval and is open relative to $\cK_\kappa(x)$.
Since $\bar r_x(0)\le 0$ while $\sup_{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x)}\bar r_x(\kappa)>0$ by Assumption \ref{ass:window}, the strict positive set $\cI_+(x)$ is a nonempty open interval of the stated form.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Single-threshold special case]\label{cor:singlethresholdspecialcase}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
If $\bar r_x$ is strictly increasing on $\cK_\kappa(x)$, then
\[
\cI_+(x)=\{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x):\kappa>\kappa_c(x)\},
\]
for $\kappa_c(x):=\inf\{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x):\bar r_x(\kappa)>0\}$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proposition}[Closed-form special case]\label{prop:closed}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
If $\mu(\kappa,p,q;x)\equiv\mu_0$, $p,q$ are fixed constants, and
\[
\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(\kappa)=\phi_{\mathrm{base}}+\frac{\phi_0}{1+\kappa},
\]
then the positive-threshold boundary solves
\[
\kappa_c=\frac{\phi_0}{e^{\mu_0}(1+\phi_{\mathrm{base}})-1}-1,
\]
whenever the denominator is positive.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set $r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa)=0$:
\[
\mu_0-\log\!\left(1+\phi_{\mathrm{base}}+\frac{\phi_0}{1+\kappa}\right)=0.
\]
Exponentiate and solve linearly for $(1+\kappa)^{-1}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Audit-compressed RSI bound]\label{thm:rsi}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:compress]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:compress},
\[
\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(\kappa,p,q;x_t)
\le
\phi_{\mathrm{meas}}(x_t)+(1-p)(1-q)\phi_{\mathrm{replay}}(x_t)+\phi_{\mathrm{tax}}^{\max}(x_t),
\]
with fail-closed rejection whenever tax metering exceeds $\phi_{\mathrm{tax}}^{\max}(x_t)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the definition of $\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}$ and admissibility constraints in $\cK(x_t)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Sub-1\% overhead condition]\label{cor:sub1overheadcondition}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[thm:rsi]}
If the right-hand side in Theorem \ref{thm:rsi} is at most $0.01$, then overhead remains below 1\%.
\end{corollary}

\begin{assumption}[Anytime envelope certification under finite budget]\label{ass:globalopt}
For each fixed state $x$ and compute budget $B\in\N$, the optimization engine outputs:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item a finite candidate set $\cS_x(B)\subseteq \cK_\kappa(x)$,
  \item certified bounds $L_x(B),U_x(B)$ such that
  \[
  L_x(B)\le \sup_{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x)}\bar r_x(\kappa)\le U_x(B),
  \]
  \item monotone refinement:
  \[
  L_x(B+1)\ge L_x(B),\qquad U_x(B+1)\le U_x(B).
  \]
\end{enumerate}
Define anytime residual uncertainty
\[
G_x(B):=U_x(B)-L_x(B)\ge 0.
\]
No uniform finite-budget convergence $G_x(B)\le\eps$ for all instances is assumed.
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[Budgeted anytime compression certification]\label{thm:optkappa}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:globalopt]}
Fix state $x$.
Under Assumption \ref{ass:globalopt}, let
\[
\kappa_B\in\arg\max_{\kappa\in\cS_x(B)} \bar r_x(\kappa)
\]
for budget $B$.
Then the auditable suboptimality bound is
\[
0\le \sup_{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x)}\bar r_x(\kappa)-\bar r_x(\kappa_B)\le G_x(B).
\]
Moreover $G_x(B)$ is nonincreasing in $B$, so additional compute never worsens certified regret.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By construction of $\kappa_B$, $\bar r_x(\kappa_B)\ge L_x(B)$.
Assumption \ref{ass:globalopt} gives
\[
\sup_{\kappa}\bar r_x(\kappa)\le U_x(B),
\]
hence
\[
\sup_{\kappa}\bar r_x(\kappa)-\bar r_x(\kappa_B)\le U_x(B)-L_x(B)=G_x(B).
\]
Monotonicity follows directly from refinement inequalities for $L_x,U_x$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[No uniform finite-time global certificate on universal classes]
\label{prop:nouniformcertificate}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
If the prover-tax landscape family contains Turing-universal instances with self-referential verification dynamics, then no single algorithm can guarantee a fixed $\eps$-global certificate for all instances within a uniform finite budget bound.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assume for contradiction that there exists an algorithm $\mathcal A$ and a finite budget bound $B$ such that, for every instance in the declared landscape family (including Turing-universal ones with self-referential verification dynamics), $\mathcal A$ returns within budget $B$ an $\eps$-global certificate asserting that a given objective-gap predicate holds (or returns a universally valid failure certificate).

Fix any Turing machine $M$ and input $w$.
Construct (by an effective reduction) an instance $\mathcal I(M,w)$ whose ledger-admissible dynamics encode the computation of $M(w)$ so that:
(i) if $M(w)$ halts, then there exists a control sequence within the admissible class that forces the objective-gap predicate to be satisfied, and
(ii) if $M(w)$ does not halt, then no admissible control sequence can satisfy the predicate (or any satisfaction would require violating the strict completeness/finality rules).
Such encodings are standard: objective-gap predicates can be arranged to depend on the existence of a finite witness trace corresponding to a halting computation, while strict admissibility prevents ``cheating'' witnesses.

Run $\mathcal A$ on $\mathcal I(M,w)$.
By assumption, $\mathcal A$ terminates within $B$ and decides whether the certificate is attainable.
This yields a decider for the halting problem, contradicting its undecidability.
Therefore no such uniform finite-budget global-certificate algorithm can exist on any family that contains Turing-universal instances with self-referential verification dynamics.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Safe online compression control with compute-aware regret]\label{cor:safeonlinecompressioncontrolwithcompute}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:danskin]}
On each admitted cycle choose budget $B_t$ and set
\[
\kappa_t:=\kappa_{B_t}.
\]
Then per-cycle auditable regret satisfies
\[
\sup_{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x_t)}\bar r_{x_t}(\kappa)-\bar r_{x_t}(\kappa_t)\le G_{x_t}(B_t).
\]
Subgradient signals from Assumption \ref{ass:danskin} may accelerate local search, while safety-critical guarantees are carried only by certified uncertainty envelopes.
\end{corollary}

\subsection{Ontology engineering and endogenous trigger conditions}
\begin{definition}[Measurement dimension]\label{def:measurement_dimension}
$d(t)\in\N$ is the effective dimensionality of declared observation channels used in strict evaluation.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Non-regressive amendment gate]\label{ass:amend}
Accepted amendments preserve strict closure, fail-closed semantics, floor certifiability, and reserve floors.
Amendments violating these constraints are rejected.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Dimension-gain class]\label{ass:dim}
There exists an amendment class $\cU_{\mathrm{ont}}$ and constants $\Delta d_{\min}>0$, $W_{\mathrm{ont}}^{\max}$, $\Delta S_C^{\max}$ such that any accepted $u\in\cU_{\mathrm{ont}}$ satisfies:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item $d(t+1)-d(t)\ge \Delta d_{\min}$,
  \item work cost $\le W_{\mathrm{ont}}^{\max}$ and constitutional reserve draw $\le \Delta S_C^{\max}$,
  \item acceptance only when trigger evidence (representation bottleneck, semantic-floor risk, or persistent unresolved novelty) is bridge-certified and replay-verifiable \cite{Takahashi2025EndogenousTrigger,Takahashi2025Teleogenetic}.
\end{enumerate}
Moreover there exists nondecreasing $g_{x^{\setminus d}}(d)$ for each reduced state class $x^{\setminus d}$ such that
\[
\bar r_{(x^{\setminus d},d')}(\kappa)\ge \bar r_{(x^{\setminus d},d)}(\kappa)+g_{x^{\setminus d}}(d')-g_{x^{\setminus d}}(d),\quad d'\ge d.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Ontology-engineering gain]\label{prop:ontology}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:amend,ass:dim]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:amend} and \ref{ass:dim}, if gate preconditions hold for $m$ consecutive cycles, then
\[
d(t+m)-d(t)\ge m\Delta d_{\min}.
\]
For any fixed reduced state class $x^{\setminus d}$ and admissible $\kappa$,
\[
\bar r_{(x^{\setminus d},d(t+m))}(\kappa)-\bar r_{(x^{\setminus d},d(t))}(\kappa)
\ge
g_{x^{\setminus d}}\big(d(t+m)\big)-g_{x^{\setminus d}}\big(d(t)\big)\ge 0.
\]
Hence admissible ontology amendments weakly expand takeoff-feasible compression regions.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
First inequality follows by summing per-cycle increments from Assumption \ref{ass:dim}(1).
Second inequality is direct from monotone response gain assumption applied at $d=d(t)$ and $d'=d(t+m)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Semantic novelty entropy]\label{def:semantic_novelty_entropy}
For active task/floor kernel $\Gamma_t$, let $H_{\mathrm{sem}}(t)$ be the conditional entropy rate of novel strict artifacts not losslessly predictable from previously certified artifacts under $\Gamma_t$.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Semantic exhaustion under fixed kernel]\label{ass:exhaust}
For any epoch in which $\Gamma_t$ and measurement dimension $d(t)$ are fixed, if strict operations continue indefinitely then
\[
\lim_{t\to\infty}H_{\mathrm{sem}}(t)=0
\]
and there exists a nonnegative envelope sequence $e^{\mathrm{sem}}_t$ such that attainable per-cycle strict gain is at most $e^{\mathrm{sem}}_t$ with
\[
\sum_{t=0}^{\infty}e^{\mathrm{sem}}_t<\infty.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Discontinuous teleogenesis event]\label{def:discontinuous_teleogenesis_event}
A discontinuous teleogenesis jump is a kernel-adoption boundary $(t-1)\to t$ at which the ledger records a pinned adoption event that installs a new governance/evaluation kernel $\Gamma_t$ for cycle $t$.
The adoption record declares \emph{cross-kernel adoption credit transfer} fixed to zero, meaning that the justification for adopting $\Gamma_t$ may not cite strict credit accumulated under earlier kernels; it must rely on higher-order observable witnesses (independent challenge domains, replayable risk evidence, and reserve-safe ratification).
This restriction is about \emph{adoption justification} and does not alter strict credit accounting after activation.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Teleogenesis epoch-mass lower envelope]\label{ass:jumpmass}
Let $\tau_0:=0$ and let $0<\tau_1<\tau_2<\cdots$ be the activation cycles of discontinuous teleogenesis jumps, meaning that each boundary $(\tau_n-1)\to\tau_n$ satisfies Definition \ref{def:discontinuous_teleogenesis_event}.
Define teleogenesis epochs by
\[
I_n:=[\tau_n,\tau_{n+1})\quad (n\ge 0),
\]
with the convention $\tau_{n+1}=\infty$ if no further jump occurs.
Define the strict epoch mass
\[
J_n:=\sum_{t\in I_n}\Delta_s(t).
\]
Each epoch must publish an auditable lower witness $\underline J_n\in[0,J_n]$ that is a deterministic function of strict public artifacts (e.g., an anytime-valid partial-sum witness that can be finalized by the next jump boundary).
For unbounded-growth claims, the declared lower envelope must satisfy
\[
\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}\underline J_n=\infty.
\]
\end{assumption}


\begin{proposition}[Teleogenesis epoch-mass decomposition]\label{prop:teleo}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:exhaust,ass:jumpmass,def:discontinuous_teleogenesis_event]}
Assume Assumption \ref{ass:exhaust}.
Let $\tau_0:=0$ and let $0<\tau_1<\tau_2<\cdots$ be the activation cycles of discontinuous teleogenesis jumps (Definition \ref{def:discontinuous_teleogenesis_event}).
Let $I_n=[\tau_n,\tau_{n+1})$ and $J_n=\sum_{t\in I_n}\Delta_s(t)$ be the corresponding epoch masses as in Assumption \ref{ass:jumpmass}.
Then the cumulative strict credit decomposes as
\[
\sum_{t=0}^{\infty}\Delta_s(t)=\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}J_n.
\]
In particular,
\[
\sum_{t=0}^{\infty}\Delta_s(t)=\infty
\iff
\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}J_n=\infty.
\]
Moreover, if some terminal epoch has $\tau_{n+1}=\infty$ while $\Gamma_t$ and $d(t)$ remain fixed on that epoch, then Assumption \ref{ass:exhaust} implies $J_n<\infty$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By construction, the intervals $I_n$ form a disjoint partition of $[0,\infty)$.
Therefore
\[
\sum_{t=0}^{\infty}\Delta_s(t)=\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}\sum_{t\in I_n}\Delta_s(t)=\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}J_n,
\]
where the equality is by regrouping a nonnegative series.
The divergence equivalence follows immediately.
For the final statement, if an epoch is infinite and $\Gamma_t$ and $d(t)$ are fixed on that epoch, Assumption \ref{ass:exhaust} provides a summable envelope for attainable per-cycle strict gain on that epoch, hence its total mass is finite.
\end{proof}


\begin{corollary}[Auditable sufficiency for unbounded growth]\label{cor:auditablesufficiencyforunboundedgrowth}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:jumpmass]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:jumpmass}, if $J_n\ge \underline J_n$ and
$\sum_n \underline J_n=\infty$, then $\sum_t\Delta_s(t)=\infty$.
