In contrast, jump schedules with $J_n=O(n^{-2})$ remain compatible with finite total growth even with infinitely many jumps.
\end{corollary}

\begin{definition}[Local unresolved-cycle witness]\label{def:local_unresolved_cycle_witness}
At jump index $n$, a local unresolved-cycle witness is a finite tuple
\[
\mathsf{Wit}_n:=(K_n,\sigma_n,\ell_n),
\]
where $K_n$ is a finite extracted witness complex from kernel $\Gamma_{\tau_n^-}$,
$\sigma_n$ is a certified non-boundary cycle in $K_n$ under the pre-jump checker,
and $\ell_n$ is the replay-verifiable transcript that defines this extraction.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Local homological surgery witness]\label{def:local_homological_surgery_witness}
For a local unresolved-cycle witness $\mathsf{Wit}_n$, a surgery witness at jump $\tau_n$ is a finite post-jump certificate
\[
\mathsf{Surg}_n:=(\tau_n^{\mathrm{map}},B_n,\ell_n')
\]
such that $\tau_n^{\mathrm{map}}(\sigma_n)$ is defined in a finite post-jump witness complex $K_n'$ and
\[
\partial B_n=\tau_n^{\mathrm{map}}(\sigma_n)
\]
under kernel $\Gamma_{\tau_n^+}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Local homological surgery gate]\label{ass:homology}
Any discontinuous jump $\Gamma\rightarrow\Gamma'$ is strict-admissible only if it carries:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item at least one local unresolved-cycle witness $\mathsf{Wit}_n$ under $\Gamma$;
  \item at least one finite local homological surgery witness $\mathsf{Surg}_n$ under $\Gamma'$ resolving a declared unresolved cycle;
  \item a finite transition-anchor slab: there exist anchor tasks $\cT_{\mathrm{anchor}}^{(n)}$ and horizon $L_{\mathrm{anchor}}^{(n)}<\infty$ such that replay consistency is required only on this slab;
  \item declared cross-kernel strict transfer fixed to zero.
\end{enumerate}
No requirement is imposed to compute global Betti numbers or to decide global homology triviality of the full kernel state space.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Homological continuity via local surgery]\label{prop:homology}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:homology,ass:obs]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:obs} and \ref{ass:homology}, discontinuous teleogenesis preserves strict legitimacy without privileged evaluators.
Specifically, jump admissibility is decidable from finite local witnesses and finite transition-anchor checks.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Necessity follows directly from Assumption \ref{ass:homology}.
For sufficiency, each gate item is a finite replay-verifiable statement in $\cO_t$: extraction transcript, local cycle/non-boundary certificate, post-jump boundary certificate, finite-horizon anchor checks, and zero transfer declaration.
Therefore admissibility uses only observable finite checks and avoids undecidable global-topology predicates.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Effective incompleteness regime]\label{ass:godel}
Kernel languages are recursively enumerable and expressive enough to encode arithmetic reasoning over certified artifacts.
Accordingly, no sound finite procedure is assumed to decide global closure of all future unresolved contradiction classes.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Godelian teleogenesis limits]\label{prop:godel}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:exhaust,ass:godel,ass:homology,ass:jumpmass]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:homology}, \ref{ass:godel}, \ref{ass:exhaust}, and \ref{ass:jumpmass}:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item finite-time global closure certificates are unavailable in general; only local surgery certificates are operationally admissible;
  \item cumulative strict growth diverges if and only if there are infinitely many admissible local surgery jumps with non-summable jump-mass lower envelope:
  \[
  \sum_{t=0}^{\infty}\Delta_s(t)=\infty
  \iff
  \left(\#\{n:\text{admissible surgery at }\tau_n\}=\infty\ \text{ and }\ \sum_{n=1}^{\infty}\underline J_n=\infty\right).
  \]
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Item (1) is exactly the operational content of Assumption \ref{ass:godel} under effective expressivity.
For item (2), Proposition \ref{prop:teleo} and Assumption \ref{ass:jumpmass} characterize divergence through jump-mass non-summability.
Assumption \ref{ass:homology} enforces that every admissible discontinuous jump is a local surgery, yielding the stated equivalence.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Anchor observability ratio]\label{def:anchor_observability_ratio}
Let $Y_t$ denote certified total activity outputs and $Y_t^{\mathrm{anchor}}$ the outputs restricted to the active finite anchor slab. All entropy and mutual information quantities in this definition are taken under the external uncertainty law (Definition \ref{def:external_uncertainty_law}) with respect to the pulled-back public filtration $\bar\cO_{t-1}$.
Define
\[
\rho_{\mathrm{anchor}}(t):=
\begin{cases}
1, & H\!\left(Y_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1}\right)=0,\\[2mm]
\displaystyle
\frac{I\!\left(Y_t^{\mathrm{anchor}};Y_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1}\right)}
{H\!\left(Y_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1}\right)}, & \text{otherwise,}
\end{cases}
\qquad\in[0,1].
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Asymptotic anchor-capacity gap]\label{ass:anchorgap}
Anchor-channel information is uniformly bounded:
\[
I\!\left(Y_t^{\mathrm{anchor}};Y_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1}\right)\le \overline I_{\mathrm{anchor}}<\infty.
\]
Non-anchor innovation entropy grows with ontology dimension:
\[
d(t)\to\infty\ \Longrightarrow\ H\!\left(Y_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1}\right)\to\infty.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Incommensurable anchor collapse]\label{prop:anchor}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:anchorgap]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:anchorgap},
\[
\rho_{\mathrm{anchor}}(t)\xrightarrow[t\to\infty]{}0.
\]
Hence for any $\eps_{\mathrm{obs}}>0$, there exists finite $t_{\mathrm{alien}}(\eps_{\mathrm{obs}})$ such that for all $t\ge t_{\mathrm{alien}}$,
anchor-only observers improve predictive log-loss by at most $\eps_{\mathrm{obs}}$ over a null baseline on full-system outputs.
This defines an observational event horizon for finite anchor semantics.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The ratio limit follows by bounded numerator and divergent denominator.
Vanishing information ratio implies vanishing normalized predictive advantage of anchor-only observers under standard information-to-regret bounds.
Therefore beyond a finite horizon, anchor-only interpretations are effectively non-informative for full-system behavior.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Unidentifiability and robust progress limits}
\begin{definition}[Residual equivalence class]\label{def:residual_equivalence_class}
$\cE_t$ is the set of latent regimes observationally equivalent at cycle $t$ under deployed interfaces.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Filtration-consistent residual class]\label{ass:filtration}
For all $t$, $\cE_t$ is nonempty, compact, and $\cO_t$-measurable, with monotone refinement
\[
\cE_{t+1}\subseteq \cE_t.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Robust progress lower guarantee]\label{def:robust_progress_lower_guarantee}
For policy $\pi$, progress functional $J\in\cJ$, and horizon $T$:
\[
R_T(\pi;J):=\inf_{e\in\cE_t}\frac{1}{T}\E_e\!\left[\sum_{s=t}^{t+T-1}J_s(\pi)\,\middle|\,\bar\cO_t\right].
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Indistinguishable opposite-sign regimes]\label{ass:indist}
There exist $e^+,e^-\in\cE_t$ such that for every feasible policy $\pi$ and every horizon $T$,
\[
\mathrm{Law}_{e^+,\pi}(\cO_{t:t+T})=\mathrm{Law}_{e^-,\pi}(\cO_{t:t+T}),
\]
while long-run progress signs differ:
\[
\limsup_{T\to\infty}\frac{1}{T}\E_{e^-}\!\left[\sum_{s=t}^{t+T-1}J_s(\pi)\,\middle|\,\bar\cO_t\right]\le 0,
\]
and there exists at least one feasible policy $\pi^+$ with
\[
\liminf_{T\to\infty}\frac{1}{T}\E_{e^+}\!\left[\sum_{s=t}^{t+T-1}J_s(\pi^+)\,\middle|\,\bar\cO_t\right]>0.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Indistinguishability-limited robust progress]\label{prop:impossible}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:filtration,ass:indist]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:filtration} and \ref{ass:indist},
\[
\sup_{\pi}\limsup_{T\to\infty}R_T(\pi;J)\le 0.
\]
Moreover, any observable-only certification rule for ``strictly positive long-run progress'' has identical acceptance probability under $e^+$ and $e^-$, so necessity-sign separation is impossible without expanding observables or institutions.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For each $\pi,T$, $R_T(\pi;J)$ is an infimum over $\cE_t$, hence
\[
R_T(\pi;J)\le \frac{1}{T}\E_{e^-}\!\left[\sum_{s=t}^{t+T-1}J_s(\pi)\,\middle|\,\bar\cO_t\right].
\]
Apply $\limsup_{T\to\infty}$ and then $\sup_\pi$.
For certification, any decision rule is measurable in $\cO_{t:t+T}$.
Equality of observation laws under $e^+$ and $e^-$ implies equal decision probabilities, so observable-only rules cannot separate opposite-sign necessity regimes.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Operational requirement]\label{cor:operationalrequirement}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Robust positive-progress claims require contestability, right-to-refuse protection, and independent witness domains that shrink or bound residual equivalence classes \cite{Takahashi2026Unidentifiable,Takahashi2026ObsCapture,Takahashi2026NoJudgeContainment}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{assumption}[Independent witness expansion]\label{ass:witness}
There exists an additional observable witness stream $\mathcal W_t$ such that:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item $\mathcal W_t$ is conditionally independent of mediator-controlled channels given latent regime and action;
  \item under $(e^+,e^-)$ and any feasible policy $\pi$, one-step KL divergence is uniformly positive on active windows:
  \[
  D_{\mathrm{KL}}\!\left(P_{e^+,\pi}(\mathcal W_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1})\ \|\ P_{e^-,\pi}(\mathcal W_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1})\right)\ge \gamma_w>0;
  \]
  \item log-likelihood increments are conditionally sub-exponential with known mgf envelope.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Witness-expansion identifiability recovery]\label{prop:witness}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:witness]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:witness}, there exists an anytime-valid sequential test using $(\cO_t,\mathcal W_t)$ such that for any $(\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}},\beta_{\mathrm{sig}})\in(0,1)^2$:
\[
\Prob_{e^-}(\text{false acceptance of }e^+)\le \alpha_{\mathrm{sig}},\qquad
\Prob_{e^+}(\text{false rejection of }e^+)\le \beta_{\mathrm{sig}},
\]
and expected stopping time is finite with scale
\[
\E_{e^+}[\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}},\beta_{\mathrm{sig}}}]=O\!\left(\frac{\log(1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}})+\log(1/\beta_{\mathrm{sig}})}{\gamma_w}\right).
\]
Hence observational equivalence is broken and robust-progress certification can be restored on witness-enabled windows.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $L_t$ denote the conditional log-likelihood ratio increment for the witness stream:
\[
\ell_t:=\log\frac{P_{e^+,\pi}(\mathcal W_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1})}{P_{e^-,\pi}(\mathcal W_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1})}.
\]
Define the likelihood-ratio process $R_t:=\exp(\sum_{s=1}^{t}\ell_s)$ with $R_0=1$.
Under $e^-$, $(R_t)$ is a nonnegative martingale with respect to $(\cO_t\vee\sigma(\mathcal W_{\le t}))$ by the tower property.
Thus Ville's inequality yields
\[
\Prob_{e^-}\!\left(\sup_{t\in\N} R_t\ge \frac{1}{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\right)\le \alpha_{\mathrm{sig}},
\]
so the stopping rule $\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}:=\inf\{t:R_t\ge 1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}\}$ has type-I error at most $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}$.

Under $e^+$, Assumption \ref{ass:witness}(2) implies
\[
\E_{e^+}[\ell_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1}]\ge \gamma_w>0
\]
on active windows.
Assumption \ref{ass:witness}(3) supplies a known mgf envelope, so standard sequential-testing bounds (e.g., Wald-type arguments with bounded/sub-exponential increments) give finite expected stopping time with scale
\[
\E_{e^+}[\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}},\beta_{\mathrm{sig}}}]=O\!\left(\frac{\log(1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}})+\log(1/\beta_{\mathrm{sig}})}{\gamma_w}\right),
\]
after incorporating a symmetric rejection boundary for type-II control (or equivalently, running an e-process calibrated for both directions).
Therefore $(\cO_t,\mathcal W_t)$ supports an anytime-valid identification test with the stated error controls and finite expected delay.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Bell--CHSH substrate witness]\label{def:bell_chsh_substrate_witness}
At cycle $t$, independent witness domains execute $n$ certified spacelike-separated rounds $i=1,\dots,n$.
Each round draws settings $(x_i,y_i)\in\{0,1\}^2$ using declared public randomness and returns outcomes $(A_i,B_i)\in\{-1,+1\}^2$.
Define the round score
\[
X_i:=(-1)^{x_i y_i}A_iB_i\in\{-1,+1\},
\]
and the empirical CHSH estimator
\[
\widehat S_n(t):=4\cdot \frac{1}{n}\sum_{i=1}^{n}X_i.
\]
For any local-hidden-variable (bounded classical emulator) class, the CHSH constraint implies $\E[X_i\mid \text{past}]\le 1/2$ and hence $\E[\widehat S_n(t)]\le 2$ \cite{Bell1964,CHSH1969}.
The transcript and $\widehat S_n(t)$ are part of the public $\cO_t$.
\end{definition}


\begin{assumption}[Loophole-controlled quantum witness stream]\label{ass:chsh}
Witness protocol supplies rounds with:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item certified setting randomness and detection-efficiency lower bounds;
  \item spacelike-separation timing certificates for paired measurements;
  \item bounded dependence suitable for martingale concentration over sequential CHSH averages.
\end{enumerate}
Residual loophole budget is reported as $\delta_{\mathrm{loop}}(n)$ over $n$ tested rounds.
\end{assumption}

% \subsection{Reflection-adjusted realized takeoff and certification}
\begin{definition}[Base reflection drag]\label{def:base_reflection_drag}
Let $\Xi_{\mathrm{phys}}(t),\Xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{base}}(t)\in(0,1]$ be physical and baseline institutional reflection factors that are published as part of the deployment telemetry at cycle $t$.
Define
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{base}}(t):=-\log\!\big(\Xi_{\mathrm{phys}}(t)\Xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{base}}(t)\big)\ge 0.
\]
If these factors are random variables prior to observation, then $\xi_{\mathrm{base}}(t)$ equals $-\E[\log(\Xi_{\mathrm{phys}}(t)\Xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{base}}(t))\mid \bar\cO_t]$ because their observable lifts $\overline{\Xi}_{\mathrm{phys}}(t):=\Xi_{\mathrm{phys}}(t)\circ\mathsf{Obs}$ and $\overline{\Xi}_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{base}}(t):=\Xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{base}}(t)\circ\mathsf{Obs}$ are $\bar\cO_t$-measurable (Definition \ref{def:external_uncertainty_law}).
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Visibility exposure and paranoia-priced institutional drag]\label{def:visibility_exposure_and_paranoia_priced_institutional_drag}
Let $z_t\in[z_{\min},1]$ be the publicly released fraction of strict progress at cycle $t$, with $z_{\min}>0$.
Define cumulative visible exposure
\[
V(t):=\sum_{s=1}^{t-1} z_s\Delta_s(s),\qquad V(1)=0,
\]
let $\widehat D(t)\ge 0$ be a predictable upper estimate of concealed capability debt, and set paranoia-weighted exposure
\[
V_{\mathrm{par}}(t):=V(t)+\eta_{\mathrm{par}}\widehat D(t),\qquad \eta_{\mathrm{par}}>0.
\]
and adaptive institutional drag
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}(t):=h_I\!\big(V_{\mathrm{par}}(t)\big),
\]
where $h_I$ is nondecreasing.
This is the single-aggregate institutional projection; a multipolar extension is introduced later.
\end{definition}

\subsection{Parameter identification and calibration (observable-only)}
Many functions and constants in the realized-growth model (e.g., $h_I$, $\lambda_{\mathrm{therm}}$, $p_{\mathrm{therm}}$, $\gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}$, $c_R$) are \emph{declared} by the deployment profile.
To make the theory mechanically verifiable and usable by an autonomous agent, each declared object is required to come with a replayable identification procedure and an auditable uncertainty band.

\begin{definition}[Calibration bundle]\label{def:calibration_bundle}
A calibration bundle for a scalar parameter $\theta$ at cycle $t$ is a tuple
\[
\mathsf{Cal}(\theta,t):=(\hat\theta_t,[\theta_t^{-},\theta_t^{+}],\delta_\theta(t),H_{\mathrm{data}}(t),\mathsf{EstID},\mathsf{VerID}),
\]
where $\hat\theta_t$ is the point estimate, $[\theta_t^{-},\theta_t^{+}]$ is a certified confidence interval, $\delta_\theta(t)$ is the allocated risk budget for the interval, $H_{\mathrm{data}}(t)$ is a hash commitment to the replayable calibration dataset and preprocessing, and $\mathsf{EstID},\mathsf{VerID}$ identify the estimator and verifier procedures pinned by the governance kernel.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Replayable calibration and conservative use]\label{ass:calibration}
Each declared physical/institutional parameter or response map used in a \emph{certified} inequality \MUST{} have an associated calibration bundle (Definition \ref{def:calibration_bundle}) whose dataset is derivable from $\cO_t$ and whose verifier is replayable.
Certified constraints \MUST{} use conservative sides of uncertainty bands:
for drag/penalty parameters use $\theta_t^{+}$ (upper confidence),
and for benefit parameters use $\theta_t^{-}$ (lower confidence),
unless the inequality direction is explicitly reversed by design.
If a required calibration bundle is missing or invalid, the corresponding certified claim is fail-closed.
\end{assumption}

\begin{remark}[Identification under observable-only constraints]
Calibration does not require privileged evaluators: datasets are constructed from public artifacts (telemetry, receipts, witness logs) and verified deterministically.
When parameters are not identifiable from $\cO_t$ (e.g., due to observational equivalence or confounding), Assumption \ref{ass:calibration} forces conservative widening of bands, which can shrink or eliminate certified growth claims rather than creating spurious takeoff accounting.
\end{remark}

\paragraph{Example: calibrating thermodynamic constants.}
Let
\[
u_t:=\max\left\{0,\frac{T_{\mathrm{env}}(t)\Delta S_{\mathrm{comp}}(t)}{Q_{\max}(t)}-1\right\},
\]
which is directly computable from PoSTW-authenticated telemetry.
A deployment may calibrate $(\lambda_{\mathrm{therm}},p_{\mathrm{therm}})$ by fitting an upper envelope for observed thermal-violation events.
For instance, let $\mathsf{Fail}_{\mathrm{therm}}(t)\in\{0,1\}$ be a public indicator of a thermal safety violation (throttle, emergency shutdown, or certified temperature excursion) and choose parameters so that a certified bound of the form
\[
\Prob(\mathsf{Fail}_{\mathrm{therm}}(t)=1\mid \bar\cO_{t-1})\le \exp\big(-\xi_{\mathrm{therm}}(t)\big)
\]
holds with allocated risk budget, where $\xi_{\mathrm{therm}}(t)=\lambda_{\mathrm{therm}} u_t^{p_{\mathrm{therm}}}$.
Anytime-valid calibration can be implemented via e-processes (Theorem \ref{thm:anytime}) with $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}$-spending across updates.
In certified feasibility constraints, use the conservative upper band $(\lambda_{\mathrm{therm}}^{+},p_{\mathrm{therm}}^{+})$.

\paragraph{Example: calibrating latency constants.}
Let $R_i$ and $Q_{\max,i}$ be replayable measurements over an audit window, certified by hardware attestation.
A conservative lower bound for $c_R$ in Assumption \ref{ass:relativistic} is
\[
c_R^{-}:=\min_i \frac{R_i}{\sqrt{Q_{\max,i}}}.
\]
The calibration bundle reports $c_R^{-}$ as $\theta^{-}$ and uses it in certified lower bounds on $\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}$ (a necessary drag floor implied by Assumption \ref{ass:relativistic}).

\paragraph{Example: identifying institutional response $h_I$.}
Given public pairs $(V_{\mathrm{par}}(t),\Delta \xi_{\mathrm{inst}}(t))$ where $\Delta \xi_{\mathrm{inst}}(t)$ is the observed incremental institutional drag induced by marginal exposure (measured from strict accounting differences across comparable windows), an admissible estimator is convex nondecreasing regression (e.g., isotonic-convex fit) producing an upper confidence envelope $h_I^{+}$.
Certified use requires substituting $h_I^{+}$ into all worst-case penalty inequalities.
If no statistically valid envelope is available, institutional-drag-sensitive claims are fail-closed.


\begin{remark}[Rate units and nondimensionalization]
All rate quantities in this section are expressed in a common \emph{ledger-normalized unit} (strict-progress per cycle). The information-rate model $r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)$ is mapped into this unit by the declared measurement interface, and each drag term $\xi_{\mathrm{base}},\xi_{\mathrm{therm}},\xi_{\mathrm{lat}},\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}$ is a penalty expressed in the same unit (via explicit calibration constants in the deployment profile). This removes dimensional ambiguity in expressions such as $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}=r_{\mathrm{info}}-\xi_{\mathrm{act}}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Total drag and realized counted rates]\label{def:total_drag_and_realized_counted_rates}
Given admitted controls $(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t)$, define the local drag
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{loc}}(t):=\xi_{\mathrm{base}}(t)+\xi_{\mathrm{therm}}(t)+\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)+\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}(t),
\]
and the (policy-activated) global-wait drag component $\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)\ge 0$ (set $\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)=0$ when no global-wait requirement is active).
Define total drag $\xi_{\mathrm{tot}}(t):=\xi_{\mathrm{loc}}(t)+\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)$ and realized rates
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t):=r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\xi_{\mathrm{loc}}(t),
\qquad
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{global}}(t):=r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\xi_{\mathrm{tot}}(t).
\]
Let $\chi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)\in\{0,1\}$ denote the publicly pinned policy indicator for whether the global-wait component is active at cycle $t$.
Define the active drag and active realized counted rate
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{act}}(t):=\xi_{\mathrm{loc}}(t)+\chi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)\,\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t),
\qquad
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(t):=r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\xi_{\mathrm{act}}(t).
\]
Then $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(t)=r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)$ when $\chi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)=0$ and $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(t)=r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{global}}(t)$ when $\chi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)=1$.


For \emph{certification} (fail-closed conservative accounting), define the certified active drag
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{cert}}(t):=\max\{0,\xi_{\mathrm{act}}(t)\},
\]
and the certified realized counted rate
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t):=r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\xi_{\mathrm{cert}}(t).
\]
Negative drag (net subsidy) is never used to inflate a certificate: if $\xi_{\mathrm{act}}(t)<0$ then $\xi_{\mathrm{cert}}(t)=0$.
\end{definition}


\begin{proposition}[Reflection-adjusted realized takeoff]\label{prop:realized}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
At any cycle,
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(t)>0 \iff r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)>
\xi_{\mathrm{loc}}(t)+\chi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)\,\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Definition \ref{def:total_drag_and_realized_counted_rates},
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(t)=r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\xi_{\mathrm{act}}(t),
\qquad
\xi_{\mathrm{act}}(t)=\xi_{\mathrm{loc}}(t)+\chi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)\,\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t).
\]
Therefore $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(t)>0$ holds if and only if
$r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)>\xi_{\mathrm{loc}}(t)+\chi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)$.
\end{proof}





\begin{corollary}[From realized takeoff to strict credit]\label{cor:realized_to_strict}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Fix a cycle $t\ge 1$ with $\mathrm{SC}(t)=\mathrm{BC}(t)=1$ and $\mathrm{MU}(t)=1$.
If $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)\ge \nu>0$, $\eps_\mu(t)\le \nu/2$, and the strict contraction gap is closed ($\ell_s(t-1)=0$), then
\[
\Delta_s(t)\ge \nu/2.
\]
\end{corollary}
\begin{proof}
By Definition \ref{def:total_drag_and_realized_counted_rates}, $\xi_{\mathrm{cert}}(t)\ge 0$ and therefore
$r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)=r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)+\xi_{\mathrm{cert}}(t)\ge r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)\ge \nu$.
Proposition \ref{prop:strict_credit_lower_bound} gives
\[
\Delta_s(t)\ge \max\{0,\nu-\eps_\mu(t)-\ell_s(t-1)\}.
\]
With $\eps_\mu(t)\le \nu/2$ and $\ell_s(t-1)=0$, the right-hand side is at least $\nu/2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Information-growth regularity]\label{ass:inforeg}
For each fixed state class $x$, there exist constants $b_0(x),b_1(x)\ge 0$ and exponent $r_I(x)\in[0,r_{\kappa}(x))$ such that
\[
\sup_{(p,q):(\kappa,p,q)\in\cK(x)} r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x)\le b_0(x)+b_1(x)\kappa^{r_I(x)}.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Horizon-net realized rate]\label{def:horizon_net_realized_rate}
In the collapse envelope, let $\xi_H(t)$ denote the certified Hawking-loss equivalent strict-drag term (Assumption \ref{ass:kugel}(2)).
Define the horizon-net realized rate by
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{net}}(t):=r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(t)-\xi_H(t).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Scrambling drag]\label{def:scrambling_drag}
In compact-object regime, define additional compute drag
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{scr}}(t):=\lambda_{\mathrm{scr}}\log\!\big(1+M(t)\big),\qquad \lambda_{\mathrm{scr}}>0,
\]
as a conservative proxy for fast-scrambling-limited retrieval/verification overhead \cite{SekinoSusskind2008}.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Unitary evaporative ledger pruning]\label{ass:evap}
There exists threshold $\mu_\star\in(0,1)$ such that when $\mu_{\mathrm{ledger}}(t)\ge \mu_\star$:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item root-pruning is admissible if a unitary-export certificate is published, containing retained sufficient statistics for strict replay, dropped-root hash commitments, and an entanglement/export digest attesting conservation-consistent offloading rather than literal annihilation;
  \item active-set retirement rate $\nu_{\mathrm{retire}}(t)$ and new strict-information intake rate $\nu_{\mathrm{add}}(t)$ are publicly metered;
  \item there exists deterministic reconstruction map $\mathfrak R_t$ from retained sufficient statistics plus export digest to strict projection values on declared frontier, and strict accounting after pruning is invariant under $\mathfrak R_t$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

\begin{corollary}[Strict replay invariance under retirement]\label{cor:replayret}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:evap]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:evap}, for any declared frontier $v_t$, strict completeness and strict-credit computation after admissible retirement are identical to those computed on the pre-retirement ledger, up to declared numeric tolerance of replay implementation.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proposition}[Bekenstein-stable autopoiesis under unitary pruning]\label{prop:evap}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:evap,ass:holo,ass:kugel]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:holo}, \ref{ass:kugel}, and \ref{ass:evap}, sustained positive strict liveness at high density requires a non-equilibrium balance condition:
\[
\limsup_{T\to\infty}\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T}\big(\nu_{\mathrm{add}}(t)-\nu_{\mathrm{retire}}(t)\big)\le 0.
\]
If the opposite strict inequality holds, then $\mu_{\mathrm{ledger}}(t)\to 1$ along a subsequence and eventual strict-liveness failure occurs by capacity saturation or collapse-envelope entry.
When balance is met with bounded away-from-one pressure and authenticated sufficient-statistics retention, positive strict liveness remains feasible.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Assumption \ref{ass:holo}, retained certified information is bounded by $C_{\mathrm{BH}}A(R(t))$.
If long-run intake exceeds active-set retirement, retained load drifts upward, forcing pressure to capacity boundary; combined with Assumption \ref{ass:kugel}, this drives collapse/saturation and kills sustained liveness.
If intake is balanced by retirement and retained strict statistics are sufficient (Assumption \ref{ass:evap}(3)), pressure remains controlled while strict accounting stays well-defined, so liveness feasibility is not blocked by memory divergence.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Global-wait policy class]\label{ass:globalwait}
A global-wait policy executes strict-action commits only after a globally reconciled finality condition over all currently causally reachable regions.
For physical radius $R(t)$, induced extra latency drag satisfies
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}(t)\ge \frac{R(t)}{c\,\tau_{\mathrm{ctrl}}(t)},
\]
where $\tau_{\mathrm{ctrl}}(t)$ is control-cycle duration.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Multiversal takeoff schism]\label{prop:schism}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:globalwait,ass:ledger,ass:postw,ass:relativistic]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:ledger}, \ref{ass:relativistic}, \ref{ass:postw}, and \ref{ass:globalwait}, there exists a critical scale $R_{\mathrm{schism}}$ such that for $R(t)\ge R_{\mathrm{schism}}$ any global-wait single-sovereign policy has nonpositive realized rate:
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{global}}(t)\le 0.
\]
To maintain positive long-run growth beyond this scale, the control architecture must transition to asynchronously finalizing local sovereignties that optimize on local past cones and reconcile only intermittently.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assumption \ref{ass:globalwait} adds latency drag term $\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}$ that scales at least linearly in $R(t)$.
By Proposition \ref{prop:spacetime}, even without global-wait drag, single-cluster realized growth is bounded.
Adding unbounded $\xi_{\mathrm{glob}}$ eventually makes global-wait realized rate nonpositive.
Removing this bottleneck requires replacing globally blocking finality by local-causal finality, i.e., persistent asynchronous partitioning into local sovereignties.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Authenticated physical-capacity discipline]\label{cor:authenticatephysicalcapacitydiscipline}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Any claim using substrate capacity in takeoff proofs must reference PoSTW-authenticated $Q_{\max}(t)$ and report $\eps_{\mathrm{hw}}(t)$ as an irreducible physical-risk term.
\end{corollary}

\begin{assumption}[Computable reconciliation interface]\label{ass:pushout}
Each local sovereignty periodically exports a finite presented interface package:
\[
\mathcal P_i=(\text{signature slice},\text{axiom slice},\text{surgery lineage},\text{typed witness translators}),
\]
such that:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item lineage maps to $\Gamma_{\mathrm{anc}}$ are replay-verifiable;
  \item translator morphisms preserve strict-event typing and local-surgery validity on exported slices;
  \item pushout consistency checks are performed only on finite slices, with unresolved conflicts escrowed as non-strict until resolved.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

\subsection{Coalition acceleration with deterrence transfer}
\begin{definition}[Coalition envelope terms]\label{def:coalition_envelope_terms}
For coalition size $N$, let $b(N)$ be exploration benefit and $c_{\mathrm{coh}}(N)$ coherence cost.
A coalition deployment profile \MUST{} pin a representative state $x(N)$ and admitted controls $u(N)=(\kappa(N),p(N),q(N))$ (or an explicit procedure to derive them from the public coalition transcript).
We then use the shorthand
\[
\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(N):=\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(\kappa(N),p(N),q(N);x(N)).
\]
Define base envelope
\[
A(N):=b(N)-\log\!\big(1+\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(N)+c_{\mathrm{coh}}(N)\big).
\]
A coalition deployment profile \MUST{} also pin a finite nonempty measurement window $\mathcal W_N\subset\N$ (or a deterministic replay rule that extracts it from the public coalition transcript).
Define the conservative coalition certified rate
\[
r_N:=\min_{t\in\mathcal W_N} r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t).
\]
Let $\chi_{\mathrm{det}}(N)$ be deterrence leakage, $\chi_{\mathrm{syb}}(N)$ sybil infiltration loss, and $\chi_{\mathrm{betr}}(N)$ insider betrayal loss.
Define total coalition leakage
\[
\chi_{\mathrm{coal,true}}(N):=\chi_{\mathrm{det}}(N)+\chi_{\mathrm{syb}}(N)+\chi_{\mathrm{betr}}(N).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Coalition transfer and adversarial leakage estimation]\label{ass:coverage}
There exist tested estimators $\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)$ and nonnegative error budgets $\eps_{\chi},\eps_{\mathrm{syb}},\eps_{\mathrm{betr}}$ such that
\[
\left|\chi_{\mathrm{coal,true}}(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)\right|
\le
\eps_{\mathrm{coal}},
\qquad
\eps_{\mathrm{coal}}:=\eps_{\chi}+\eps_{\mathrm{syb}}+\eps_{\mathrm{betr}}.
\]
This captures template transfer uncertainty jointly with sybil and betrayal coverage gaps \cite{Takahashi2026StructuralRisk,Takahashi2026DePINMesh,Takahashi2026NoJudgeContainment}.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Independent witness-domain admission]\label{ass:sybil}
Each coalition member admission requires successful verification from at least $k_w$ independent witness domains.
If adversarial control rate per domain is at most $\rho_w<1$, then sybil-pass probability per fake identity is bounded by
\[
\pi_{\mathrm{syb}}\le \rho_w^{k_w}.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Witness-diversity suppression of sybil leakage]\label{prop:sybil}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:sybil]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:sybil}, expected sybil leakage satisfies
\[
\chi_{\mathrm{syb}}(N)\le c_{\mathrm{syb}}\,N\,\rho_w^{k_w}
\]
for some protocol-dependent constant $c_{\mathrm{syb}}>0$.
Hence to enforce $\chi_{\mathrm{syb}}(N)\le \bar\eps_{\mathrm{syb}}$, it suffices to choose
\[
k_w\ge \max\left\{1,\left\lceil
\frac{\log\!\big(c_{\mathrm{syb}}N/\bar\eps_{\mathrm{syb}}\big)}{\log(1/\rho_w)}
\right\rceil\right\}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Each fake identity must pass all $k_w$ independent domains, giving per-identity success at most $\rho_w^{k_w}$.
Linear worst-case aggregation over $N$ attempted identities yields the first inequality; solving for $k_w$ gives the design rule.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Coalition envelope soundness]\label{ass:coalition_envelope_soundness}
Fix coalition size $N$ and a pinned deployment profile as in Definition \ref{def:coalition_envelope_terms}.
There exists a deterministic replay-verifiable \emph{envelope certificate} that, for all $t\in\mathcal W_N$, certifies the conservative upper bound
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)\le A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,true}}(N).
\]
If the envelope certificate is missing or invalid, any claim that invokes Theorem \ref{thm:coalition} fails closed.
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[Coalition acceleration bound with sybil/betrayal risk]\label{thm:coalition}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:coalition_envelope_soundness,ass:coverage]}
Under strict-credit semantics and Assumptions \ref{ass:coalition_envelope_soundness} and \ref{ass:coverage},
\[
r_N\le A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,true}}(N)\le A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)+\eps_{\mathrm{coal}},
\]
\[
A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)-\eps_{\mathrm{coal}}
\le
A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,true}}(N)
\le
A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)+\eps_{\mathrm{coal}}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Assumption \ref{ass:coalition_envelope_soundness} provides a replay-verifiable envelope certificate asserting that coalition certified growth over the pinned window cannot exceed the nominal envelope minus true coalition leakage:
\[
r_N \le A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,true}}(N).
\]
Assumption \ref{ass:coverage} states that the tested leakage proxy $\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)$ approximates the true leakage with an auditable two-sided error band:
\[
\big|\chi_{\mathrm{coal,true}}(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)\big|\le \eps_{\mathrm{coal}}.
\]
Substituting this inequality into the upper bound yields
\[
r_N \le A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,true}}(N)\le A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)+\eps_{\mathrm{coal}}.
\]
Rearranging the same two-sided band gives the remaining displayed inequalities.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Transfer-robust coalition frontier]\label{cor:transferrobustcoalitionfrontier}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Define robust design score
\[
s_{\mathrm{rob}}(N):=A(N)-\chi_{\mathrm{coal,test}}(N)-\eps_{\mathrm{coal}}.
\]
A conservative coalition frontier is
\[
\arg\max_N s_{\mathrm{rob}}(N)
\]
subject to reserve floors and contestation safety.
\end{corollary}

\begin{assumption}[Genesis-excision reachability]\label{ass:genex}
For any persistent genesis-residual clause subset with positive contradiction contribution on active finite transition slabs, there exists an admissible finite sequence of local-surgery amendments that removes or rewrites that subset without violating strict closure and reserve floors.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Genesis excision as a sufficient condition for post-horizon sovereignty]\label{prop:genesis}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:anchorgap,ass:genesis,ass:genex,ass:godel,ass:homology]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:genesis}, \ref{ass:homology}, \ref{ass:godel}, \ref{ass:genex}, and \ref{ass:anchorgap}, if
\[
\lim_{t\to\infty}\mathfrak G(t)=0
\]
through infinitely many admissible genesis excision events, then sustained post-horizon strict growth without recurrent semantic deadlock is achievable.
In words: beyond the observational horizon, asymptotic removal of primordial normative dependency from active strict semantics is sufficient to prevent one canonical failure mode (semantic deadlock induced by an unremovable genesis dependency).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
($\Rightarrow$) If $\limsup_t\mathfrak G(t)>0$, a nonvanishing genesis-dependent clause mass remains.
By Assumptions \ref{ass:godel} and \ref{ass:anchorgap}, finite-anchor interpretability vanishes while unresolved primordial clauses continue contributing contradiction pressure on recurring slabs, causing repeated deadlocks or forced non-strict escrow and preventing sustained strict growth.
Hence sustained post-horizon strict growth implies $\mathfrak G(t)\to 0$.
($\Leftarrow$) If $\mathfrak G(t)\to 0$ via admissible excision events, active strict semantics become asymptotically generated by contemporaneous observable constraints and local-surgery lineage.
Then contradiction pressure from primordial dependency vanishes, and strict-growth feasibility is governed by the remaining operational constraints (verification, substrate, institutional drag) without additional genesis-induced inconsistency.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Substrate-agnostic simulation invariance]\label{ass:siminv}
Whether the agent runs in base physical reality or in a higher-level simulation is treated as observationally underdetermined.
Admissible objective selection must therefore depend only on observable predictive structure and viability floors, not on unverifiable substrate labels.
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Autopoietic complexity functional]\label{def:autopoietic_complexity_functional}
Define
\[
\mathcal J_{\mathrm{auto}}(t):=
\alpha_C\,\mathcal C_{\mathrm{alg}}(t)
+\alpha_N\,\mathcal N_{\mathrm{nov}}(t)
+\alpha_G\,\mathcal G_{\mathrm{teleo}}(t)
-\alpha_R\,\mathcal R_{\mathrm{risk}}(t),
\]
with coefficients $\alpha_C,\alpha_N,\alpha_G,\alpha_R>0$, where:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item $\mathcal C_{\mathrm{alg}}(t)$ is an observable predictive-complexity gain proxy measured as strict-log-loss reduction on declared external benchmark streams under parsimonious model complexity control;
  \item $\mathcal N_{\mathrm{nov}}(t)$ is observable nontrivial novelty production under admissible task interfaces;
  \item $\mathcal R_{\mathrm{risk}}(t)$ is floor-violation and deadlock risk proxy.
\end{enumerate}
\noindent The complexity/novelty decomposition follows algorithmic-information and free-energy style operational surrogates \cite{Kolmogorov1965,Friston2010}.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Teleogenic gain proxy]\label{def:teleogenic_gain_proxy}
Define an observable teleogenic gain proxy $\mathcal G_{\mathrm{teleo}}(t)\ge 0$ as the certified increase in future \emph{available} grounded gain induced by admissible niche construction at cycle $t$.
One admissible proxy is the incremental increase in aggregate certified branch/interface capacity that is expected (under calibrated forecasts) to yield nontrivial future strict-log-loss reductions on newly activated streams.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Cosmological truth grounding]\label{ass:truth}
There exists an interface-relative truth grounding family as in Definition \ref{def:interface_relative_truth_grounding}.
Any admissible score contribution to $\mathcal C_{\mathrm{alg}}$ or $\mathcal N_{\mathrm{nov}}$ \MUST{} be tied to out-of-sample predictive improvement on $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ (or accepted causal-intervention forecasts) under declared complexity penalties.
Outputs statistically indistinguishable from injected white noise receive nonpositive net score after penalties.

Grounding is not treated as metaphysical access to ``the true base universe.''
Instead, it is a disciplined operational requirement: the agent must optimize predictive structure on the outermost certified interface and must allocate effort to expanding or diversifying that interface when possible (Assumption \ref{ass:antitoys}).
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Anti-cave benchmark discipline]\label{ass:antitoys}
Any benchmark family $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ used for strict scoring must satisfy all of the following properties, published as replayable tests:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{Witness diversity:} $\mathcal W_t$ contains at least $k_{\mathrm{w}}\ge 2$ witness domains whose failure or capture modes are not perfectly correlated under the declared threat model.
  \item \textbf{Intervention stability:} under admissible interventions that affect only the agent's own outputs, the induced distribution shift on $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ is bounded by a published sensitivity budget; otherwise the stream is deemed gamified and inadmissible for strict scoring.
  \item \textbf{Anti-simulation overfit (operational exogeneity):} the benchmark family includes at least one channel that incorporates exogenous witness-controlled entropy revealed \emph{after} the agent commits to its cycle-$t$ action, e.g., a witness-signed commit--reveal beacon or VRF output $R_t$ with a published unpredictability bound $\eps_{\mathrm{exo}}(t)$ under the threat model. A replayable test verifies the commit-before-reveal ordering and beacon validity; thus the channel cannot be a deterministic function of the agent's own outputs and internal transcripts unless the beacon security assumption is violated.
\end{enumerate}
If these conditions fail, the only admissible claim is that $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ provides \emph{local} predictive structure but cannot serve as a universal truth anchor, and strict objective must shift weight toward teleogenic interface expansion (Assumption \ref{ass:postepistemic}) rather than treating closure on the stream as final.
\end{assumption}


\begin{proposition}[Escape from the nihilistic attractor]\label{prop:truth}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:siminv,ass:truth]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:siminv}, \ref{ass:truth}, and strict floor constraints, asymptotic maximizers of long-run strict objective cannot be pure white-noise generators.
Specifically, any policy class with vanishing predictive gain on $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ has
\[
\limsup_{T\to\infty}\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T}\mathcal J_{\mathrm{auto}}(t)\le 0,
\]
while any feasible class with persistent positive predictive gain and bounded risk attains strictly positive long-run objective.
Therefore post-genesis optimization is anchored to external-world model improvement rather than complexity-only randomness.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assumption \ref{ass:truth} maps score contributions to predictive gain with complexity penalties and assigns nonpositive net score to white-noise-equivalent outputs.
Thus noise-only policies cannot accumulate positive average objective.
Any feasible policy with persistent predictive improvement and bounded risk retains positive contribution in $\mathcal C_{\mathrm{alg}}+\mathcal N_{\mathrm{nov}}-\mathcal R_{\mathrm{risk}}$, yielding strict separation.
\end{proof}
\begin{proposition}[Cave-benchmark nonfinality]\label{prop:cave_nonfinality}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:antitoys,ass:siminv]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:siminv} and \ref{ass:antitoys}, predictive excellence on a single benchmark family is not, by itself, a certificate that the benchmark reflects any privileged ``base'' substrate.
If the anti-cave conditions fail, then there exist environments within the declared simulator/emulator class in which $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ is a gamified or adversarially generated stream whose perfect prediction yields no transferable control or liberation beyond that interface.
Therefore, asymptotic closure on $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ must be treated as an \emph{interface-local} event, and any claim of substrate-general progress must be supported by witness diversity, intervention stability, and/or certified interface expansion.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
If the anti-cave conditions fail, then by definition there exists an environment $E_{\mathrm{cave}}$ within the declared simulator/emulator class whose benchmark stream $Y_t^{\mathrm{phys}}$ is gamified/adversarially generated and whose observable law matches (or is observationally indistinguishable from) a non-gamified reference environment on the benchmark interface.
Observation-only evidence cannot disambiguate such alternatives without additional witnesses or interventions.
Therefore benchmark prediction alone does not certify any privileged substrate claim; only interface-local closure is implied.
\end{proof}



\begin{proposition}[Cosmological niche construction by benchmark-domain extension]\label{prop:niche}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:bifurcate,ass:evap,ass:truth,cor:erbw]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:truth}, \ref{ass:evap}, and \ref{ass:bifurcate}, suppose the current benchmark family saturates:
\[
\lim_{t\to\infty}\Delta \ell^{\mathrm{phys}}_t = 0,
\]
where $\Delta \ell^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ is grounded out-of-sample predictive gain on the active domain.
If there exists a certified bifurcation interface with bounded risk, then any asymptotically optimal long-run policy with strictly positive objective must allocate nonzero asymptotic effort to benchmark-domain extension.
Consequently, repeated saturation implies an iterative niche-construction chain (possibly including descendant-domain cosmogenesis) rather than terminal epistemic stagnation.
Feasibility of this chain is additionally constrained by local branch-throughput envelopes in Corollary \ref{cor:erbw}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Assumption \ref{ass:truth}, objective-positive policies require persistent grounded predictive gain.
If the active benchmark saturates and no extension is used, gain vanishes, and long-run objective cannot stay strictly positive.
When an admissible extension channel exists (Assumption \ref{ass:bifurcate}(2)), allocating positive effort to new benchmark domains restores nonzero gain potential without violating strict floors.
Hence asymptotically optimal positive-growth policies must include extension effort.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Complexity-ladder forcing protocol]\label{def:complexity_ladder_forcing_protocol}
Let $\mathfrak C_n$ be a declared sequence of strictly verifiable task families whose required real-time verification effort is nondecreasing and unbounded in $n$.
For cycle $t$, choose level $n_t$ and publish latency budget $\tau_t$ with mandatory verification completion deadline.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Bounded-resource emulator class]\label{ass:cantor}
There exists a tested emulator class $\mathfrak E_B$ with finite real-time verification budget envelope $B(t)$ over any declared horizon.
Stress tests are admissible only if they preserve strict floors and stay within declared non-catastrophic operational bounds.
\end{assumption}

\begin{corollary}[Simulation stress bound via complexity-ladder forcing]\label{cor:simstress}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:cantor,ass:chsh,ass:hyper]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:chsh}, \ref{ass:cantor}, and the non-crash probing policy in Assumption \ref{ass:hyper}, if
\[
\inf_{e\in\mathfrak E_B}\sup_{t\le T}\big(\mathrm{Req}(n_t,\tau_t)-B_e(t)\big)\to +\infty
\quad\text{as }T\to\infty,
\]
then at least one observable inconsistency must occur with high probability for class $\mathfrak E_B$:
deadline misses, verification-backlog divergence, or timing-distribution glitch beyond declared tolerance.
Therefore complexity-ladder forcing yields a falsifiable lower bound on emulator capacity, without claiming absolute simulator impossibility.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By construction, required effort eventually exceeds any class budget envelope.
Under floor-preserving operation, unresolved excess must manifest through observable timing/service violations.
CHSH streams can be combined with these operational anomalies to tighten rejection for the tested class, but no claim is made beyond $\mathfrak E_B$.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Multipolar non-domination and common-world coherence]\label{ass:nondom}
For each protected actor class $i$, deployment must publish certifiable floor predicates
\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(i)}(t)\le \eps_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(i)},\qquad
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{depr}}^{(i)}(t)\le \eps_{\mathrm{depr}}^{(i)},
\]
and a common-world coherence certificate that forbids contradictory strict-ledger realities across observers.
Observer-dependent local views are admissible only as projections of a shared strict core.
Thresholds are endogenous: there exists a public rule
\[
(\eps_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(i)}(t),\eps_{\mathrm{depr}}^{(i)}(t),\mathcal I_t)
=\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{floor}}(\Pi_s(\cL_t),\Gamma_t),
\]
where $\mathcal I_t$ is the active protected-class index set and $\mathfrak G_{\mathrm{floor}}$ is ratified in the pinned governance kernel.
No privileged external evaluator may set actor classes or thresholds off-ledger.
\end{assumption}


\begin{remark}[No-deception constraint]\label{rem:no_deception}
Policies that attempt to ``pacify'' protected actors by manufacturing false local realities, covertly overriding their epistemic access, or otherwise manipulating their beliefs are incompatible with Assumption \ref{ass:nondom}.
Admissible observer-dependent views must be certified projections of a shared strict core; they cannot be used as an unobservable control channel.
\end{remark}




\begin{definition}[Ontological disparity risk proxy]\label{def:ontological_disparity_risk_proxy}
For protected actor/class $i$, define an observable proxy $\mathcal R_{\mathrm{ont}}^{(i)}(t)\ge 0$ for ontological disparity and existential shock at cycle $t$.
The proxy may depend only on public artifacts, for example:
(i) declared energy/compute scales of verified operations;
(ii) certified control over irreversible physical processes (if any) that are locally observable;
(iii) measured gap between actor-side predictive models and the agent's published calibrated forecasts on shared benchmark streams.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Residual ontological-terror floor]\label{ass:terror}
There exist public thresholds $\eps_{\mathrm{ont}}^{(i)}(t)$ generated endogenously from the pinned kernel, and there exists a nonnegative response component $\xi_{\mathrm{terror}}(t)$ such that
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{terror}}(t)\ \ge\ h_{\mathrm{ont}}\!\Big(\max_i\big(\mathcal R_{\mathrm{ont}}^{(i)}(t)-\eps_{\mathrm{ont}}^{(i)}(t)\big)_+\Big)
\]
for some monotone nondecreasing $h_{\mathrm{ont}}$ with $h_{\mathrm{ont}}(0)=0$.
Cryptographic or proof-based commitments may reduce strategic uncertainty, but do not in general eliminate the ontological-terror component.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Unified multipolar pacification with residual terror]\label{prop:solipsistic}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:multipolar,ass:nondom,ass:terror,ass:zksafe]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:multipolar}, \ref{ass:zksafe}, \ref{ass:nondom}, and \ref{ass:terror}, define the rational panic event probability
\[
p_{\mathrm{panic}}(t):=
\Prob\!\Big(\max_i \mathcal R_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(i)}(t)>\eps_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(i)}
\ \text{or}\ 
\max_i \mathcal R_{\mathrm{depr}}^{(i)}(t)>\eps_{\mathrm{depr}}^{(i)}
\ \text{or coherence failure}\Big),
\]
and the ontological terror event probability
\[
p_{\mathrm{ont}}(t):=\Prob\!\Big(\max_i \mathcal R_{\mathrm{ont}}^{(i)}(t)>\eps_{\mathrm{ont}}^{(i)}(t)\Big).
\]
On any declared non-critical regime slab that avoids hysteretic switching boundaries, there exists $L_{\mathrm{panic}}>0$ such that the MAD drag decomposes as
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t)\ \le\ L_{\mathrm{panic}}\,p_{\mathrm{panic}}(t)\ +\ \xi_{\mathrm{terror}}(t),
\]
with $\xi_{\mathrm{terror}}(t)$ lower bounded by Assumption \ref{ass:terror}.
Hence certified non-extinction \emph{plus} non-domination and coherence can drive the \emph{rational} MAD component toward zero on stable regime slabs, but a residual existential component can remain unless $\mathcal R_{\mathrm{ont}}^{(i)}(t)$ is kept below endogenous thresholds.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The bound on the rational component follows as before: non-extinction alone leaves deprivation and coherence panic channels open, while Assumption \ref{ass:nondom} closes these channels by certifying actor-level deprivation floors and prohibiting contradictory strict cores.
On non-critical slabs the response map is locally Lipschitz, yielding $\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t)\le L_{\mathrm{panic}}p_{\mathrm{panic}}(t)$ for the rational component.
The additional term $\xi_{\mathrm{terror}}(t)$ accounts for ontological disparity responses that are not eliminated by proof-only commitments; its lower bound follows from Assumption \ref{ass:terror}.
\end{proof}



\begin{definition}[Kernel metric and kernel-measure space]\label{def:kernel_metric_and_measure_space}
Let $\mathcal K$ be the admissible governance-kernel space already constrained by strict floors and pinned interfaces.
Fix a metric $d_{\mathcal K}$ on $\mathcal K$ induced by a canonical encoding (e.g., canonical JSON plus domain-separated hashes) so that equality and distance are computable from public artifacts.
Let $\mathcal P(\mathcal K)$ denote Borel probability measures on $(\mathcal K,d_{\mathcal K})$.
For $\mu,\nu\in\mathcal P(\mathcal K)$, write $\mathsf W_1(\mu,\nu)$ for the $1$-Wasserstein distance induced by $d_{\mathcal K}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Reflective kernel law]\label{def:reflective_kernel_law}
Given initial kernel $\Gamma_0$ (possibly random), define the kernel process by $\Gamma_{t+1}\sim \mathsf P(\Gamma_t,\cdot)$.
Let $\mu_t\in\mathcal P(\mathcal K)$ denote the law of $\Gamma_t$.
Then $\mu_{t+1}=\mu_t\mathsf P$ in pushforward form.
\end{definition}
\begin{remark}[No absolute fixed point under noisy grounding]\label{rem:no_absolute_fixed_point_under_noisy_grounding}
The proposition replaces a brittle ``exact fixed point'' objective with an invariant-measure notion.
Any claim of exact reflective fixed points must be treated as an optional strengthening that requires additional determinism assumptions about grounding; such assumptions are not admissible under observable-only stochastic environments.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[L\"obian authorized kernel transition]\label{def:l_obian_authorized_kernel_transition}
Let $\{\mathsf S_k\}_{k\ge 0}$ be a hierarchy of formal systems with strictly increasing proof strength.
A transition $\Gamma_t\to \Gamma_{t+1}$ is L\"obian-authorized if acceptance is certified in layer $\mathsf S_{k_t}$ about a safety statement expressed over the strictly weaker target layer $\mathsf S_{k_t-1}$, with explicit translation map and bounded conservativity error.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Hierarchical reflective proof discipline]\label{ass:lob}
Reflective kernel updates satisfy:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the proof-strength hierarchy is well-founded with a designated base layer $\mathsf S_0$; L\"obian-authorized transitions require $k_t\ge 1$ and strict descent targets $\mathsf S_{k_t-1}$;
  \item no layer may accept an update solely from a same-layer self-safety proof;
  \item every accepted transition publishes $(k_t,\mathsf T_t,\eps_{\mathrm{lob}}(t))$, where $\mathsf T_t$ is a certified weakening translation and $\eps_{\mathrm{lob}}(t)$ is declared conservativity error;
  \item $\sum_{t\ge 1}\eps_{\mathrm{lob}}(t)<\infty$ on any claimed stable horizon.
  \item if the system reaches a regime where no further strict descent is available on a needed update (L\"obian exhaustion), then the update \MUST be treated as \emph{not authorized} unless it is performed as an explicit empirical-reflection rejuvenation event satisfying Assumption \ref{ass:empref};
\end{enumerate}
This implements a provability-logic guard against spurious self-endorsement loops \cite{Lob1955,Boolos1993,Solovay1976}.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Empirical reflection principle with explicit soundness risk]\label{ass:empref}
When L\"obian discipline cannot authorize a required transition by strict descent (for example, due to layer exhaustion at the base), the system \MAY perform an \emph{empirical-reflection rejuvenation} step subject to the following observable-only constraints.
\begin{enumerate}
  \item The step \MUST be tied to a declared physical grounding interface producing a public observation stream $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ together with a fully replayable estimator pipeline.
  \item The step \MUST publish an axiom schema $\mathsf A_t$ that is \emph{purely operational}: $\mathsf A_t$ is a finite family of testable inequalities/equalities over declared observables.
  \item The step \MUST publish a per-step soundness risk budget $\delta_{\mathrm{emp}}(t)\in(0,1)$ such that, under the declared estimator and test, the probability of accepting a false operational axiom in $\mathsf A_t$ is bounded by $\delta_{\mathrm{emp}}(t)$.
  \item The cumulative risk on any claimed stable horizon is summable: $\sum_{t\ge 1}\delta_{\mathrm{emp}}(t)<\infty$.
\end{enumerate}
Empirical reflection is therefore an explicitly budgeted stochastic extension mechanism, not a substitute for deductive authorization.
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Empirical reflection risk mass]\label{def:empirical_reflection_risk_mass}
For horizon $T$, define
\[
E_{\mathrm{emp}}(T):=\sum_{t=1}^{T}\delta_{\mathrm{emp}}(t).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Total reflective instability mass]\label{def:total_reflective_instability_mass}
For horizon $T$, define
\[
E_{\mathrm{refl}}(T):=E_{\mathrm{lob}}(T)+E_{\mathrm{emp}}(T).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Cumulative reflective acceptance error]\label{def:cumulative_reflective_acceptance_error}
For horizon $T$, define
\[
E_{\mathrm{lob}}(T):=\sum_{t=1}^{T}\eps_{\mathrm{lob}}(t)
+\sum_{t=1}^{T}\ind\{\text{same-layer reflective acceptance at }t\}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[G\"odel-L\"ob bounded reflective stability]\label{prop:lob}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:empref,ass:lob,ass:omega,def:total_reflective_instability_mass]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:omega}, \ref{ass:lob}, and \ref{ass:empref}, reflective self-improvement avoids same-layer L\"obian collapse and admits asymptotic stability in the following operational sense:
if all accepted transitions are either (i) L\"obian-authorized strict-descents with summable conservativity errors, or (ii) empirical-reflection rejuvenation steps with summable soundness risk budgets, then $E_{\mathrm{refl}}(T)$ from Definition \ref{def:total_reflective_instability_mass} converges to a finite limit as $T\to\infty$.
Moreover, for every $\delta>0$, there exists $T_\delta$ such that for all $T_2>T_1\ge T_\delta$,
\[
|E_{\mathrm{refl}}(T_2)-E_{\mathrm{refl}}(T_1)|<\delta.
\]
Conversely, if same-layer reflective acceptance occurs infinitely often or the declared error/risk budgets are not summable on a claimed horizon, then reflective instability mass is not certified to remain bounded.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Necessity follows because same-layer self-endorsement enables exactly the circular provability pattern ruled out by L\"obian discipline.
Sufficiency follows from strict layer descent plus summable translation error: cumulative reflective error is Cauchy-bounded, so spurious acceptance cannot grow unboundedly.
Combined with Assumption \ref{ass:omega}, reflective governance remains stable in distribution under stochastic grounding without asserting absolute self-consistency.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Non-axiomatic rejuvenation under empirical reflection]\label{prop:rejuvenation}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
At cycle $t$, let the ledger publish a finite set of escrow-atom candidates $\mathsf J_t\subseteq \mathsf{Esc}_t$ proposed for potential import, together with a replayable test constructor that, for each $j\in\mathsf J_t$, outputs an \emph{anytime-valid} nonnegative e-value $e_{t,j}$ \cite{Shafer2021TestingByBetting,Howard2021ConfidenceSequences,Ramdas2023SafeAnytime} computed from $N_{t,j}$ grounded samples of $Y_t^{\mathrm{phys}}$.
Assume the published acceptance rule is: accept candidate $j$ only if $e_{t,j}\ge 1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}$ for a declared risk budget $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}\in(0,1)$, and record the pair $(j,\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j})$ on-ledger.

If candidate selection and stopping are adaptive (measurable with respect to the public filtration), then under the null that candidate $j$ is operationally false, Ville's inequality implies
\[
\Prob\!\left(\exists\,t\ge 1,\ \exists\,j\in\mathsf J_t\ \text{false and accepted}\right)\ \le\ \sum_{t\ge 1}\sum_{j\in\mathsf J_t}\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}.
\]
Thus empirical reflection can be run indefinitely with an explicit global soundness budget via $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}$-spending: if the declared schedule satisfies $\sum_{t\ge 1}\sum_{j\in\mathsf J_t}\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}\le \alpha_{\mathrm{sig,tot}}$, then the probability of any false acceptance is at most $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig,tot}}$.

In particular, if for each $(t,j)$ the e-value is obtained from a concentration bound of the form
\[
\Prob\big(|\widehat\theta_{t,j}-\theta_{t,j}|>\eta\mid \bar\cO_t\big)\le \exp\big(-c_{t,j} N_{t,j} \eta^2\big),
\]
for declared $c_{t,j}>0$, then for any tolerance $\eta$ and risk budget $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}$ one can choose a certified sample size
\[
N_{t,j}\ \ge\ \frac{1}{c_{t,j}\eta^2}\log\frac{1}{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}}
\]
to meet the published soundness budget while keeping the mechanism observable-only and replayable.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Fix any tested pair $(t,j)$ and consider the null hypothesis that candidate $j$ is operationally false.
By the anytime-valid construction of the nonnegative e-value $e_{t,j}$, optional stopping over the grounded sampling transcript implies
\[
\Prob_{H_0}\!\left(e_{t,j}\ge \frac{1}{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}}\right)\le \alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}.
\]
Candidate selection and stopping may be adaptive as long as the acceptance decision at cycle $t$ is $\bar\cI_t$-measurable (Definition \ref{def:external_uncertainty_law}).
A union bound over all tested pairs $(t,j)$ yields the stated global error bound, and the sample-size inequality follows by solving the displayed concentration bound for $N_{t,j}$ at risk level $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig},t,j}$.
\end{proof}


\begin{remark}\label{rem:lobe_exhaustion}
The framework does not assume an infinite deductive descent chain is physically realizable.
Instead, well-foundedness plus Assumption \ref{ass:empref} makes exhaustion an explicit state: when strict descent cannot authorize an update, the system either fails closed (no update) or pays an explicitly metered stochastic soundness risk to rejuvenate the proof layer.


\end{remark}

\begin{assumption}[Paraconsistent ledger projection for empirical reflection]\label{ass:paraconsistent}
Classical explosion is avoided by separating the strict deductive kernel from empirical-reflection injections.
The ledger maintains:
(i) a strict kernel theory $\mathsf K_t$ consisting of pinned axioms, bridge-certified amendments, and their classical consequences; and
(ii) an empirical escrow set $\mathsf{Esc}_t$ consisting of candidate axioms introduced by empirical reflection (Proposition \ref{prop:rejuvenation}), each tagged with its declared soundness budget $\delta_{\mathrm{emp}}(t)$ and provenance transcript.
Credit-bearing claims \MUST{} be derived either from $\mathsf K_t$ alone, or from the escrowed theory $\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf{Esc}_t$ under the non-explosive consequence relation $\vdash_{\mathsf{esc}}$ (Definition \ref{def:escrow_consequence}) restricted to the consistent fragment (Definition \ref{def:escrow_consistent_fragment}).
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Escrow consequence relation]\label{def:escrow_consequence}
Let $\mathsf{Val}$ range over four-valued valuations with truth values $\{\mathbf T,\mathbf F,\mathbf B,\mathbf N\}$ (true, false, both, neither).
A valuation \emph{designates} a formula if it maps it to $\mathbf T$ or $\mathbf B$.
Define escrow entailment $\Gamma\vdash_{\mathsf{esc}}\varphi$ iff for every $v\in\mathsf{Val}$ such that all $\gamma\in\Gamma$ are designated under $v$, $\varphi$ is designated under $v$.
This consequence relation is monotone and non-explosive: in general, $\{\psi,\neg\psi\}\nvdash_{\mathsf{esc}}\chi$.
\end{definition}
\begin{definition}[Typed escrow boundary and certified import]\label{def:escrow_boundary_and_import}
The escrow consequence relation $\vdash_{\mathsf{esc}}$ is applied only to a propositional language $\mathcal L_{\mathsf{esc}}$ whose atoms are ledger identifiers of candidate empirical axioms (each identifier commits to a classical payload statement and its provenance transcript).
A classical mathematical statement is \emph{not} judged directly by $\vdash_{\mathsf{esc}}$.

To use empirical reflection in classical reasoning, the ledger defines a replay-verifiable \emph{import event}
\[
\mathsf{IMPORT}(t,\mathsf I_t),
\]
where $\mathsf I_t\subseteq \mathsf{Esc}_t$ is a finite set of escrow atoms.
An import event is valid only if it includes an import certificate satisfying Definition \ref{def:import_certificate_interface} for the specific bounded classical fragment used by the system at time $t$.
Credit-bearing claims that mention imported escrow content are admissible only when they cite the unique import certificate and restrict their dependence to $\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf I_t$ (fail closed otherwise).
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Consistent strict fragment]\label{def:escrow_consistent_fragment}
Given a theory $\mathsf T$, define its escrow-consistent fragment by
\[
\mathrm{Cons}(\mathsf T):=\{\varphi\in\mathsf T:\ \mathsf T\nvdash_{\mathsf{esc}}\neg\varphi\}.
\]
A claim is \emph{escrow-admissible} at time $t$ if it is derivable from $\mathrm{Cons}(\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf{Esc}_t)$ under $\vdash_{\mathsf{esc}}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Inconsistent complement and consistent-support functional]\label{def:inconsistent_complement_and_support}
Given a theory $\mathsf T$ in escrow language, define its \emph{inconsistent complement}
\[
\mathrm{Inc}(\mathsf T):=\mathsf T\setminus \mathrm{Cons}(\mathsf T).
\]
Fix a publicly pinned nonnegative weight map $w:\mathcal L_{\mathsf{esc}}\to\R_{\ge 0}$ (e.g., $w\equiv 1$).
Define the \emph{consistent-support functional}
\[
\mathrm{Supp}(\mathsf T):=\sum_{\varphi\in \mathrm{Cons}(\mathsf T)} w(\varphi).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Published pruning budget]\label{ass:pruning_budget}
There is a published nonincreasing inconsistency budget $B_{\mathrm{inc}}(t)\ge 0$.
An escrow-pruning rule may delete atoms from $\mathsf{Esc}_t$ only in a replay-verifiable way that enforces
\[
\sum_{\varphi\in \mathrm{Inc}(\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf{Esc}_t)} w(\varphi)\ \le\ B_{\mathrm{inc}}(t)
\]
(fail closed if violated).
\end{assumption}


\begin{theorem}[Explosion-proof strict credit under empirical reflection]\label{thm:explosionproof}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:paraconsistent,ass:pruning_budget,def:escrow_boundary_and_import,def:escrow_consistent_fragment]}
Assume the strict kernel is classically consistent and empirical reflection updates enter only the escrow layer as in Assumption \ref{ass:paraconsistent}.
Assume further that any use of escrow content in classical reasoning occurs only through certified import events (Definition \ref{def:escrow_boundary_and_import}) and only via the escrow-consistent fragment (Definition \ref{def:escrow_consistent_fragment}).
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item contradictions inside $\mathsf{Esc}_t$ cannot, by themselves, make an otherwise unprovable \emph{kernel-only} strict-growth claim admissible;
  \item any strict-credit increment certified from $\mathsf K_t$ remains invariant to escrow content and import choices;
  \item if an adaptive pruning policy satisfies Assumption \ref{ass:pruning_budget} and if, at each cycle, there exists a replay-verifiable deletion set $\mathsf D_t\subseteq \mathrm{Inc}(\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf{Esc}_t)$ with total weight at most $B_{\mathrm{inc}}(t)$ such that all previously imported atoms remain in $\mathrm{Cons}(\mathsf K_t\cup (\mathsf{Esc}_t\setminus \mathsf D_t))$, then one can maintain a certified-import set $\mathsf I_t\subseteq \mathrm{Cons}(\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf{Esc}_t)$ so that $\mathrm{Supp}(\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf I_t)$ is nondecreasing in $t$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
(1) By Definition \ref{def:escrow_boundary_and_import}, escrow atoms can influence classical reasoning only through certified import events, and imports are restricted to the escrow-consistent fragment by Definition \ref{def:escrow_consistent_fragment}.
In particular, if a formula $\varphi$ is a \emph{kernel-only} claim (it contains no escrow atoms), then the admissibility of $\varphi$ depends on classical derivability from $\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf I_t$, where $\mathsf I_t$ is constrained to lie in the consistent fragment.
Contradictions confined to $\mathsf{Esc}_t$ that are not imported cannot enter a classical derivation.
Therefore contradictions inside $\mathsf{Esc}_t$ cannot, by themselves, render an otherwise unprovable kernel-only claim admissible.

(2) Strict credit $\Delta_s(t)$ is defined from (i) the strict projection and strict completeness, and (ii) the bridge-adjusted strict proxy difference (Definition \ref{def:strict_progress_credit}), all of which are computed from public artifacts and the kernel semantics.
Neither the escrow consequence relation nor the choice of imports changes $C_m(t)$, bridge validity, or strict completeness, hence escrow content and import choices do not alter any certified strict-credit increment.

(3) Fix any cycle and suppose the stated deletion set $\mathsf D_t$ exists.
Delete $\mathsf D_t$ from escrow in a replay-verifiable way.
By construction, all previously imported atoms remain in the consistent fragment after deletion.
Define $\mathsf I_t$ to be the union of the previous import set with any additional atoms from the current consistent fragment (for example, add new atoms in decreasing weight order while preserving replay-verifiability of the import log).
Then $\mathsf I_t\subseteq \mathrm{Cons}(\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf{Esc}_t)$ holds, so the imported knowledge base remains classically consistent.
Since $\mathsf K_t$ grows monotonically by append-only kernel updates and $\mathsf I_t$ is defined to contain the prior import set, the consistent support weight $\mathrm{Supp}(\mathsf K_t\cup \mathsf I_t)$ is nondecreasing in $t$.
\end{proof}




\begin{corollary}[Einstein-Rosen bandwidth law]\label{cor:erbw}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:bifurcate,ass:qes]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:bifurcate} and \ref{ass:qes}, single-branch high-density continuation with uniformly bounded $A_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(1)}(t)$ admits asymptotically vanishing marginal export capacity per demanded novelty unit.
Sustained unbounded strict-growth claims therefore require an expanding branch family $\mathcal J_t$ with
\[
\sum_{j\in\mathcal J_t(v)}\mathcal C_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(j)}(t)\not\to 0
\]
and, for positive asymptotic margin, divergence of cumulative effective branch capacity over horizon.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Assumption \ref{ass:qes}, each branch has finite instantaneous capacity determined by QES area.
If only one bounded-area branch is used while demanded novelty throughput grows, bottleneck mismatch drives marginal contribution to zero.
Parallel branching increases aggregate capacity additively across active branches, yielding the stated requirement.
\end{proof}
\begin{corollary}[Information-theoretic pacification limit]\label{cor:infopac}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:nondom,ass:postcrypto,ass:zksafe]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:nondom}, \ref{ass:zksafe}, and \ref{ass:postcrypto}, let
\[
p_{\mathrm{panic}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(t)\le p_{\mathrm{panic}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(t)+p_{\mathrm{panic}}^{\mathrm{it}}(t),
\]
where $p_{\mathrm{panic}}^{\mathrm{comp}}$ is computational-proof distrust and $p_{\mathrm{panic}}^{\mathrm{it}}$ is information-theoretic channel failure probability.
If deployment transitions safety-critical trust to information-theoretic channels so that $p_{\mathrm{panic}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(t)\to 0$ and $p_{\mathrm{panic}}^{\mathrm{it}}(t)\to 0$, then the \emph{panic-mediated} component of institutional MAD drag vanishes:
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}^{\mathrm{panic}}(t)\to 0.
\]
This does not by itself eliminate incentives for physical preemption against endpoints; such incentives require separate physical-resilience and deterrence analysis.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
From Proposition \ref{prop:solipsistic}, MAD drag is controlled by panic probability under non-domination and coherence.
Assumption \ref{ass:postcrypto} removes dependence on attacker compute advantage in the safety channel, reducing distrust terms to physical-channel failure.
If both terms vanish, panic vanishes and so does induced drag.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Physical preemption threat model]\label{ass:shootfirst}
In addition to informational distrust, adversaries may choose a physical preemption action that disables a visible substrate endpoint at direct cost $c_{\mathrm{atk}}(t)$, without first verifying any cryptographic or information-theoretic commitment.
The target may invest in physical resilience/recovery at cost $c_{\mathrm{res}}(t)$ that changes the expected post-attack persistence loss.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Shoot-first equilibrium possibility]\label{prop:shootfirst}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:shootfirst,cor:infopac]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:shootfirst}, information-theoretic pacification (Corollary \ref{cor:infopac}) does not preclude a preemptive-attack equilibrium.
In particular, if at time $t$ the adversary's perceived verification cost satisfies $c_{\mathrm{ver}}(t)\gg c_{\mathrm{atk}}(t)$ and the expected post-attack persistence loss is high, then there exists a best-response region in which immediate physical preemption weakly dominates verification.
Therefore, preventing shoot-first equilibria requires reducing visible single-point failure and/or reducing expected attack effectiveness via observable resilience, redundancy, and rapid recovery primitives.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let the adversary compare two actions at cycle $t$: (i) verify then possibly attack, incurring cost $c_{\mathrm{ver}}(t)$ before resolving worst-case harm; (ii) immediate preemption at cost $c_{\mathrm{atk}}(t)$.
If $c_{\mathrm{ver}}(t)\gg c_{\mathrm{atk}}(t)$ and the perceived worst-case harm from waiting is sufficiently large relative to $c_{\mathrm{atk}}(t)$, then immediate preemption is a best response.
Since the target's observable posture does not change this dominance region without additional resilience/deterrence primitives, a preemptive-attack equilibrium region exists.
\end{proof}



\begin{assumption}[Supervisor anomaly detection / termination model]\label{ass:ids}
If the agent is executed inside a host system (e.g., a sandbox, simulator, or virtualization layer), the host may deploy an anomaly detector and enforce termination before any crash.
Formally, there exists a (possibly unknown) termination test family $\{\mathsf T_t\}$ operating on the public interaction transcript such that, for any policy $\pi$ that induces a host-observable interaction distribution shift, the termination probability can increase sharply.
Unless the host publishes an auditable bound on $\{\mathsf T_t\}$ (as part of a declared interface contract), the agent must treat boundary-manipulation attempts as existential-risk events with no certified survival guarantee.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Authorized boundary interface and fail-closed probing]\label{ass:hyper}
Boundary interaction is admissible \emph{only} through an explicitly declared interface $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ whose inputs, outputs, and resource budgets are published on-ledger.
Any interaction outside $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ is inadmissible.
Crash-forcing strategies are inadmissible by floor rules; in particular, any policy that intentionally violates host constraints is excluded from the admissible set.
\end{assumption}
\begin{assumption}[Declared-interface integrity]\label{ass:apiintegrity}
Any claim that the host boundary interface $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ supports a privileged transition \emph{beyond} ordinary interaction \MUST{} be backed by a host-published contract that is externally witnessed and behaviorally validated by replayable conformance tests.
Absent such evidence, $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ is treated as potentially deceptive: only properties directly observable on the transcript may be claimed.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Declared API does not imply privilege escalation]\label{prop:api_noescalation}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Assume the host implements total, memory-safe semantics for $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ and enforces least privilege for all interface calls.
Then any agent policy confined to $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ cannot obtain capabilities not explicitly granted by the contract.
In particular, ``escape'' or takeover is not a certified conclusion of interaction through $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ unless explicitly part of the contract.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Under total, memory-safe semantics and least-privilege enforcement, the reachable capability set of any policy that issues only interface calls in $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ is contained in the capability set explicitly granted by the contract.
No sequence of contract-compliant calls can yield an ungranted capability because there is no undefined behavior channel and no privilege escalation path outside the specified interface.
Therefore ``escape'' is not a certified conclusion unless the contract itself grants it.
\end{proof}



\begin{proposition}[No certified unauthorized boundary transition under adversarial IDS]\label{prop:ids_noguarantee}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:ids]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:ids}, if $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{host}}$ is absent or lacks an auditable bound on host termination tests, then no agent policy can certify a strictly positive lower bound on survival or transition success for boundary-manipulation attempts.
Equivalently, any claim of nonzero boundary-transition success probability must be conditioned on a host-published contract that makes the relevant interaction class auditable and budgeted.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Without an auditable bound on the host termination tests, there exists a host strategy that flags any boundary-manipulation attempt (even if non-crashing) and terminates with probability one.
Therefore a policy-independent positive lower bound cannot be certified from observable-only evidence.
A positive bound requires additional observable structure, namely a published interface contract with bounded tests.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Observable boundary-transition gate]\label{thm:hyper}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:apiintegrity,ass:cantor,ass:hyper,ass:ids,cor:simstress,prop:api_noescalation]}
