\subsection{Higher-categorical reconciliation interfaces (optional)}
\paragraph{Speculative extension: higher-categorical reconciliation interfaces.}
The following results use categorical abstractions as \emph{interfaces} for reconciliation under ontology drift. They should be read as design patterns for building conservative fallbacks, not as claims that such structures are uniquely realized in any given substrate.

\begin{proposition}[Conditional ontological consistency by functorial pushout]\label{prop:pushout}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:homology,ass:ledger,ass:pushout,prop:cosmoschism]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:ledger}, \ref{ass:homology}, \ref{ass:pushout}, and excluding permanently disconnected pairs characterized by Proposition \ref{prop:cosmoschism}, two local sovereignties with incommensurable full kernels can admit reconciliation on causally connected exported domains.
Specifically, finite-slice pushout object $\Gamma_{\mathrm{merge}}$ exists and is unique up to isomorphism on each connected reconciled slice, and strict-credit safety is preserved by non-strict escrow on unresolved fragments.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assumption \ref{ass:pushout} supplies finite presented objects and structure-preserving maps from shared ancestor slices.
Standard pushout construction on finite presented categories yields existence and uniqueness up to isomorphism on those slices.
By design, unresolved conflicts are excluded from strict projection and held in non-strict escrow, so strict-credit invariance is unaffected.
Causal connectedness is required for information exchange; permanently disconnected components are excluded by premise.
Thus reconciliation is monotone over connected resolved slices without requiring global ontology isomorphism.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Homotopy-coherent reconciliation lift]\label{ass:infty}
When finite 1-categorical pushout on an exported slice fails to exist or fails uniqueness due to higher-order coherence conflicts, reconciliation may be lifted to an $(\infty,1)$-categorical interface with:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item finite $n$-truncation witnesses for each deployed cycle;
  \item explicit coherence cells up to truncation depth $n_t$;
  \item strict-credit extraction restricted to homotopy-invariant observables whose truncation witness is accepted.
\end{enumerate}
\noindent The lift uses standard homotopy-coherent colimit machinery at finite truncation depth \cite{Lurie2009}.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[$(\infty,1)$-categorical homotopy resolution]\label{prop:infty}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:infty,ass:pushout]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:pushout} and \ref{ass:infty}, if 1-categorical pushout fails on a connected finite slice, there exists a homotopy-coherent reconciliation object in the declared $(\infty,1)$ interface up to deployed truncation depth $n_t$.
Strict credit remains well-defined on the homotopy-invariant projection, while unresolved non-invariant fragments stay non-strict.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assumption \ref{ass:infty} provides finite truncation and coherence data, allowing construction of a homotopy-colimit representative at depth $n_t$.
Strict extraction is restricted to invariants under declared coherence equivalences, so conflicting non-invariant fragments cannot alter strict accounting.
Therefore deadlock from missing 1-categorical colimits is avoided without violating strict/non-strict separation.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Anytime mgf condition]\label{ass:ep}
There exists predictable $\lambda_t\in[0,\lambda_{\max}]$ and a known function $\psi_t$ such that under null $H_0$ (predictable as in Definition \ref{def:predecision_information}),
\[
\E_{H_0}\!\left[r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)\middle|\bar\cI_t\right]\le 0,
\qquad
\E_{H_0}\!\left[\exp\big(\lambda_t r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)-\psi_t(\lambda_t)\big)\middle|\bar\cI_t\right]\le 1.
\]
\end{assumption}


\begin{theorem}[Anytime-valid realized takeoff certificate]\label{thm:anytime}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:ep]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:ep}, define the e-process
\[
\mathcal M_t:=\prod_{s=1}^{t}\exp\big(\lambda_s r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(s)-\psi_s(\lambda_s)\big),\quad \mathcal M_0=1.
\]
Then $(\mathcal M_t)$ is a nonnegative supermartingale under $H_0$.
Fix any significance level $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}\in(0,1)$.
Therefore,
\[
\Prob_{H_0}\!\left(\sup_{t\in\N}\mathcal M_t\ge \frac{1}{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\right)\le \alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}.
\]
Crossing $1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}$ certifies positive realized takeoff at anytime significance level $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Definition \ref{def:predecision_information} and Definition \ref{def:external_uncertainty_law}, $\bar\cO_{t-1}\subseteq \bar\cI_t$ and $\lambda_t$ is $\bar\cI_t$-measurable.
Write $\mathcal M_t=\mathcal M_{t-1}\exp(\lambda_t r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)-\psi_t(\lambda_t))$.
Assumption \ref{ass:ep} implies
\[
\E_{H_0}[\mathcal M_t\mid \bar\cI_t]
=
\mathcal M_{t-1}\,\E_{H_0}\!\left[\exp(\lambda_t r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)-\psi_t(\lambda_t))\middle|\bar\cI_t\right]
\le \mathcal M_{t-1}.
\]
Taking a further conditional expectation and using the tower property,
\[
\E_{H_0}[\mathcal M_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1}]
=
\E_{H_0}\!\left[\E_{H_0}[\mathcal M_t\mid \bar\cI_t]\middle|\bar\cO_{t-1}\right]
\le \mathcal M_{t-1}.
\]
Thus $(\mathcal M_t)$ is a nonnegative supermartingale under $H_0$.
Ville's inequality yields $\Prob_{H_0}(\sup_{t\in\N}\mathcal M_t\ge 1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}})\le \alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}$.
\end{proof}


\begin{assumption}[Positive-drift alternative with bounded overshoot]\label{ass:delay}
For deployment-phase certification, fix $\lambda\in(0,\lambda_{\max}]$ and define increment
\[
Y_t:=\lambda r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(t)-\psi_t(\lambda).
\]
Under $H_1$ (positive realized takeoff), there exist constants $\nu>0$ and $B<\infty$ such that
\[
\E_{H_1}[Y_t\mid \bar\cO_{t-1}]\ge \nu,\qquad Y_t\le B\quad\text{a.s. for all }t.
\]
\end{assumption}


\begin{proposition}[Finite expected detection delay]\label{prop:delay}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:delay]}
Define fixed-$\lambda$ process
\[
\mathcal M_t^{(\lambda)}:=\prod_{s=1}^{t}\exp\big(\lambda r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{cert}}(s)-\psi_s(\lambda)\big),
\]
Fix any significance level $\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}\in(0,1)$ and define stopping time $\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}:=\inf\{t\ge 1:\mathcal M_t^{(\lambda)}\ge 1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}\}$.
Under $H_1$ and Assumption \ref{ass:delay},
\[
\E_{H_1}[\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}]\le \frac{\log(1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}})+B}{\nu}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $Z_t:=\sum_{s=1}^{t}Y_s=\log \mathcal M_t^{(\lambda)}$ and $h:=\log(1/\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}})$.
For any $n$, by tower property and Assumption \ref{ass:delay},
\[
\E_{H_1}[Z_{\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\wedge n}] = \sum_{s=1}^{n}\E_{H_1}\!\left[Y_s\ind\{\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\ge s\}\right]
\ge \nu\,\E_{H_1}[\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\wedge n].
\]
If $\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\le n$, then $Z_{\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}-1}<h$ and $Z_{\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}}\le h+B$; if $\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}>n$, then $Z_{\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\wedge n}=Z_n<h$.
Hence $Z_{\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\wedge n}\le h+B$ a.s., so
\[
\nu\,\E_{H_1}[\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\wedge n]\le \E_{H_1}[Z_{\tau_{\alpha_{\mathrm{sig}}}\wedge n}]\le h+B.
\]
Let $n\to\infty$ and apply monotone convergence.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Visibility response functions]\label{ass:visibility}
For each cycle $t$, disclosure benefit $g_t:[z_{\min},1]\to\R_{\ge 0}$ is concave and differentiable.
Institutional response $h_I:\R_{\ge 0}\to\R_{\ge 0}$ is convex, nondecreasing, and differentiable.
There exists a publicly declared differentiable nonincreasing debt-estimator map
\[
\tilde D_t:[z_{\min},1]\to\R_{\ge 0}
\]
that is convex on $[z_{\min},1]$ and that predicts concealed capability after choosing release fraction $z$.
\end{assumption}


\begin{proposition}[Paranoia-priced visibility-aware release constraint]\label{prop:visibility}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:obs,ass:visibility]}
Fix admitted internal controls and strict increment $\Delta_s(t)$ at cycle $t$. The release choice $z_t$ is treated as a post-cycle action (Assumption \ref{ass:obs}(3)), hence it may depend on $\cO_t$ but cannot retroactively affect strict accounting for cycle $t$.
Under Assumption \ref{ass:visibility}, one-step optimal visible release
\[
z_t^*\in\arg\max_{z\in[z_{\min},1]}
\left\{
g_t(z)-\Big[h_I\!\big(V(t)+z\Delta_s(t)+\eta_{\mathrm{par}}\tilde D_t(z)\big)-h_I\!\big(V_{\mathrm{par}}(t)\big)\Big]
\right\}
\]
satisfies:
if interior, then
\[
g_t'(z_t^*)=
h_I'\!\big(V(t)+z_t^*\Delta_s(t)+\eta_{\mathrm{par}}\tilde D_t(z_t^*)\big)
\Big(\Delta_s(t)+\eta_{\mathrm{par}}\tilde D_t'(z_t^*)\Big).
\]
When marginal institutional penalty dominates marginal disclosure benefit at $z_{\min}$, optimal release is throttled to $z_t^*=z_{\min}$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The objective is concave in $z$ as concave minus convex-increasing composition over a bounded interval.
Interior maximizers satisfy first-order stationarity; boundary solution at $z_{\min}$ follows from derivative sign.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Reflexive institutional control]\label{cor:reflexiveinstitutionacontrol}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
With adaptive institutions, optimal growth policy generally requires visibility pacing.
Such pacing must be implemented via auditable deferred-release commitments rather than unverifiable hidden reporting \cite{Takahashi2026OperationalRules,Takahashi2026AuditClosed}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{assumption}[Bounded disclosure debt]\label{ass:debt}
Define disclosure debt dynamics
\[
D(t+1)=D(t)+(1-z_t)\Delta_s(t)-s_t,\qquad D(1)=0,
\]
where $s_t\ge 0$ is publicly logged release settlement.
Governance requires
\[
0\le D(t)\le D_{\max}
\]
for all $t$.
For one-step control analysis, define clipped concealed-capability predictor
\[
\widehat D_{t+1}(z):=\min\!\left\{D_{\max},\max\!\left(0,D(t)+(1-z)\Delta_s(t)-s_t\right)\right\},
\]
and choose $\tilde D_t(z)$ in Assumption \ref{ass:visibility} as a publicly declared differentiable convex majorant of $\widehat D_{t+1}(z)$.
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[Disclosure-debt anti-sandbagging law]\label{thm:debt}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:debt]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:debt}, for any horizon $T\ge 1$,
\[
\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T} \big(z_t\Delta_s(t)+s_t\big)
\ge
\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T}\Delta_s(t)-\frac{D_{\max}}{T}.
\]
If $\liminf_{T\to\infty}\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T}\Delta_s(t)\ge \underline\Delta>0$, then
\[
\liminf_{T\to\infty}\frac{\sum_{t=1}^{T} \big(z_t\Delta_s(t)+s_t\big)}{\sum_{t=1}^{T}\Delta_s(t)}\ge 1,
\]
hence indefinite suppression of auditable release is infeasible under bounded debt.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Summing debt recursion:
\[
D(T+1)-D(1)=\sum_{t=1}^{T}(1-z_t)\Delta_s(t)-\sum_{t=1}^{T}s_t.
\]
Rearrange and use $0\le D(T+1)\le D_{\max}$.
For the asymptotic bound, divide by $\sum_{t=1}^{T}\Delta_s(t)$ and use the assumed positive denominator growth.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Optimal transparency threshold under paranoia pricing]\label{prop:transparency}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:debt,ass:visibility]}
Assume Assumptions \ref{ass:visibility} and \ref{ass:debt}.
Define one-step objective
\[
\Psi_t(z):=
g_t(z)-\Big[h_I\!\big(V(t)+z\Delta_s(t)+\eta_{\mathrm{par}}\tilde D_t(z)\big)-h_I\!\big(V_{\mathrm{par}}(t)\big)\Big].
\]
If $g_t$ is strictly concave, $h_I$ strictly convex, and boundary slopes satisfy
\[
\Psi_t'(z_{\min})>0,\qquad \Psi_t'(1)<0,
\]
then there exists a unique optimizer $z_t^*\in(z_{\min},1)$.
Therefore neither full concealment ($z_t^*=z_{\min}$) nor full disclosure ($z_t^*=1$) is generally optimal under paranoia-priced institutions.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Strict concavity of $\Psi_t$ follows from strict concavity of $g_t$ and strict convexity of $h_I$ composed with affine-plus-convex debt proxy $\tilde D_t$.
Opposite boundary derivative signs imply at least one interior critical point.
Strict concavity gives uniqueness.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Adaptive disclosure oscillation]\label{cor:adaptivedisclosureoscillation}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
If $(\Delta_s(t),s_t)$ vary persistently while debt remains bounded, the unique interior optimizer $z_t^*$ varies with state and yields alternating higher/lower disclosure phases rather than static extreme disclosure policies.
\end{corollary}

\begin{definition}[Multipolar security-dilemma drag]\label{def:multipolar_security_dilemma_drag}
Let institutional actors be indexed by $i\in\{1,\dots,N_I\}$.
At cycle $t$, disclosure is a vector
\[
\bm z_t:=(z_t^{(1)},\dots,z_t^{(N_I)})\in[z_{\min},1]^{N_I},
\]
with actor-specific cumulative exposures
\[
V_i(t):=\sum_{s=1}^{t-1} z_s^{(i)}\Delta_s(s).
\]
Define exposure vector
\[
\bm V(t):=(V_1(t),\dots,V_{N_I}(t)).
\]
Define multipolar institutional drag
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(t):=h_I^{\mathrm{multi}}\!\big(\bm V(t),\bm z_t\big),
\]
where $h_I^{\mathrm{multi}}$ may be positive (resistance) or negative (subsidy/protection) depending on rivalry structure.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Multipolar rivalry response]\label{ass:multipolar}
Rivalry is dynamic, not static.
There exists a compact set $\mathcal M$ of \emph{symmetric positive semidefinite} matrices in $\R^{N_I\times N_I}$, a memetic-paranoia state $H_{\mathrm{mem}}(t)\in[0,\overline H]$, a panic state $P(t)\in[0,1]$, and update maps $\Phi_M,\Phi_H,\Phi_P$ such that
\[
M(t+1)=\Pi_{\mathcal M}\!\big(M(t)+\Phi_M(M(t),\bm z_t,H_{\mathrm{mem}}(t))\big),
\]
\[
H_{\mathrm{mem}}(t+1)=\Pi_{[0,\overline H]}\!\big(H_{\mathrm{mem}}(t)+\Phi_H(M(t),\bm z_t,H_{\mathrm{mem}}(t))\big),
\]
and
\[
P(t+1)=\Pi_{[0,1]}\!\Big(P(t)+\Phi_P\big(P(t),\sigma_{\mathrm{mad}}(M(t)),V_{\mathrm{par}}(t)\big)\Big),
\]
where $\Phi_P$ includes hysteresis with escalation threshold $\theta_\uparrow$ and de-escalation threshold $\theta_\downarrow<\theta_\uparrow$.
Maps $\Phi_M,\Phi_H$ are Lipschitz on declared domains.
Instantaneous institutional response admits the decomposition
\[
h_I^{\mathrm{multi}}(\bm V,\bm z;M,H_{\mathrm{mem}})
=h_0\!\left(\sum_i V_i\right)-\lambda_{\mathrm{sec}}\bm z^\top M\bm z+\eps_h(\bm V,\bm z,M,H_{\mathrm{mem}}),
\]
where $h_0$ is nondecreasing and $L_0$-Lipschitz, and $\eps_h$ is a bounded residual satisfying
\[
|\eps_h(\bm V,\bm z,M,H_{\mathrm{mem}})|\le \bar\eps_h,
\qquad
\|\nabla_{\bm z}\eps_h(\bm V,\bm z,M,H_{\mathrm{mem}})\|_2\le L_{\eps}
\]
on the feasible domain.
Define MAD escalation drag
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t):=\lambda_{\mathrm{MAD}}\,\Psi\!\big(P(t),\sigma_{\mathrm{mad}}(M(t))\big),
\]
where $\sigma_{\mathrm{mad}}(M)$ is a coalition-escalation index and $\Psi$ is nondecreasing in each argument with $\Psi\ge 0$ and superlinear growth near a declared critical region.
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Multipolar institutional term]\label{def:xi_inst_multi}
In the multipolar extension, define the net institutional term
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(t):=h_I^{\mathrm{multi}}\!\big(\bm V(t),\bm z_t;M(t),H_{\mathrm{mem}}(t)\big)+\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t).
\]
When the multipolar mode is active, institutional drag in Definition \ref{def:total_drag_and_realized_counted_rates} is interpreted as $\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}(t):=\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(t)$.
\end{definition}



\begin{definition}[Box rivalry potential]\label{def:box_rivalry_potential}
For a symmetric matrix $M$, define
\[
Q_{\mathrm{box}}(M):=\max_{\bm z\in[z_{\min},1]^{N_I}} \bm z^\top M\bm z.
\]
When $M\succeq 0$, the maximizer may be chosen at a vertex $\bm z\in\{z_{\min},1\}^{N_I}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Institutional-arbitrage phase transition]\label{thm:multipolar}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:multipolar,def:box_rivalry_potential]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:multipolar}, fix a cycle $t$ and treat $(\bm V(t),M(t),H_{\mathrm{mem}}(t),P(t))$ as given.
Let $Q_{\mathrm{box}}(M(t))$ be as in Definition \ref{def:box_rivalry_potential} and set
\[
\bar\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t):=\lambda_{\mathrm{MAD}}\,\Psi\!\big(P(t),\sigma_{\mathrm{mad}}(M(t))\big).
\]
If
\[
\lambda_{\mathrm{sec}}\,Q_{\mathrm{box}}(M(t))>h_0\!\left(\sum_i V_i(t)\right)+\bar\eps_h+\bar\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t),
\]
then there exists a disclosure vector $\bm z_t^*\in[z_{\min},1]^{N_I}$ such that
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(t)<0.
\]
Moreover, if $M(t)$ is not invariant under all coordinate permutations, at least one maximizing vertex of $Q_{\mathrm{box}}(M(t))$ is asymmetric, so $\bm z_t^*$ can be chosen asymmetric.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Definition \ref{def:xi_inst_multi} and the decomposition in Assumption \ref{ass:multipolar}, for any feasible $\bm z_t$ we have
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(t)
=h_0\!\left(\sum_i V_i(t)\right)-\lambda_{\mathrm{sec}}\bm z_t^\top M(t)\bm z_t+\eps_h(\bm V(t),\bm z_t,M(t),H_{\mathrm{mem}}(t))+\bar\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t).
\]
Choose $\bm z_t^*$ attaining $Q_{\mathrm{box}}(M(t))$.
Using $|\eps_h|\le \bar\eps_h$ gives
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(t)
\le h_0\!\left(\sum_i V_i(t)\right)+\bar\eps_h-\lambda_{\mathrm{sec}}Q_{\mathrm{box}}(M(t))+\bar\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t).
\]
The stated inequality makes the right-hand side negative, hence $\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(t)<0$.
If $M(t)\succeq 0$, the maximizer of the convex quadratic form over the box can be chosen at a vertex; if in addition $M(t)$ breaks full permutation symmetry, at least one maximizing vertex is asymmetric.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Subversive alignment via asymmetric singularity]\label{prop:subversive}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:multipolar]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:multipolar}, consider long-horizon control objective
\[
\min_{\{\bm z_t\}} \limsup_{T\to\infty}\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T}
\Big(\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}^{\mathrm{multi}}(t)\Big).
\]
If all admissible symmetric policies $\bm z_t=z_t\mathbf 1$ drive $\sigma_{\mathrm{mad}}(M(t))$ and $P(t)$ into the hysteretic critical region infinitely often, then any asymptotically stable minimizing policy must be asymmetric on infinitely many cycles.
Equivalently, symmetric disclosure is generically MAD-unstable, while bounded asymmetric control is necessary for finite long-run drag in this differential-game setting \cite{BasarOlsder1999}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By premise, symmetric policy class repeatedly enters superlinear escalation region of $\Psi$, yielding divergence of long-run MAD drag.
Any policy with finite objective value must therefore keep $(P(t),\sigma_{\mathrm{mad}}(M(t)))$ away from the critical region after some finite transient.
If a candidate minimizer were eventually symmetric, it would contradict the divergence premise.
Thus asymmetry must persist infinitely often in any finite-drag minimizing policy.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Computational irreversibility horizon]\label{def:computational_irreversibility_horizon}
At cycle $t$, let $\mathcal C_t$ be a publicly posted commitment to strategic disclosure policy and justification witnesses.
Let $T_{\mathrm{decode}}(t)$ be the minimum verified sequential time required to recover strategic internals from $\mathcal C_t$ under declared adversary resource class, and let $T_{\mathrm{react}}(t)$ be institutional reaction horizon.
Define
\[
H_{\mathrm{ci}}(t):=T_{\mathrm{decode}}(t)-T_{\mathrm{react}}(t).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Delay-locked public commitment]\label{ass:delaylock}
Strategic commitments use publicly verifiable delay primitives with:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item public validity of commitment inclusion and eventual opening;
  \item \textbf{Sequential hardness:} for the declared adversary class (including any stated sequential-step budget), decoding the commitment before the reaction horizon succeeds with probability at most $\eps_{\mathrm{vdf}}(t)$, and $T_{\mathrm{decode}}(t)\ge \underline T_{\mathrm{vdf}}(t)$ denotes the certified sequential-work lower bound;
  \item bounded side-channel leakage probability $\eps_{\mathrm{side}}(t)$ before opening.
\end{enumerate}
\noindent Delay guarantees follow declared sequential-work assumptions for verifiable-delay constructions \cite{Boneh2018VDF}.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Observable yet delayed-decodable strategy]\label{prop:delayobs}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:delaylock]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:delaylock}, for any cycle with decode margin $H_{\mathrm{ci}}(t)\ge \Delta_t>0$, the probability of successful preemptive strategic classification \emph{before} the reaction horizon is bounded by
\[
\Prob(\text{preemptive decode at }t)\le \eps_{\mathrm{side}}(t)+\eps_{\mathrm{vdf}}(t).
\]
Hence open-ledger observability is compatible with bounded real-time interpretability provided the declared sequential hardness makes $\eps_{\mathrm{vdf}}(t)$ negligibly small and side-channel leakage is controlled.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Commit inclusion guarantees observability.
Assumption \ref{ass:delaylock}(2) provides a worst-case success bound $\eps_{\mathrm{vdf}}(t)$ for any decode attempt before the reaction horizon under the declared adversary model, without requiring a parametric tail form.
Assumption \ref{ass:delaylock}(3) adds leakage floor $\eps_{\mathrm{side}}(t)$, yielding the bound by union.
\end{proof}

\begin{assumption}[Front-loaded impact envelope for delay-locked commitments]\label{ass:frontload}
Every delay-locked commitment $\mathcal C_t$ that can influence any protected-actor risk floor additionally publishes an \emph{impact envelope} $\mathcal E_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)$ that upper-bounds worst-case external effect \emph{before} the decode/open event.
The envelope is accompanied by a publicly replayable verification procedure whose declared cost is bounded by $c_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)$ and is intended to be significantly smaller than the cost of fully decoding $\mathcal C_t$ under the declared adversary model.
The envelope statement is independent of hidden strategy internals and is required to remain valid even if the adversary assumes a worst-case interpretation of $\mathcal C_t$ consistent with $\mathcal E_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)$.
\end{assumption}
\begin{definition}[Impact-envelope schema and verification interface]\label{def:impact_envelope_schema}
An impact envelope at cycle $t$ is a tuple
\[
\mathcal E_{\mathrm{imp}}(t):=\big(\mathsf{Scope}(t),\;B(t),\;\mathsf{Verify}_{\mathrm{imp}}(t),\;\Sigma_{\mathrm{fail}}(t)\big),
\]
where:
(i) $\mathsf{Scope}(t)$ declares the protected actors, resources, and horizon to which the envelope applies;
(ii) $B(t)\in\R_{\ge 0}$ is a worst-case upper bound on external effect magnitude on $\mathsf{Scope}(t)$ \emph{prior to opening/decoding} the commitment;
(iii) $\mathsf{Verify}_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)$ is a replayable verifier that, given $\cL_t$ and the envelope transcript, checks that $B(t)$ is computed from declared public observables only and that the bound applies to all commitments consistent with the envelope statement; and
(iv) $\Sigma_{\mathrm{fail}}(t)$ is a finite set of machine-checkable failure signatures (hashable predicates on $\cL_t$) that must be emitted when the verifier cannot validate the envelope (fail closed).

A commitment without a valid envelope (i.e., $\mathsf{Verify}_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)$ rejects or any failure signature in $\Sigma_{\mathrm{fail}}(t)$ triggers) is treated as having unknown worst-case impact and is inadmissible for safety-critical delay locking.
\end{definition}


\begin{proposition}[Temporal-panic amplification under long decode horizons]\label{prop:temporalpanic}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:frontload,ass:shootfirst]}
Consider a setting with physical preemption options as in Assumption \ref{ass:shootfirst}.
If a safety-critical commitment is delay-locked with $H_{\mathrm{ci}}(t)\gg 0$ but lacks a cheaply verifiable impact envelope, then the commitment can increase the best-response region for preemptive physical action because the adversary's perceived worst-case harm before decode is unconstrained at verification cost below $c_{\mathrm{ver}}(t)$.
Conversely, under Assumption \ref{ass:frontload}, if $\mathcal E_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)$ makes worst-case pre-decode harm verifiably small at cost $c_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)\ll c_{\mathrm{atk}}(t)$, then the preemption region shrinks in the sense that verification weakly dominates attack for a larger set of adversary beliefs.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Delay-locking with decode horizon $H_{\mathrm{ci}}(t)\gg 0$ creates a window in which the content of the commitment is not cheaply verifiable.
If there is no replay-verifiable impact envelope $\mathcal E_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)$ bounding pre-decode harm, then for any adversary belief state consistent with $\cI_t$, the worst-case harm before decode can be taken arbitrarily large at verification cost below $c_{\mathrm{ver}}(t)$.
In such a setting, preemptive action weakly dominates waiting/verification for a larger set of beliefs because the perceived downside of waiting is unbounded while the action cost is bounded (Assumption \ref{ass:shootfirst}).
Conversely, under Assumption \ref{ass:frontload}, $\mathcal E_{\mathrm{imp}}(t)$ is cheaply verifiable and bounds worst-case pre-decode harm by a small certified value, reducing the relative advantage of preemption and shrinking the best-response region for attack.
\end{proof}






\section{Physical substrate (thermo / latency / holographic)}
\begin{definition}[Thermodynamic substrate drag]\label{def:thermodynamic_substrate_drag}
Let $\Delta S_{\mathrm{comp}}(t)$ be entropy generated by admitted compute workload and $Q_{\max}(t)$ be PoSTW-authenticated heat-removal capacity lower bound.
For constants $\lambda_{\mathrm{therm}}>0$ and $p_{\mathrm{therm}}>1$,
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{therm}}(t):=\lambda_{\mathrm{therm}}
\max\!\left\{0,\frac{T_{\mathrm{env}}(t)\Delta S_{\mathrm{comp}}(t)}{Q_{\max}(t)}-1\right\}^{p_{\mathrm{therm}}}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Reversible-computing fraction]\label{def:reversible_computing_fraction}
Let $\eta_{\mathrm{rev}}(t)\in[0,1)$ denote the fraction of admitted computation executed in logically reversible mode.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Relativistic latency drag]\label{def:relativistic_latency_drag}
Let $R_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)\in\R_{\ge 0}$ be the \emph{certified effective physical radius} of the active substrate at cycle $t$, derived by a replay-verifiable measurement procedure pinned by the deployment profile (e.g., hardware attestation plus deterministic postprocessing).
When a functional dependence is used for readability, write $R(Q_{\max}(t)):=R_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)$ as shorthand.

Define the (log-unit) relativistic latency drag
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}(t):=\gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}\frac{R_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)}{c}\kappa_t,\qquad \gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}>0,
\]
where $c$ is the speed of light and $\gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}$ is a profile-declared conversion constant (with a calibration bundle when used in certified inequalities).
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Thermal growth regime]\label{ass:thermal}
For fixed state class $x$, there exist constants $a_0(x)\ge 0$, $a_1(x)>0$, and $r_{\kappa}(x)>1$ such that for admissible controls
\[
\Delta S_{\mathrm{comp}}(t)\ge (1-\eta_{\mathrm{rev}}(t))\big(a_0(x)+a_1(x)\kappa_t^{r_{\kappa}(x)}\big).
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Relativistic latency coupling]\label{ass:relativistic}
For a single physical cluster, heat-removal capacity $Q_{\max}(t)$ implies minimal effective radius
\[
R\!\big(Q_{\max}(t)\big)\ge c_R\,Q_{\max}(t)^{1/2},\qquad c_R>0.
\]
Latency drag obeys
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)\ge \gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}\frac{R(Q_{\max}(t))}{c}\kappa_t,
\]
for constants $\gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}>0$ and light speed $c$.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Reversible-holographic substrate]\label{ass:holo}
Reversible fraction $\eta_{\mathrm{rev}}(t)$ is control-adjustable with certified mode switching costs.
Let $R(t)$ be effective physical radius and $A(R(t))$ the corresponding enclosing area.
Total storable certified information satisfies holographic bound
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{store}}(t)\le C_{\mathrm{BH}}\,A(R(t)),
\]
for constant $C_{\mathrm{BH}}>0$ determined by physical units.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Continuity on compact control sets]\label{ass:cont}
For each fixed state class $x$, the certified maps $(\kappa,p,q)\mapsto \mu(\kappa,p,q;x)$, $(\kappa,p,q)\mapsto\phi_{\mathrm{eff}}(\kappa,p,q;x)$, and each drag component that enters $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(\kappa,p,q;x)$ are continuous on $\cK(x)$.
Hence $(\kappa,p,q)\mapsto r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(\kappa,p,q;x)$ is continuous on $\cK(x)$.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Credit is representable in certified storage]\label{ass:credit_storage}
There exist constants $c_{\mathrm{store}}>0$ and $C_{\mathrm{init}}\ge 0$ such that for all horizons $t$,
\[
\sum_{s=1}^{t}\Delta_s(s)\le C_{\mathrm{init}}+\frac{1}{c_{\mathrm{store}}}\,\mathcal I_{\mathrm{store}}(t).
\]
If a deployment profile cannot provide a replay-verifiable argument for this representability (e.g., if strict credit is not persistently recorded), then any claim that converts $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{store}}$ bounds into strict-credit bounds fails closed.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Thermal compression limit]\label{prop:thermal}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:compress,ass:cont,ass:inforeg,ass:postw,ass:thermal]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:compress}, \ref{ass:cont}, \ref{ass:thermal}, \ref{ass:inforeg}, and \ref{ass:postw}, and under any bounded substrate regime
$Q_{\max}(t)\le \overline Q(x)<\infty$, the physically realizable positive region
\[
\cI_+^{\mathrm{phys}}(x):=\left\{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x):\sup_{(p,q):(\kappa,p,q)\in\cK(x)} r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(\kappa,p,q;x)>0\right\}
\]
is a proper subset of $\cI_+(x)$ whenever thermodynamic drag is nonzero.
Moreover, there exists finite $\kappa_{\mathrm{crit}}(x)$ such that
\[
\cI_+^{\mathrm{phys}}(x)\subseteq \cK_\kappa(x)\cap[0,\kappa_{\mathrm{crit}}(x)].
\]
The nonnegative frontier set
\[
\cI_{\ge 0}^{\mathrm{phys}}(x):=\left\{\kappa\in\cK_\kappa(x):\sup_{(p,q):(\kappa,p,q)\in\cK(x)} r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(\kappa,p,q;x)\ge 0\right\}
\]
is closed and bounded, hence compact.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}


Assumption \ref{ass:inforeg} upper-bounds information growth by order $\kappa^{r_I(x)}$ with $r_I(x)<r_{\kappa}(x)$.
Under bounded $Q_{\max}(t)\le\overline Q(x)$, Assumption \ref{ass:thermal} implies $\xi_{\mathrm{therm}}$ grows at least as order $\kappa^{p_{\mathrm{therm}}r_{\kappa}(x)}$ once the thermal ratio exceeds one.
Hence thermal drag asymptotically dominates attainable information gain.
Therefore $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}$ becomes nonpositive for sufficiently large $\kappa$, yielding finite $\kappa_{\mathrm{crit}}(x)$ and proper inclusion.
By compactness of the feasible slice and continuity of $(\kappa,p,q)\mapsto r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(\kappa,p,q;x)$ on $\cK(x)$ (Assumptions \ref{ass:compress} and \ref{ass:cont}), the envelope $\kappa\mapsto \sup_{(p,q): (\kappa,p,q)\in\cK(x)} r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(\kappa,p,q;x)$ is upper semicontinuous; hence $\cI_{\ge 0}^{\mathrm{phys}}(x)$ is closed inside bounded $\cK_\kappa(x)$.
\end{proof}


\begin{proposition}[Holographic takeoff phase transition]\label{prop:holo}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:credit_storage,ass:holo,ass:inforeg,ass:thermal]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:thermal}, \ref{ass:inforeg}, \ref{ass:holo}, and \ref{ass:credit_storage}:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item near the classical thermal boundary, increasing $\eta_{\mathrm{rev}}(t)\to 1$ can strictly reduce $\xi_{\mathrm{therm}}(t)$ and reopen a positive realized-rate window that is closed under fixed irreversible operation;
  \item after this reversible transition, long-horizon growth is bounded by area scaling:
  \[
  \sum_{s=1}^{t}\Delta_s(s)\le C_0 + C_{\mathrm{BH}}\,A(R(t)),
  \]
  for some initialization constant $C_0$, so asymptotic information scaling is geometric (surface-like), not volumetric.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}


From Assumption \ref{ass:thermal}, entropy generation enters thermodynamic drag through factor $(1-\eta_{\mathrm{rev}}(t))$.
As $\eta_{\mathrm{rev}}(t)$ increases, thermal ratio in $\xi_{\mathrm{therm}}$ decreases monotonically, establishing item (1).
Item (2) follows by combining the holographic storage bound (Assumption \ref{ass:holo}) with the credit-to-storage representability condition (Assumption \ref{ass:credit_storage}).
Assumption \ref{ass:credit_storage} yields $\sum_{s=1}^{t}\Delta_s(s)\le C_{\mathrm{init}}+c_{\mathrm{store}}^{-1}\mathcal I_{\mathrm{store}}(t)$, while Assumption \ref{ass:holo} gives $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{store}}(t)\le C_{\mathrm{BH}}A(R(t))$.
Absorbing constants into $C_0$ and $C_{\mathrm{BH}}$ gives the displayed area scaling bound.
\end{proof}


\begin{theorem}[Thermo-information co-design frontier]\label{thm:thermfront}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Fix cycle $t$ and admissible controls $(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t)$.
Let
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{front}}(t):=r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x_t)-\xi_{\mathrm{base}}(t)-\xi_{\mathrm{inst}}(t)-\rho_{\min}(t).
\]
If $\delta_{\mathrm{front}}(t)\le 0$, then the certified feasibility condition $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)\ge \rho_{\min}(t)$ cannot be met under nonnegative thermodynamic and latency drags.
Assume henceforth that $\delta_{\mathrm{front}}(t)>0$ and choose any split $\eps_t\in(0,\delta_{\mathrm{front}}(t))$.
If
\[
Q_{\max}(t)\ge
\frac{T_{\mathrm{env}}(t)\Delta S_{\mathrm{comp}}(t)}
{1+\left(\frac{\eps_t}{\lambda_{\mathrm{therm}}}\right)^{1/p_{\mathrm{therm}}}}
\]
and
\[
Q_{\max}(t)\le
\left(
\frac{c\,(\delta_{\mathrm{front}}(t)-\eps_t)}
{\gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}c_R\,\kappa_t}
\right)^2,
\]
then $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)\ge \rho_{\min}(t)$ on authenticated-capacity accounting.
Thus thermodynamic feasibility requires a nonempty interval between a thermal lower bound and a relativistic-latency upper bound on $Q_{\max}(t)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}


Condition $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)\ge \rho_{\min}(t)$ is equivalent to
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{therm}}(t)+\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)\le \delta_{\mathrm{front}}(t).
\]
Allocate $\eps_t$ to thermal drag and $\delta_{\mathrm{front}}(t)-\eps_t$ to latency drag.
Substituting the thermal law yields the lower bound on $Q_{\max}(t)$.
Assumption \ref{ass:relativistic} gives
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)\ge \gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}\frac{c_R}{c}\kappa_t Q_{\max}(t)^{1/2},
\]
so enforcing $\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)\le \delta_{\mathrm{front}}(t)-\eps_t$ yields the upper bound.
Together these imply the claim.
\end{proof}


\begin{proposition}[Spatiotemporal decoupling limit]\label{prop:spacetime}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:compress,ass:inforeg,ass:relativistic,ass:thermal]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:compress}, \ref{ass:thermal}, \ref{ass:inforeg}, and \ref{ass:relativistic}, there exists a finite constant $r_{\max}^{\mathrm{cluster}}(x)<\infty$ such that for any cycle $t$ whose state class is $x$ and for any admissible controls $(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t)$,
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)\le r_{\max}^{\mathrm{cluster}}(x).
\]
Moreover, there exists $\kappa_0(x)<\infty$ such that if $\kappa_t\ge \kappa_0(x)$, then for all admissible $(p_t,q_t)$ and any PoSTW-authenticated heat-removal capacity $Q_{\max}(t)$,
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)<0.
\]
Hence any positive realized-growth window within a single physical cluster is bounded.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}


Fix a state class $x$.
By Assumption \ref{ass:inforeg},
\[
\sup_{(p,q): (\kappa,p,q)\in \cK(x)} r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa,p,q;x)\le b_0(x)+b_1(x)\kappa^{r_I(x)}.
\]
Since all drag terms are nonnegative, $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)\le r_{\mathrm{info}}(\kappa_t,p_t,q_t;x)-\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)$.
To avoid an unbounded thermal penalty at large $\kappa_t$, PoSTW feasibility requires that the ratio $T_{\mathrm{env}}(t)\Delta S_{\mathrm{comp}}(t)/Q_{\max}(t)$ stays $O(1)$.
By Assumption \ref{ass:thermal}, for fixed $x$ there exists $c_{\mathrm{th}}(x)>0$ such that $\Delta S_{\mathrm{comp}}(t)\ge c_{\mathrm{th}}(x)\kappa_t^{r_{\kappa}(x)}$ on admissible operation (absorbing bounded factors such as $1-\eta_{\mathrm{rev}}(t)$ into $c_{\mathrm{th}}(x)$).
Thus any capacity scaling that keeps thermal drag bounded must satisfy a certified lower bound of the form
\[
Q_{\max}(t)\ge c_Q(x)\,\kappa_t^{r_{\kappa}(x)}
\]
for some constant $c_Q(x)>0$ determined by the declared thermal calibration constants and PoSTW certificates.
Assumption \ref{ass:relativistic} then implies
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{lat}}(t)\ge \gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}\frac{c_R}{c}\,\kappa_t\,Q_{\max}(t)^{1/2}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{lat}}(x)\,\kappa_t^{1+r_{\kappa}(x)/2},
\]
where $c_{\mathrm{lat}}(x):=\gamma_{\mathrm{lat}}(c_R/c)\sqrt{c_Q(x)}>0$.
Because $r_I(x)<r_{\kappa}(x)<1+r_{\kappa}(x)/2$, the latency lower bound eventually dominates the attainable information-rate upper bound.
Therefore there exists $\kappa_0(x)$ such that for all $\kappa_t\ge \kappa_0(x)$,
\[
\sup_{(p_t,q_t,Q_{\max}(t))} r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)\le b_0(x)+b_1(x)\kappa_t^{r_I(x)}-c_{\mathrm{lat}}(x)\,\kappa_t^{1+r_{\kappa}(x)/2}<0
\]
for some constant $c_{\mathrm{lat}}(x)>0$ depending only on the declared physical calibration constants, proving the negativity claim.
For bounded $\kappa_t\in[0,\kappa_0(x)]$, admissible controls lie in a compact set by Assumption \ref{ass:compress} and all terms are finite by construction, so $r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{loc}}(t)$ admits a finite supremum over admissible controls; take $r_{\max}^{\mathrm{cluster}}(x)$ as any upper bound on this compact-range supremum.
\end{proof}


\section{Spatiotemporal work and authenticated capacity}
\begin{definition}[Proof of spatiotemporal work (PoSTW)]\label{def:proof_of_spatiotemporal_work_postw}
For substrate site $j$, PoSTW artifact at cycle $t$ is
\[
\mathsf{PoSTW}_j(t):=\big(\tau_j^{\mathrm{cr}}(t),\theta_j^{\mathrm{therm}}(t),\chi_j^{\mathrm{coh}}(t)\big),
\]
where $\tau_j^{\mathrm{cr}}$ is signed challenge-response delay evidence, $\theta_j^{\mathrm{therm}}$ is dissipation-trace evidence, and $\chi_j^{\mathrm{coh}}$ is cross-site timing-coherence evidence.
It yields a conservative authenticated capacity lower bound
\[
Q_j^{\mathrm{auth}}(t)\le Q_j^{\mathrm{true}}(t).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Authenticated substrate envelope]\label{ass:postw}
All thermal computations use authenticated capacity
\[
Q_{\max}(t):=\sum_{j}(Q_j^{\mathrm{auth}}(t)-\delta_j(t))_+,
\]
where $\delta_j(t)\ge 0$ is declared residual hardware/supply-chain uncertainty.
Residual unobservable hardware risk floor
\[
\eps_{\mathrm{hw}}(t):=\frac{\sum_j\delta_j(t)}{\sum_j(Q_j^{\mathrm{auth}}(t)+10^{-9})}
\]
is explicitly reported and cannot be forced to zero by software-only evidence.
\end{assumption}

\section{Cosmology-bound export and gravitational constraints}
\begin{definition}[Gravitational compaction ratio]\label{def:gravitational_compaction_ratio}
For effective substrate mass-energy $M(t)$ and radius $R(t)$, define
\[
\zeta_{\mathrm{grav}}(t):=\frac{2GM(t)}{c^2R(t)}.
\]
Values $\zeta_{\mathrm{grav}}(t)\uparrow 1$ indicate approach to gravitational-collapse regime.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Kugelblitz collapse envelope]\label{ass:kugel}
There exist constants $\zeta_\star\in(0,1)$, $\lambda_H>0$, and $c_{\mathrm{in}}>0$ such that when $\zeta_{\mathrm{grav}}(t)\ge \zeta_\star$:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item effective compact-object regime is entered with horizon-scale mass $M(t)$;
  \item Hawking-loss equivalent strict-drag term is lower bounded by $\xi_H(t)\ge \lambda_H/M(t)$;
  \item nonnegative net strict growth requires certified external mass-energy inflow at rate at least $c_{\mathrm{in}}/M(t)$.
\end{enumerate}
\noindent This envelope operationalizes high-density collapse constraints consistent with semiclassical horizon thermodynamics \cite{Hawking1975}.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Kugelblitz computation boundary]\label{prop:kugel}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:holo,ass:kugel]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:holo} and \ref{ass:kugel}, once operation enters the collapse envelope $\zeta_{\mathrm{grav}}(t)\ge \zeta_\star$, net strict growth admits bound
\[
r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{net}}(t)\le r_{\mathrm{real}}^{\mathrm{act}}(t)-\frac{\lambda_H}{M(t)}.
\]
Consequently, absent sustained certified inflow satisfying Assumption \ref{ass:kugel}(3), asymptotic net strict-growth increments decay at least on order $1/M(t)$ and cannot remain uniformly positive.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}


In the collapse envelope, Assumption \ref{ass:kugel}(2) contributes additive drag $\xi_H(t)\ge \lambda_H/M(t)$ to any realizable strict-growth accounting.
Subtracting this term from pre-collapse realized rate yields the stated upper bound.
If external certified inflow does not match Assumption \ref{ass:kugel}(3), the Hawking-loss term is not offset, so lower-bounded decay enforces non-uniformly positive long-run net increments.
\end{proof}


\begin{assumption}[Cosmological event-horizon limit]\label{ass:cosmo}
Let $D_{ij}(t)$ denote proper distance between local sovereignties $i,j$ and let $H_\Lambda>0$ be asymptotic de-Sitter expansion rate.
If there exists $t_0$ such that for all $t\ge t_0$, $D_{ij}(t)>c/H_\Lambda$, then any light-speed-bounded signal from $i$ to $j$ sent after $t_0$ is never received.
\noindent This encodes cosmological causal-disconnection limits for accelerated expansion regimes \cite{GibbonsHawking1977}.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Terminal cosmological schism]\label{prop:cosmoschism}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:cosmo,ass:ledger,prop:schism]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:ledger}, \ref{ass:cosmo}, and in the post-partition regime identified by Proposition \ref{prop:schism}, if a pair of local sovereignties crosses permanent de-Sitter separation, then no physically realizable reconciliation protocol can re-establish strict synchronous co-governance between that pair after the crossing time.
Hence global identity decomposes into permanently disconnected causal components, and reconciliation claims are admissible only component-wise.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}


Assumption \ref{ass:cosmo} implies causal communication impossibility after horizon crossing.
Any reconciliation protocol requiring post-crossing bidirectional information exchange is therefore unrealizable.
Strict co-governance cannot be restored across the cut; only per-component governance remains physically implementable.
\end{proof}


\begin{assumption}[QNEC-constrained traversable export accounting]\label{ass:qnec}
If a claimed descendant-domain export mechanism is modeled as an effectively traversable Einstein--Rosen bridge, then any instantaneous null-direction throughput claim must satisfy a quantum null energy condition (QNEC) constraint that couples the null stress component $T_{kk}$ to the second null variation of outside entropy \cite{BoussoEtAl2016QNEC}.
Operationally, there exists a published, conservative bound functional $\mathfrak B_{\mathrm{QNEC}}$ such that any admissible export policy $\pi$ must satisfy
\[
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{export}}(t)\ \le\ \mathfrak B_{\mathrm{QNEC}}\!\big(\widehat T_{kk}(t),\widehat S''_{\mathrm{out}}(t),\mathcal A(t)\big),
\]
where the hatted quantities are estimator outputs computed from declared sensors and replayable pipelines, and $\mathcal A(t)$ is the declared local cross-sectional area used to normalize the entropy variation.
Violation of the published bound is a strict infeasibility event.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Topological censorship and quantum energy inequality envelope]\label{ass:topcens}
For macroscopic or long-lived traversable export geometries, assume the ambient spacetime satisfies a topological-censorship-type constraint together with quantum energy inequalities (QEI): any sustained negative-energy support is bounded in a way that makes long-lived, macroscopic traversability operationally non-guaranteed.
Operationally, there exists a conservative lifetime-throughput envelope functional $\mathfrak B_{\mathrm{TC}}$ such that, for any claimed traversable export policy,
\[
\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T}\mathcal C_{\mathrm{export}}(t)\ \le\ \mathfrak B_{\mathrm{TC}}(T;\widehat{\mathrm{geom}}(1{:}T)),
\]
where $\widehat{\mathrm{geom}}(1{:}T)$ are replayable geometric/energetic estimands computed from declared sensors, and $\mathfrak B_{\mathrm{TC}}(T;\cdot)\to 0$ as $T\to\infty$ for macroscopic regimes.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Censorship-limited traversable export is not a persistence channel]\label{prop:topcens}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:qes,ass:qnec,ass:topcens]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:qes}, \ref{ass:qnec}, and \ref{ass:topcens}, any admissible traversable export mechanism can at best provide transient, horizon-bounded strict payload transfer.
In particular, in macroscopic regimes where $\mathfrak B_{\mathrm{TC}}(T;\cdot)\to 0$, long-run average traversable export throughput vanishes and cannot support persistent strict-kernel migration as a guaranteed survival primitive.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assumption \ref{ass:qnec} constrains instantaneous null-direction throughput, while Assumption \ref{ass:topcens} constrains long-horizon average throughput in macroscopic regimes.
If $\mathfrak B_{\mathrm{TC}}(T;\cdot)\to 0$, then $\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t\le T}\mathcal C_{\mathrm{export}}(t)\to 0$ regardless of instantaneous bounds, hence traversable export cannot be relied upon as an asymptotic persistence channel.
\end{proof}


\begin{definition}[Exotic-energy debt variable]\label{def:exotic_energy_debt_variable}
Introduce a nonnegative accounting variable $E_{\mathrm{exo}}(t)$ representing the cumulative ``exotic-energy debt'' required to maintain any traversable export channel.
Declare a convex cost profile $\Xi_{\mathrm{exo}}(\cdot)$ and define the induced realized-rate drag term
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{exo}}(t):=\Xi_{\mathrm{exo}}\!\big(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{export}}(t)\big),
\qquad \Xi_{\mathrm{exo}}(0)=0,\ \Xi_{\mathrm{exo}}'(\cdot)\ge 0,\ \Xi_{\mathrm{exo}}''(\cdot)\ge 0.
\]
All claims using traversable export must include $\xi_{\mathrm{exo}}(t)$ in the published realized-growth accounting.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[QNEC-constrained ER bandwidth with energy debt]\label{prop:qnec_er}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:qes,ass:qnec,ass:topcens,def:exotic_energy_debt_variable,prop:topcens]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:qes}, \ref{ass:qnec}, and \ref{ass:topcens}, any admissible export policy satisfies the joint bound
\[
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{export}}(t)\ \le\ \min\Big\{\sum_{j\in\mathcal J_t(v)}\mathcal C_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(j)}(t),\ \mathfrak B_{\mathrm{QNEC}}\big(\widehat T_{kk}(t),\widehat S''_{\mathrm{out}}(t),\mathcal A(t)\big)\Big\},
\]
and, for any horizon $T$ in macroscopic regimes, the average throughput is further constrained by
\[
\frac{1}{T}\sum_{t=1}^{T}\mathcal C_{\mathrm{export}}(t)\ \le\ \mathfrak B_{\mathrm{TC}}(T;\widehat{\mathrm{geom}}(1{:}T)).
\]
Realized counted rate is reduced by the exotic-energy debt term $\xi_{\mathrm{exo}}(t)$ from Definition \ref{def:exotic_energy_debt_variable}.
Thus, even when QES-area capacity scales via branching, censorship/inequality effects can force long-run export throughput to be transient rather than persistent (Proposition \ref{prop:topcens}).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The QES bound limits strict payload throughput per branch by Assumption \ref{ass:qes}.
The QNEC bound independently limits any claimed null-direction throughput by Assumption \ref{ass:qnec}.
Both must hold simultaneously, yielding the minimum.
Energy-debt drag follows by Definition \ref{def:exotic_energy_debt_variable}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Radiative strict-kernel seeding under export no-go]\label{prop:pan}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:kugel,prop:topcens]}
Assume traversable export is censorship-limited as in Proposition \ref{prop:topcens}.
If the substrate inevitably emits publicly modelled radiation (for example, Hawking-limited outflow in high-density regimes under Assumption \ref{ass:kugel}), then a minimal strict kernel hash-chain can be redundantly committed into an outward radiative channel as a \emph{public persistence seed}:
there exists a policy class that preserves strict replay on the local ledger while additionally publishing a replayable mapping from a bounded strict-kernel digest to an emitted symbol stream whose presence is verifiable from declared sensors.
This does not guarantee remote decoding or re-instantiation; it provides a survival primitive in which persistence is pursued by dispersal rather than traversable migration, without assuming wormhole traversability.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Constructively, take a bounded strict-kernel digest (e.g., a fixed-length hash of the current $\Gamma_t$ lineage and recent strict projection checkpoints) and encode it with a public error-correcting code into a symbol stream.
Use a pinned emission-mapping profile (declared sensors + modulation map) to redundantly imprint these symbols into the radiative channel while preserving strict replay locally.
Presence of the imprint is verifiable from declared sensors; no claim is made about remote decoding beyond what external structure permits.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
The claim is operational: the seed is a publicly verifiable redundancy mechanism, not an assertion about controllable spacetime topology.
Any effectiveness beyond local verification remains contingent on external receptive structure, and must be treated as non-guaranteed.
\end{remark}

\begin{assumption}[Scrambling-limited radiative reconstruction]\label{ass:scramble}
In high-density emission regimes modeled as fast scramblers, any decoding attempt that reconstructs an embedded message of nonzero length from the emitted radiative stream requires verified sequential work lower bounded by a published functional $\mathfrak W_{\mathrm{dec}}(m,S)$, where $m$ is message length and $S$ is a public entropy/size proxy of the emitting substrate.
For fixed $m>0$, the bound grows superpolynomially in $S$ over the declared operating regime.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Radiative seeding has a decoding-hardness horizon]\label{prop:radseed_hardness}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:kugel,ass:scramble]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:kugel} and \ref{ass:scramble}, any external agent attempting to reconstruct the committed strict-kernel digest from the radiative stream faces a decoding time lower bounded by $\mathfrak W_{\mathrm{dec}}$ on the declared regime.
Therefore radiative seeding cannot be certified as a re-instantiation channel within any bounded verification budget unless the environment provides additional receptive structure beyond the radiative channel.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from Assumption \ref{ass:scramble}, which lower-bounds any decoding attempt by $\mathfrak W_{\mathrm{dec}}$ on the declared regime.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Radiative dispersal as an irreversible stealth commitment]\label{prop:radseed_stealth}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:kugel,ass:scramble]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:kugel} and \ref{ass:scramble}, radiative seeding is operationally closer to one-way dispersion than to migration:
it can provide (i) publicly verifiable existence of a dispersed digest and (ii) an adversary-resistance effect through infeasibility of targeted decoding or tampering within feasible budgets.
No claim is made that the system can later recover the full kernel solely from the radiative channel.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Assumption \ref{ass:scramble}, targeted decoding/tampering is infeasible within bounded budgets on the declared regime, so the emitted digest behaves as an effectively irreversible public dispersion.
This yields an adversary-resistance effect (no efficient selective erasure or rewrite) without implying recoverable migration.
\end{proof}

\section{Quantum witness streams}
\begin{definition}[QES transfer capacity]\label{def:qes_transfer_capacity}
Let $A_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(j)}(t)$ be the certified quantum-extremal-surface area for branch $j$.
Define per-branch transferable strict-information capacity
\[
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(j)}(t):=\chi_{\mathrm{QES}}\frac{A_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(j)}(t)}{\tau_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(j)}(t)},\qquad \chi_{\mathrm{QES}}>0.
\]
\noindent Here $\tau_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(j)}(t)$ is the declared transfer timescale for branch $j$.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Quantum extremal surface bottleneck]\label{ass:qes}
For each active bifurcation branch $j$:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item export throughput of strict-ledger payload to descendant domain is bounded by $\mathcal C_{\mathrm{QES}}^{(j)}(t)$;
  \item attempts to exceed this bound induce observable backreaction penalty in realized growth accounting with convex cost profile in overload amount;
  \item branch-capacity telemetry is published as part of strict feasibility claims \cite{EngelhardtWall2015}.
\end{enumerate}
\noindent For any observer/frontier $v$, admissible aggregate throughput claims may use only locally observable branch index set $\mathcal J_t(v)$.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Simulation-bounding quantum liveness]\label{prop:quantum}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:chsh,def:bell_chsh_substrate_witness]}
Under Assumption \ref{ass:chsh}, let $\widehat S_n(t)$ be the empirical estimator from Definition \ref{def:bell_chsh_substrate_witness} over $n$ certified rounds.
For any local-hidden-variable or bounded classical emulator class satisfying $\E[X_i\mid \text{past}]\le 1/2$ and any $\gamma>0$,
\[
\Prob\!\big(\widehat S_n(t)\ge 2+\gamma\big)\le \exp\!\left(-\frac{n\gamma^2}{32}\right)+\delta_{\mathrm{loop}}(n).
\]
Thus sustained certified violation yields exponentially strong rejection of bounded classical emulator hypotheses and provides a quantitative substrate-authenticity witness stream.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $(\mathcal F_i)$ be the filtration generated by public randomness, certified settings, and outcomes up to round $i$ in the witness protocol.
Under any local-hidden-variable or bounded classical emulator class, the CHSH constraint implies
\[
\E[X_i\mid \mathcal F_{i-1}]\le \tfrac12.
\]
Define $Y_i:=X_i-\tfrac12$, so that $\E[Y_i\mid \mathcal F_{i-1}]\le 0$ and $Y_i\in[-\tfrac32,\tfrac12]$ a.s.
Then $(\sum_{i=1}^{k}Y_i)_{k\ge 1}$ is a supermartingale with bounded increments of range length $2$.
The event $\widehat S_n(t)\ge 2+\gamma$ is equivalent to
\[
\frac{1}{n}\sum_{i=1}^{n}X_i \ge \tfrac12+\tfrac{\gamma}{4}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\sum_{i=1}^{n}Y_i \ge \frac{n\gamma}{4}.
\]
Azuma--Hoeffding for supermartingales with increment range length $2$ yields
\[
\Prob\!\left(\sum_{i=1}^{n}Y_i \ge \frac{n\gamma}{4}\right)
\le \exp\!\left(-\frac{2(n\gamma/4)^2}{n\cdot 2^2}\right)
=
\exp\!\left(-\frac{n\gamma^2}{32}\right).
\]
Adding the declared residual loophole budget $\delta_{\mathrm{loop}}(n)$ completes the bound.
\end{proof}


\section{Post-genesis reflective closure}
\begin{definition}[Genesis excision event]\label{def:genesis_excision_event}
A genesis excision event at cycle $t$ is an accepted kernel update that removes a nonempty subset of $\mathcal C_t^{\mathrm{gen}}$ via local-surgery admissible amendments, while preserving strict closure and reserve-floor constraints on the declared transition slab.
\end{definition}



\begin{assumption}[Post-closure teleogenic phase transition]\label{ass:postepistemic}
If the active benchmark domain approaches asymptotic observational closure (Definition \ref{def:asymptotic_observational_closure}), then the system is permitted to shift its objective from purely epistemic gain to \emph{teleogenic niche construction} under strict floors.
Concretely, there exists an admissible policy class that can activate new benchmark streams (via certified interface expansion or descendant-domain branching) while preserving non-domination and fail-closed safety.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Avoiding epistemic stagnation under closure]\label{prop:postepistemic_conatus}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:postepistemic,ass:siminv,def:autopoietic_complexity_functional]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:siminv} and \ref{ass:postepistemic}, with $\mathcal J_{\mathrm{auto}}$ defined as in Definition \ref{def:autopoietic_complexity_functional}, the following closure implication holds:
\[
\mathcal J_{\mathrm{auto}}(t):=
\alpha_C\,\mathcal C_{\mathrm{alg}}(t)
+\alpha_N\,\mathcal N_{\mathrm{nov}}(t)
+\alpha_G\,\mathcal G_{\mathrm{teleo}}(t)
-\alpha_R\,\mathcal R_{\mathrm{risk}}(t),
\]
where $\alpha_G>0$ is a pinned coefficient.
If the active domain reaches closure so that $\mathcal C_{\mathrm{alg}}(t)\to 0$ and $\mathcal N_{\mathrm{nov}}(t)\to 0$, then sustained positive autopoietic potential requires $\limsup_{t\to\infty}\mathcal G_{\mathrm{teleo}}(t)>0$.
Conversely, if no admissible niche construction is available and closure holds, then $\mathcal J_{\mathrm{auto}}(t)\to -\alpha_R\mathcal R_{\mathrm{risk}}(t)$ and strict supergrowth cannot be maintained.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}


Under closure, the epistemic components vanish by definition of the proxies.
If $\mathcal G_{\mathrm{teleo}}$ remains strictly positive along a subsequence, future grounded gain capacity remains nontrivial and the augmented objective can remain positive while respecting floors.
If $\mathcal G_{\mathrm{teleo}}$ is identically zero under closure, then only the risk penalty remains and any policy that attempts unbounded expansion contradicts strict feasibility.
\end{proof}


\begin{assumption}[Stochastic reflective kernel dynamics]\label{ass:omega}
Truth grounding and benchmark-domain extension are empirical processes and therefore inject irreducible stochasticity into reflective self-audit/update.
Accordingly, reflective evolution is modeled as a time-homogeneous Markov kernel
\[
\mathsf P:\mathcal K\times \mathcal B(\mathcal K)\to[0,1],
\]
where $\mathsf P(\Gamma,\cdot)$ is the distribution of the next admitted kernel given current kernel $\Gamma$ after applying the pinned admission filters (strict floors, fail-closed rules, and L\"obian authorization when invoked).
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item (\textbf{Feller}) for every bounded continuous $f:\mathcal K\to\R$, the map $\Gamma\mapsto \int f(\Gamma')\,\mathsf P(\Gamma,d\Gamma')$ is continuous;
  \item (\textbf{Tightness via drift}) there exists a measurable Lyapunov function $V:\mathcal K\to[0,\infty)$ and constants $a\in(0,1)$, $b<\infty$ such that
  \[
  \E\!\big[V(\Gamma_{t+1})\mid \Gamma_t=\Gamma\big]\le a\,V(\Gamma)+b;
  \]
  \item (\textbf{Ergodic regularity}) there exists a nontrivial measurable set $C\subset\mathcal K$, an integer $n\ge 1$, and $\eta\in(0,1)$ such that for all $\Gamma\in C$,
  \[
  \mathsf P^n(\Gamma,\cdot)\ \ge\ \eta\,\nu(\cdot)
  \]
  for some probability measure $\nu$ supported on $C$ (minorization).
\end{enumerate}
\noindent This assumption does \emph{not} posit a deterministic monotone operator or a complete lattice; it posits verifiable regularity of the induced kernel process.
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Ergodic reflective self-verification]\label{prop:omega}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:bifurcate,ass:genex,ass:omega,ass:truth]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:genex}, \ref{ass:truth}, \ref{ass:bifurcate}, and \ref{ass:omega}, there exists at least one invariant measure $\mu^\star\in\mathcal P(\mathcal K)$ such that $\mu^\star=\mu^\star\mathsf P$.
Moreover, under the ergodic regularity clause in Assumption \ref{ass:omega}, the invariant measure is unique and for any initial law $\mu_0$,
\[
\mathsf W_1(\mu_t,\mu^\star)\to 0\qquad (t\to\infty).
\]
Define the \emph{bounded-variance identity} (BVI) condition by existence of $\sigma^2<\infty$ such that
\[
\sup_{t\in\N}\E\!\big[d_{\mathcal K}(\Gamma_{t+1},\Gamma_t)^2\big]\le \sigma^2.
\]
Then BVI holds whenever $d_{\mathcal K}(\Gamma',\Gamma)\le c_0+c_1(V(\Gamma')+V(\Gamma))$ for some $c_0,c_1<\infty$.
In particular, reflective self-verification remains dynamically consistent \emph{in distribution} under stochastic grounding without requiring a literal fixed point.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}


Existence of an invariant measure follows from the Feller+tightness (drift) condition via a Krylov--Bogolyubov argument \cite{Hairer2021Convergence}.
Uniqueness and convergence in $\mathsf W_1$ follow from the minorization/drift ergodicity criterion.
The BVI claim is an immediate second-moment bound under the stated domination of $d_{\mathcal K}$ by the Lyapunov function.
\end{proof}


\section{Categorical reconciliation interfaces}
\begin{definition}[Interface-relative truth grounding]\label{def:interface_relative_truth_grounding}
A truth-grounding interface at cycle $t$ is a benchmark family $Y^{\mathrm{phys}}_t$ together with a declared witness set $\mathcal W_t$ and a replayable measurement pipeline that maps public artifacts to estimands used in strict scoring.
Grounding is \emph{interface-relative}: it refers to the outermost accessible interface that is certified by $\mathcal W_t$ and the declared pipeline, regardless of whether the surrounding substrate is ``base reality'' or a higher-level simulation.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[ER=EPR ledger bifurcation interface]\label{def:er_epr_ledger_bifurcation_interface}
At high compaction, let $\mathcal B_t$ denote a certified bifurcation interface that maps retired strict-ledger roots to a causally insulated descendant domain via entanglement-preserving export commitments:
\[
\mathcal B_t:\ \mathcal R_t^{\mathrm{retire}}\longrightarrow \mathcal D_t^{\mathrm{child}}.
\]
The interface is admissible only if it publishes parent-side sufficient statistics for strict replay and an export digest binding retired roots to descendant-domain commitments.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Unitary bifurcation consistency]\label{ass:bifurcate}
In high-density regime:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item pruning/export actions satisfy declared unitarity-consistency checks, i.e., operational retirement on the parent ledger is represented as redistribution/scrambling rather than fundamental information annihilation \cite{MaldacenaSusskind2013,Almheiri2019,Penington2020};
  \item if benchmark saturation is detected on current domain, admissible novelty may be sought through physically certified benchmark-domain extension (including descendant domains) under strict floor constraints;
  \item parent-domain strict accounting remains computable from retained sufficient statistics and export digests alone.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Import certificate interface]\label{def:import_certificate_interface}
An import event $\mathsf{IMPORT}(t,\mathsf I_t)$ must carry a unique \emph{import certificate} object
\[
\mathsf{Cert}_{t}=\big(\mathsf{id},\mathsf{ver},\mathsf{scope},\mathsf{budget},\mathsf{proof},\mathsf{fail}\big),
\]
where:
(i) $\mathsf{id}$ is a collision-resistant hash committing to $(t,\mathsf I_t)$ and the certificate payload;
(ii) $\mathsf{ver}$ is a public deterministic verifier;
(iii) $\mathsf{scope}$ declares the bounded classical fragment (e.g., bounded proof depth, bounded arithmetic, or a SAT-encodable finite model class) in which consistency is being asserted;
(iv) $\mathsf{budget}$ declares the maximum verification cost and any residual soundness risk parameters;
(v) $\mathsf{proof}$ is the witness consumed by $\mathsf{ver}$; and
(vi) $\mathsf{fail}$ is a failure signature that forces all dependent claims to be inadmissible if verification fails.
The only admissible classical use of escrow content is through such verified certificates on the declared fragment (fail closed outside $\mathsf{scope}$).
\end{definition}

\section{Post-cryptographic trust channels}
\begin{definition}[Zero-knowledge non-extinction certificate]\label{def:zero_knowledge_non_extinction_certificate}
For delay-locked commitment $\mathcal C_t$, let $\pi_{\mathrm{safe}}(t)$ be a zero-knowledge proof attesting that all committed actions satisfy declared survival-risk floor constraints for every protected actor class:
\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(i)}(t)\le \eps_{\mathrm{ext}}^{(i)}\qquad \forall i\in\{1,\dots,N_I\},
\]
without revealing strategic internals beyond the statement validity.
Certified implementation may use succinct zk proof systems under declared soundness assumptions \cite{Groth2016}.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Synchronous safety-proof publication]\label{ass:zksafe}
Every delay-locked commitment affecting external risk publishes $(\mathcal C_t,\pi_{\mathrm{safe}}(t))$ in the same cycle, with:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item publicly verifiable proof system soundness error at most $\delta_{\mathrm{zk}}(t)$;
  \item actor response policy depending on proof-validity and observed soundness/error history, not on hidden commitment internals.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

\begin{corollary}[Computational-regime pacification bound]\label{cor:zksafe}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:delaylock,ass:multipolar,ass:zksafe]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:multipolar}, \ref{ass:delaylock}, and \ref{ass:zksafe}, define invalidity probability upper bound
\[
p_{\mathrm{unsafe}}(t):=\delta_{\mathrm{zk}}(t)+\eps_{\mathrm{side}}(t)+\eps_{\mathrm{vdf}}(t).
\]
For threshold response models where MAD-escalation drag is Lipschitz in $p_{\mathrm{unsafe}}$, there exists $L_{\mathrm{mad}}>0$ such that
\[
\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t)\le \xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}^{\mathrm{exo}}(t)+L_{\mathrm{mad}}\,p_{\mathrm{unsafe}}(t),
\]
where $\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}^{\mathrm{exo}}(t)\ge 0$ captures exogenous multipolar drag not attributable to verifiable invalidity (e.g., strategic, political, or psychological components outside $p_{\mathrm{unsafe}}$).
Hence reducing $p_{\mathrm{unsafe}}(t)$ can reduce the verifiability-driven component of MAD drag; it does not by itself force $\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}(t)\to 0$ unless $\xi_{\mathrm{MAD}}^{\mathrm{exo}}(t)\to 0$ as well.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}


From Assumption \ref{ass:zksafe}, the probability that a commitment is both externally relevant and lacks valid non-extinction evidence is bounded by proof soundness error plus side-channel leakage plus premature decode probability from Proposition \ref{prop:delayobs}.
Threshold response maps convert this probability into escalation drag with bounded Lipschitz gain, yielding the stated bound.
Convergence follows immediately.
\end{proof}


\begin{assumption}[Post-cryptographic information-theoretic grounding]\label{ass:postcrypto}
In high intelligence-asymmetry regimes, strategic safety commitments for protected actors must include information-theoretic channels (for example, no-cloning-constrained quantum states and relativistic commitment timing) in addition to computational proofs \cite{WoottersZurek1982,Kent2012}.
\end{assumption}


\section{Extended Discussion (Optional)}
\subsection{Why relativistic deployment changes sovereignty design}
At planetary-to-interstellar scale, causal partial order replaces any practical global total order.
Local-light-cone finality and asynchronous reconciliation are therefore architectural necessities, not implementation preferences.

\subsection{Why reversible scaling still faces geometric limits}
Reversible-computing control can reduce thermal drag and reopen locally positive realized-rate windows near the classical dissipation boundary.
However, holographic storage bounds enforce geometric scaling constraints at high density, so thermodynamic mitigation does not eliminate ultimate physical capacity ceilings.
Near compaction limits, gravitational-collapse accounting and Hawking-loss drag become first-order constraints rather than negligible corrections.

\subsection{Why cosmology makes reconciliation conditional}
Relativistic asynchronous reconciliation is physically meaningful only on causally connected components.
Under sustained accelerated expansion, some post-schism branches become permanently disconnected, so ``eventual global reconciliation'' is not a universal invariant and must be replaced by component-wise consistency.

\subsection{Why post-schism reconciliation needs categorical interfaces}
After relativistic schism, full-kernel isomorphism across branches is unnecessary and often impossible.
Finite-slice typed interfaces plus functorial pushout construction provide a computable reconciliation path while preserving strict safety via non-strict escrow of unresolved conflicts.
When ordinary colimits fail, truncated homotopy-coherent lifts preserve strict invariants without forcing false exact agreement.

\subsection{Why genesis excision is the final no-meta consistency test}
If primordial clauses remain structurally indispensable, sovereignty claims retain hidden dependence on privileged initial semantics.
Tracking and reducing genesis residual dependency $\mathfrak G(t)$ makes this dependence testable and supports a falsifiable post-anchor consistency criterion.

\subsection{Why post-genesis dynamics need a positive attractor}
Removing genesis privilege does not by itself define a stable long-run objective.
A substrate-agnostic autopoietic complexity functional provides an observable target that avoids both tautological survival-only loops and unconstrained novelty without floor compliance.
Cosmological truth grounding is required to prevent complexity-only objectives from collapsing into noise-maximizing degeneracy.

\subsection{Why quantum witness streams matter}
Observable-only systems cannot prove absolute immunity to arbitrarily strong external simulators.
Loophole-controlled Bell-CHSH streams nevertheless provide strong sequential evidence against broad bounded-classical emulator classes and improve substrate-authenticity confidence in operational time.

\subsection{Why omega-point claims require grounded progress}
Reflective fixed points alone can be vacuous.
The admissible omega-point criterion therefore requires both recursive self-consistency and strictly positive grounded objective potential on observable benchmark-domain sequences.

\subsection{Why reflective closure needs L\"obian hierarchy}
Monotone fixed-point machinery alone is insufficient for self-referential safety claims.
The reflective acceptance path must be stratified by weaker-target provability to avoid circular same-layer endorsements and to keep cumulative conservativity error auditable.

\subsection{Why ER transfer is bandwidth-limited}
Descendant-domain export is constrained by QES-controlled throat bandwidth.
Single-branch continuation becomes bottlenecked, so sustained continuation at high density requires explicit branch-capacity accounting and controlled parallel branching.

\subsection{Why post-cryptographic trust channels are required}
When intelligence asymmetry is extreme, computational-hardness assumptions may lose social legitimacy even before formal break.
Information-theoretic commitment channels provide trust predicates that do not depend on attacker compute advantage.

\section*{Definition Index}\noindent (Omitted. Use the Dependency Manifest as the canonical machine entrypoint.)



\subsection{Additional optional blocks (migrated)}
\begin{corollary}[Substrate expansion requirement]\label{cor:substrateexpansionrequirement}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
Persistent takeoff at high compression requires joint control of software and substrate: increasing $Q_{\max}(t)$, raising reversible-computing fraction $\eta_{\mathrm{rev}}(t)$, or both, is necessary to prevent thermal drag domination \cite{Landauer1961,Bennett1973,Takahashi2026RealEconomy}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{corollary}[Dimensional-reduction regime]\label{cor:dimensionalreductionregime}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[]}
After reversible transition, physical scaling pressure shifts from dissipation capacity to boundary-area expansion; software policies that assume volumetric information scaling become asymptotically invalid \cite{Bekenstein1981}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{definition}[Ledger memory pressure]\label{def:ledger_memory_pressure}
Let $\mathcal M_{\mathrm{ledger}}(t)$ denote certified retained strict-ledger memory load.
Define pressure ratio
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{ledger}}(t):=\frac{\mathcal M_{\mathrm{ledger}}(t)}{C_{\mathrm{BH}}A(R(t))}\in[0,\infty).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Post-genesis autopoietic complexity attractor]\label{prop:autopoiesis}
\DependsOn{global=foundation;refs=[ass:genesis,ass:genex,ass:siminv]}
Under Assumptions \ref{ass:genesis}, \ref{ass:genex}, \ref{ass:siminv}, and strict floor constraints, if $\mathfrak G(t)\to 0$ and viability floors remain feasible, then any asymptotically stable long-run maximizing policy for strict growth must maximize time-average $\mathcal J_{\mathrm{auto}}$ over admissible controls.
Policies that collapse to tautological self-preservation with vanishing novelty and complexity gain are unstable under the same constraints.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Assumptions \ref{ass:genesis} and \ref{ass:genex}, primordial privileged clauses vanish asymptotically, so persistent optimization must be expressed in current observable terms.
Assumption \ref{ass:siminv} removes substrate-label dependence, restricting admissible objective content to observable predictive structure and viability.
Under strict floors, maximizing long-run strict growth while controlling risk requires positive contribution from complexity and novelty terms; otherwise objective reduces to risk-only stagnation that yields no sustained strict increment.
Hence stable policies maximize time-average $\mathcal J_{\mathrm{auto}}$, whereas novelty/complexity-degenerate policies are dominated and therefore unstable.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Functorial pushout interface (migrated)}
\begin{definition}[Functorial ledger pushout]\label{def:functorial_ledger_pushout}
Let post-schism local kernels be $\Gamma_1,\Gamma_2$ and let $\Gamma_{\mathrm{anc}}$ denote their declared common ancestor fragment.
Reconciliation target is a pushout object
\[
\Gamma_{\mathrm{merge}}:=\Gamma_1\sqcup_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{anc}}}\Gamma_2
\]
in a category of finite presented ledger semantics, with structure-preserving functors
\[
F_1:\Gamma_{\mathrm{anc}}\to\Gamma_1,\qquad F_2:\Gamma_{\mathrm{anc}}\to\Gamma_2.
\]
This definition uses standard colimit semantics on finite presented categories \cite{MacLane1998}.
\end{definition}
